Yet the hardships of purification and taboos were no different. He also said that refining the Yellow and White arts was like compounding divine elixirs—one must purify for over a hundred days, and the oral instructions must come from a master. One should enter deep mountains, a place of purity, and not let vulgar fools know of it.

I asked again, ‘Is there no deception in this?’ Master Zheng replied, ‘The gold produced through transmutation is the essence of all medicines, surpassing even the natural. The *Immortals’ Scripture* says, *The essence of the elixir generates gold.* It also says, *Gold can be made, and the world can be delivered.* When the gold is complete, it is a true substance, uniform inside and out, unchanging even after a hundred refinements. How can this be called deceit?’”

Lu Qianxu said, “The elixir has three origins, each capable of perfecting life. These three origins are called the Celestial Origin, the Terrestrial Origin, and the Human Origin.

“The Celestial Origin is called the Divine Elixir. The Divine Elixir is refined with water above and fire below within the sacred chamber. From formlessness it generates form, and after nine cycles of transmutation, it becomes white as snow. Further refinement of the three origins transforms it into divine talismans. When ingested, one becomes weightless and ascends. This is the wondrous work of medicinal transformation and the marvel of sages and spirits. The Way of this is fully expounded in the *Dragon and Tiger* of the Yellow Emperor and the *Stone Casket* of Master Jingyang.

“The Terrestrial Origin is called the Numinous Elixir. The Numinous Elixir transmutes metals and minerals into supreme treasures. Its ingredients—silver, lead, cinnabar, and mercury—are tangible substances, capable only of prolonging life in the world but not of lightening the body. After nine cycles of transmutation, the most potent and wondrous of its medicines are cast into the sacred chamber to connect with the Celestial Origin, serving as the vessel and cauldron for cultivating the Dao. From ancient times to the present, the highest sages and perfected beings have called this a sacred endeavor. Its method is most simple and easy: one need only gather primordial lead, subdue postnatal mercury, discern ascent and descent, and recognize maturity and tenderness. Yet today’s blind masters, in their haste, often obscure this, leading to countless failures. They do not realize that the Way of the Terrestrial Origin is no different from that of the Human Origin—only those who thoroughly comprehend yin and yang and deeply penetrate the workings of creation may speak of it.

“The Human Origin is called the Great Elixir. The Great Elixir forges the crucible externally and refines the medicine internally, taking from Kan to fill Li, and reversing the mechanism of theft. The highest immortals and sages of antiquity all followed this path. Among the studies for perfecting life, none is more immediate and profound than the Human Origin.

“Thus, of the three origins of the elixir, the Celestial Origin depends on heaven and earth and the spirits and cannot be assured. The Terrestrial Origin, when cultivated with proper method, blessed with both fortune and wisdom, may be attained as easily as reaching for something at hand. The Human Origin, however, holds the cosmos in one’s grasp, generates the myriad transformations within the body, eludes the calculations of ghosts and spirits, and escapes the reckoning of yin and yang. Such are the distinctions among the three origins.”

Jiyi Zi said: “Lead, silver, cinnabar, and mercury are originally names of furnace and fire. Since yin and yang do not have separate designations, they are named after the terms of furnace and fire. Furnace and fire, yin and yang, are originally of one thread—their practices differ, but their principles are the same. Thus, those who understand internal workings have never failed to understand external workings. Yin and yang, as well as furnace and fire, each possess three origins.

“The three origins of yin and yang:
The initial barrier refines essence into qi, the work of laying the foundation—this is the Terrestrial Origin.
The middle barrier refines qi into spirit, the work of shedding the embryo and changing the crucible—this is the Human Origin.
The upper barrier refines spirit to return to emptiness, the work of facing the wall to return to the origin—this is the Celestial Origin.
The initial barrier pertains to the affairs of the Desire Realm heavens; the middle barrier, to the affairs of the Form Realm heavens; the upper barrier, to the affairs of the Formless Realm heavens.
The initial barrier yields the fruit of human immortals; the middle barrier, the fruit of divine immortals; the upper barrier, the fruit of celestial immortals.

“The three origins of furnace and fire:
The first is the Terrestrial Origin, the work of transmutation.
The middle is the Human Origin, the work of ingestion.
The last is the Celestial Origin, the work of projection into the dwelling.
As the *Cantong Qi* states: ‘The work of furnace and fire is truly well-founded.’
This is expounded in texts such as the *Bronze Talisman and Iron Contract*, the *Stone Casket Record*, the *Dragon and Tiger Classic*, the *Golden Valley Song*, the *Secret Fire Instructions of the Floating Black Ancestor*, the *Secret Writings on the Great Treasure of the Prince of Huainan*, the *Fire Lotus Sutra*, the *Three Origins Secret Methods of Master Xu*, the *True Terrestrial Origin Instructions of Bai Ziqing*, the *Divine Elixir Discourse of Zhuo Hu*, the *Guanyin Sutra of Master Peng*, and the *Fire Dragon Instructions of Shangyang Zi*. Other works, including the *Fish Manor Record*, the *Record of Inherited Aspiration*, *Mid-Autumn at Noon*, the *Grotto-Heaven Secret Canon*, the *Direct Pointer to the Yellow and White*, the *Breaking Ignorance of the Yellow and White*, the *Mirror of the Yellow and White*, the *Direct Pointer to Gold and Fire*, the *True Treasury of Hidden Books*, the *Thunder-Shocked Elixir Classic*, *Heavenly Terrace at Hand*, the *Mirror of the Yellow and White*, and the *Bamboo Spring Collection*, all provide clear evidence for study.

The Terrestrial Origin of furnace and fire focuses on creating earth and nurturing cinnabar. Once accomplished, it may assist the yin-yang work of the Human Origin. Using the yellow and white of the Terrestrial Origin to cast the divine chamber, one summons and gathers the celestial hun and terrestrial po, drawing the true water of the sun and moon. These coalesce in emptiness to form the Celestial Origin divine elixir. Thus did the Yellow Emperor ascend by the dragon’s whiskers at Lake Ding, the Prince of Huainan cause his chickens and dogs to rise together, and Master Jingyang lift his entire household into the heavens.”

The Perfected One Yin Changsheng, having attained the Dao, composed three poems to instruct future generations.

The first:
My forebears in nature and destiny lived in the age of Tang and Yu.
By the Han dynasty, the purple texts were again revered.
I alone loved the Dao and remained a common man,
Exalting plain filial piety above kings and lords.
Clinging to life, I gained life—what more could I seek?
My traces transcend the azure skies,
Riding the dragon, soaring on the floating clouds,
With pure winds bearing my wings, my foes become allies.
I enter fire unscorched, tread waves undrenched.
Carefree in the Great Ultimate, what worry or sorrow remains?
Roaming the immortal capital, I pity the multitude’s plight:
The passing of years and life flows like a river’s course.
In an instant, unseen, they become earth’s companions,
Rushing headlong toward death, never pausing to rest.

The second:
My sagely teacher embodied the true Dao,
Ascending and descending in transformation, neighbor to towering pines.
Among my fellow students, twelve in number,
We sought the Dao through cold and heat for twenty years.
Many grew indolent, their resolve and conduct unsteady.
Alas, my companions—fate comes from Heaven.
Heaven does not bestow lightly; the Dao must return to the worthy.
Their bodies perish in the dark earth—when may they return?
O you who come after, devote yourselves to diligent study,
Lest you be swayed by worldly customs or the lure of wealth and rank.
Once the divine Dao is achieved, you shall ascend to the Nine Heavens,
Your lifespan extending with the Three Luminaries—how could it be mere billions?

The third:
From the time I bound my hair, I cherished virtue and the Dao in youth,
Leaving home to follow my teacher, wandering east, west, south, and north,
Abandoning the Five Turbidities, secluding myself to evade the world.
For over thirty years beside nameless mountains,
Cold left me without time for clothing, hunger without time for food,
Longing dared not turn me homeward, toil dared not grant me rest.
I served my sagely teacher, offering joy and gladness in his presence,
My face begrimed, my feet calloused—only then was my sincerity seen.
Thus I received the essential instructions, a boundless depth of grace.
My wife and children gained extended years, all enjoying limitless blessings.
The yellow and white were perfected, yielding wealth of a thousand millions.
I command ghosts and spirits; jade maidens attend my circle.
Now I attain deliverance from the world—through the power of the divine elixir.

At Redcliff Mountain, Xie Ziran studied under Master Sima Ziwei, cultivating in accordance with the Dao. On the twelfth day of the first month in the eleventh year of the Zhenyuan reign of the Tang, she ascended to heaven in broad daylight. Li Jian, the prefect of Guozhou, reported the event and composed a record of her life. Han Changli’s poem reads:

In Nanchong County of Guozhou,
A humble scholar, Xie Ziran.
A child who knew nothing,
Yet heard of immortals.
She cast aside her life to learn their arts,
Dwelling on Golden Spring Mountain.
One morning, seated in emptiness,
Clouds and mist arose around her.
As if hearing the melody of pipes and flutes,
Descending from the unseen heavens.
In an instant, she lightly ascended,
Drifting like smoke in the clouds.
The village head reported the matter,
The prefect marveled and sighed.
He summoned neighboring officials,
The common folk vied to lead the way.
Entering her dwelling, they saw nothing—
Only her shoes and cap, shed like a cicada’s shell.
Once deemed the stuff of immortals,
Now clearly true and fit to be passed down.

*(Guozhou is present-day Shunqing Prefecture in Sichuan; its chief county is Nanchong, and Golden Spring Mountain lies outside the prefecture’s western gate.)*

Li Daochun of the Radiant Toad, styled Yuansu, wrote:
The three supreme medicines are essence, qi, and spirit.
In substance, they are one; in function, they are two.
What is meant by "substance"?

The matter of the Three Origins is fundamentally great. What is meant by "function"? It refers to the twofold operation of internal and external. The internal medicine: the primordial supreme essence, the empty and void qi, the indestructible original spirit. The external medicine: the essence of intercourse, the qi of breath, the spirit of thought. The celestial number is twenty-five, thus one, three, five, seven, nine are the odd yang numbers. The terrestrial number is thirty, thus two, four, six, eight, ten are the even yin numbers. All told, the numbers of heaven and earth sum to fifty-five. The *Great Expansion* text speaks of fifty, subtracting five as the root of the Five Phases, leaving forty-nine in use. Another is subtracted to symbolize the unmoving Great Ultimate—from this, one may know that it has both substance and function.

**Book Two: Method, Resources, Companions, and Place**

**Method**
Master Shangyang said: "The Great Dao of the Golden Elixir was transmitted by the ancients once in ten thousand kalpas—it is no trivial matter. The celestial mechanism is secret; the ancient sages and perfected immortals, though they wrote books and established teachings, never revealed it in complete, explicit terms. Its apertures are many, its names varied—truly, it cannot be fathomed by conjecture. If one guesses within the body, one falls into dull emptiness and dry sitting, harboring the folly of grinding a brick to make a mirror. If one guesses outside the body, one shuts off the breath in seclusion, only to violate the warning against carrying firewood to extinguish a fire. If one employs soldiers and generals, one risks suspicion of bedroom arts, and those who speak of the Three Peaks technique are already condemned. If one ingests through the mouth or belly, one risks suspicion of consuming elixirs, and those who use mineral and stone preparations have already courted disaster. As for employing chamber elixirs, their impurity is suspect. Pointing to furnace and fire, their waste of resources is pitiable. Truly, even one as wise as Yan or Min never attained enlightenment without a true teacher. Thus it is said: ‘Innate nature is realized through self-awakening; life is transmitted through a teacher.’ Yet true teachers are rare—one must possess the eye of great wisdom to discern them. Of old, Patriarch Lü recognized his teacher in Chang’an, and Apricot Grove bowed to his master in bonds—these were men of great wisdom. Otherwise, like Han Tuizhi meeting Han Xiang at Blue Pass or Zhu Yuanhui meeting Zi Qing at Mount Wuyi, though those two worthies were not lacking in wisdom, their self-reliance and self-opinion prevented humility, so they met their teachers yet did not truly meet them."

The Master of Following the Middle Path said: "The ancients who pursued learning invariably had a teacher. A teacher is one who transmits the Dao, imparts knowledge, and resolves doubts. Even farmers, artisans, merchants, and those of minor skills or arts rely on teachers—how much more so for transcending the mundane and entering sagehood, for the great matter of life and death? Thus the former sages exerted every effort and devoted their hearts, diligently serving their teachers to seek this Dao, faithfully receiving and practicing their teachings. Once they had attained the Dao, those who became immortals before them were as their ancestors and fathers; those who became immortals after them were as their children and grandchildren. In transmitting this lineage of the Dao, one’s original teacher becomes one’s compassionate father—how could one fail to fulfill one’s filial duty?

Consider, for instance, how the Perfected Lord Wu served Patriarch Xu as his disciple, or how Ancient Spirit praised his own disciple as his teacher—this is to judge by the Dao rather than by outward appearances. Nothing surpasses such humility in seeking instruction below oneself. This is especially extraordinary, for what they valued was the Dao alone."

The Master of Following the Middle Path said: "People today blindly cultivate and recklessly refine, failing to grasp the true essence and unable to comprehend the supreme principle. Though there are ten thousand volumes of alchemical classics, it is like counting grains of sand in the sea—perpetual realization remains elusive. If, by virtue of past good affinities, one encounters a true teacher who reveals the celestial mechanisms and wondrous workings one by one, breaking through each secret, then the eye of wisdom opens. It is like a pauper obtaining treasure, like the sick receiving medicine, like a prisoner granted amnesty, like the dead restored to life—far more precious than ten thousand taels of gold. Gold is easily exhausted, but the wondrous Dharma is inexhaustible.

Long ago, the Tathāgata said: ‘If this matter were expounded, gods and men alike would be astonished and doubtful.’ Master Shangyang remarked: ‘That people are astonished and doubtful stems from their shallow capacities and vulgar understanding—let us set that aside for now. But why would the gods also be astonished and doubtful? There must be something in this matter that is truly astonishing and worthy of doubt.’"

“In his youth, Ge Hong of the *Baopuzi* yearned for the Dao, perused ten thousand books, and equaled the wisdom of the Ten Sages while surpassing that of Yan [Hui] and Min [Sun]—yet still could not awaken to the truth. Later, he met the Perfected One Zheng Siyuan, who secretly transmitted the oral instructions. Even the ancient sages and immortals could not fathom this; how much more deluded are people today!”

Master Shangyang said: “Without seeking a teacher in distant lands or comprehending the profound mysteries of the Golden Elixir, one may instead depict the true forms of the ancestral masters—Chunyang, Chongyang, and Danyang—and offer incense and flowers morning and night, wholeheartedly facing their images. Recite this *Great Essentials of the Golden Elixir* once, ten times, a hundred times, or a thousand times; as days and months deepen, let the initial resolve never waver, and redouble one’s devotion. Naturally, the immortals will be moved to descend and personally transmit the teachings. Once the principles become thoroughly clear and the mind-ground empty and numinous, one’s feet will at once tread upon reality.

Why is this so? By decree of the Upper Realm, the Perfected Lord Danyang has been entrusted with overseeing the registers of immortals, patrolling the world to inspect the diligence of practitioners and inscribe their names upon the Elixir Terrace. He dispatches Perfected Ones and immortal maidens to descend as teachers for humanity. The Bureau of Recorded Decrees is charged with providing elixir wealth to fulfill the supreme Dao of those who study immortality—surely they will become true Perfected Ones.”

Master Shangyang further said: “My teacher, Yuanduzi, several times pointed to the primordial qi that arises from the Void. *Pursuing the Void* states: ‘Since it comes from the Void, it is neither bestowed by Heaven nor produced by Earth, nor is it inherent in the body. It is not essence, not blood, not herb, not wood, not metal, not stone—none of these.’ Without a teacher’s guidance, who could ever know this?”

Lüzu said: “To distinguish whether the water’s source is clear or turbid, to discern the separation between metal and wood—without a teacher’s guidance, these matters are difficult to know.”

Shangyangzi said: “Even with a sagely teacher’s earnest admonitions, one may still err; how then could an ordinary person attain realization on their own?”

Zhang Ziyang said: “Though your wisdom surpasses Yan and Min, without meeting a true teacher, do not force guesswork.”

Xu Zu said: “The elixir scriptures must be transmitted orally.”

Xiao Zixu said: “The primordial Heaven and primordial Earth hold the most profound mystery—how could one of shallow fortune encounter them?”

Shangyangzi said: “The patriarchs Lü Chunyang, Liu Haichan, and Wang Chongyang took pity on those drowning in the world. In their compassion to rescue the kalpa, they appeared and transformed, coming and going in the mortal realm, delivering only those who could be delivered. Thus, while the Way of the Golden Elixir may be taught to others by immortals and transcendents, they cannot ensure its completion—yet they know those who will surely complete it, and so deliver only those destined to succeed.”

Shangyangzi further said: “In the past, before I had heard of this, I thought that if I attained it, I would make the Way known to all people without concealment. But after I had heard it, I observed and reflected in secret, and truly found no one worthy of transmitting this Way. As Lüzu said: ‘In the boundless universe, among countless people, how many men are true *nan’er*?’ In the eyes of the vulgar, are *nan’er* not men?”

Shangyangzi said: “Since I encountered the perfected one and received the great Dao through sacred covenant, I have desired to accomplish this endeavor. Yet as my karmic conditions were not yet established, I sought the immortal classics, gathering rare and essential teachings to compose the *Great Essentials of the Golden Elixir*. Once the book was completed, I spared no effort in its dissemination. Whenever I passed through famous mountains or cities, I adapted to local circumstances to cultivate affinity. Lowering my head and humbling my heart, I guided the people of the world, enticing them toward this Way. For forty years, seekers came in droves, yet I never saw one of great capacity who advanced with diligence.”

Shangyangzi said: “I composed the ten-scroll *Great Essentials of the Golden Elixir*. After its completion, I feared that without oral transmission, how could the world awaken on its own? Thus, I carried the book and exhausted my efforts, humbling myself to seek others. Whenever I found even a slight potential for guidance, I lowered my head and bent my body, offering encouraging words and exhortations to spur them forward. If this Way met with scorn, I endured it in silence. Should I gain the understanding of one or two, a thousand or ten thousand would come to slander. Yet I desired only to practice the Dao, heedless of right or wrong. When met with ridicule, I received it with joy; when encountering a vessel for the Dharma, I urged them forward with encouragement. Those who could enter the gate, I led up the steps; those who could ascend the steps, I guided into the inner chamber. All my efforts to this end were but to sustain the great Dao by a single thread, to lift the common folk from the pit of fire, and to let the world know that the Way of the Golden Elixir is no deception.”

Shangyangzi said: “The Dao cannot be transmitted through words—yet without words, how could one hear of the Dao? To say it cannot be transmitted through words is only because the people of this age are mired in base habits and shallow understanding, unworthy of being spoken to. Even if one were to speak to them insistently, would they believe, accept, and practice it? Thus it is said the Dao cannot be transmitted through words. Yet if words were truly unnecessary, why would there be oral transmission? To claim that the Dao lies in wordlessness—do they not know that within it, profound words abound? But these are not for the ears of the many. Otherwise, why would the sages of old have concealed their direct pointers, leaving them unsaid even now? Later learners, whose wisdom-eyes have not yet opened, must first examine whether one is loyal, filial, upright, and honest—whether they are good or evil, wise or foolish. The great Dao is not for those who are not true gentlemen or those not already of good character. It must never be transmitted recklessly for profit or in vain. If given to the unworthy, both teacher and disciple will suffer retribution—how then could they respect their master and accomplish the Dao?

The *Yellow Court Classic* says:
‘The giver is called master, the receiver takes a covenant,
Wrapped in cloud-brocade and phoenix-silk, bound with golden cords.
In place of cutting hair or flesh, the bond is whole,
Hand in hand they ascend the mountain, sharing the cinnabar elixir’s oath.
Golden script on jade tablets is fitting,
Transmit it with care, report to the Three Officials.
Let not the seven ancestors suffer in darkness,
The Supreme’s subtle words lead to immortality.
This is the true text of the deathless Way.’

Between heaven and earth, nothing is greater than this matter. When Master Ziyang transmitted it to the unworthy, he suffered three calamities—all recorded in the immortal classics. Can one not take warning?”

Shangyangzi said: “The transmission of the Dao has three levels. The highest are cultured gentlemen of few words who delight in goodness, able to renounce wealth and honor, urgently seeking only their own salvation—these are the superior scholars, worthy of receiving the Dao. The middle are those plain in manner yet unwavering in faith upon hearing the Dao, able to sever ties of affection, practice with diligence, and disregard praise or blame—these are the middling scholars, possessing the aspirations of the superior, and thus worthy of receiving the Dao. The lowest are those simple yet sincere, who delight in goodness and reject evil, willing to set aside their own views to follow others, bold and decisive in action—these are the lesser scholars, whose resolve is still admirable, and thus worthy of receiving the Dao. Those who attain this Way are all courageous and diligent, steadfast in wisdom, restraining evil and promoting goodness.

For the word *goodness* is the ladder and ferry of the human Dao. Thus, if one’s ears constantly hear goodness, the kidneys do not leak essence. If one’s mouth constantly speaks goodness, the heart does not lose spirit. If one’s nose constantly smells goodness, the lungs can stabilize the po. If one’s eyes constantly see goodness, the liver can nurture the hun. If one’s mind constantly contemplates goodness, the spleen can generate qi. One who is centered and attuned to principle—how can a great cultivator not embody goodness?

‘Even at one hundred and twenty years, one may still return to the elixir.’ This is the Way—how could the mediocre and common be told of it? How could false teachers and deluded men comprehend it? Without a true immortal sage as master, swearing an oath to heaven and receiving oral transmission, who could know it?”

Master Stone Apricot said: “Ever since receiving my teacher’s instructions, I have known this body need not die, and this elixir can surely be accomplished. Now that the great work is underway, I proclaim this to all future seekers of immortality.”

The *Baopuzi* states: “To seek immortality as a divine transcendent, the essential method lies in treasuring essence, circulating qi, and ingesting a single great elixir—this alone suffices, and no more is needed. Yet this matter has its depths and shallows; without encountering an enlightened master, enduring hardship, and diligent practice, it cannot be fully known.”

The *Baopuzi* states: “The crux lies solely in the practice of returning essence to replenish the brain. This method was transmitted by the Perfected One Lü Dongbin, and was never committed to writing. The likes of Master Xuansu, Du Kangcheng, Peng Zu, and others recorded only its rudimentary aspects, never setting its most essential teachings upon paper. Only after ascending the altar and swearing a blood oath is the oral transmission revealed. If one is not the right person, even were the land split and cities joined, halls filled with gold and jade, it would not be rashly imparted.”

The *Baopuzi* states: “Human life receives spirit from Heaven and Earth, qi and blood from father and mother. Yet without a wise master to reveal the secrets of transcending the world, there is no way to escape death. The flame may linger in the chiseled stone, but one’s allotted years have already withered. From this we may conclude: the grace of an enlightened master truly surpasses that of Heaven and Earth, and far exceeds that of one’s parents. How can one not revere such a master? How can one not seek them out?”

The *Baopuzi* states: “Alas! Future scholars must make seeking a master their foremost duty and careful selection their most urgent task.”

The *Baopuzi* states: “Without obtaining the Great Method of the Golden Elixir, one cannot attain longevity. Though one may command ghosts and spirits, gaze a thousand *li* afar, or foresee misfortune before it arises, none of this will benefit one’s allotted years. If one feels shame in entreating or deems it beneath oneself to serve those who have gone before, this is to begrudge a moment’s humility while willingly embracing endless mediocrity.”

The *Baopuzi* states: “The oral transmission of the True Unity is always recorded in clear script. One swears an oath by drinking the blood of a white sacrificial beast on an auspicious day. A covenant is made with silver and white silk, then split like a golden contract—if lightly spoken or rashly transmitted, the spirits will not respond.”

The *Baopuzi* states: “Though the texts exist, their essentials are always concealed. The oral instructions must be given, with explanations provided while reading the text, before one can truly practice.”

The *Baopuzi* states: “All transmissions rely on a master’s instruction in the ingestion of elixirs; none are innate knowledge.”

The *Baopuzi* states: “My great-uncle, the Immortal Lord, received these teachings from Zuo Yuanfang. My master, Master Zheng, was a disciple of my great-uncle the Immortal Lord and also received them from him. Yet my family was too poor to afford the medicines. I personally served him, sweeping and cleaning for many years, until at last, in the Maiji Mountains, we erected an altar, swore an oath, and he imparted all the unrecorded oral instructions.”

The *Baopuzi* states: “Without witnessing the method or encountering an enlightened master, one would never know that such wondrous matters exist in the world.”

The *Baopuzi* states: “This Way is of utmost importance and must be transmitted only to the worthy. If one is not the right person, even if their jade and gold were piled mountain-high, this Way would not be revealed to them. The recipient casts a golden figurine and golden fish into the east-flowing waters as a covenant and swears an oath by drinking blood. Without the bone of an immortal, one cannot behold this Way.”

The *Baopuzi* states: “Eight ounces of gold are cast into the east-flowing waters, and an oath is sworn by drinking blood before the oral instructions are given. If one deviates from the original method and steals the formula to practice, it will never succeed.”

The *Baopuzi* states: “Those who indulge their desires to the full and perish in an instant—take care never to reveal the divine elixir to them, lest they mock the Way and slander the truth. To transmit it to the unworthy brings misfortune upon oneself.”

The *Baopuzi* states: “Those of shallow vision know only to cherish life but not the Way of nurturing it; they fear death but do not believe in the method of transcending it.”

The *Baopuzi* states: “Without accumulating hidden virtue and good deeds, one cannot move the spirits; without sincerity and wholehearted devotion, one cannot bind oneself to a master or friends. Without meritorious deeds, one cannot be tested in great trials. Moreover, without encountering an enlightened master, one cannot obtain the essential Way.”

The *Baopuzi* states: “The world says that a single word of goodness is worth more than a thousand pieces of gold. How much more so, then, are the instructions for longevity worth beyond mere gold?”

The *Baopuzi* states: “Golden tablets and jade slips, the scriptures of immortals, and the most essential teachings are often not written down. Only after ascending the altar and swearing a blood oath are the oral instructions transmitted.”

The *Baopuzi* states: “Longevity is not difficult; hearing the Way is difficult. Hearing the Way is not difficult; practicing it is difficult. Practicing it is not difficult; persevering to the end is difficult. A skilled craftsman can give others the compass and square but cannot ensure they will be skillful. An enlightened master can transmit the methods and texts but cannot ensure they will succeed.”

The preface to Zhang Ziyang’s *Wuzhen Pian* states: “I, having not yet met a perfected one and finding oral instructions rare, became so restless that I could neither eat nor sleep, my spirit worn and weary. I inquired far and wide across mountains and seas, seeking counsel from both the wise and the foolish, yet none could penetrate the true essence or illuminate the depths of my heart. Later, in the Xining reign’s *jiyou* year, I followed Minister Lu of the Dragon Diagram into Chengdu. Unwavering in my long-held resolve and ever more earnest in my devotion, I at last moved a true immortal to impart the oral instructions of the Golden Elixir, its ingredients, and the firing times. His words were utterly simple, his essentials unburdensome, and when compared to the immortal scriptures, they matched as if by tally.”

The *Three Commentaries* records Dao-Guang Zu as saying: “Alas! People of the world, failing to meet a true master who might awaken them, resort to guesswork, doubt, and slander. The method is utterly simple, utterly easy—even ordinary men and women, if they believe and practice it, may surely attain immortality. This Dao is verifiably capable of transcending birth and death, yet the trouble lies in people’s inability to believe; instead, they turn to slander. I have devoted myself to this Dao for years, and the Dao does not betray one. Heaven took pity on me, allowing me to meet a sagely master whose single utterance revealed that the Dao lies right before one’s eyes. Comparing it with the alchemical scriptures, all became perfectly clear: what is produced within this body is nothing other than mercury. Alas! People of the world prefer the false to the true, erring even when the truth stands before them—who among them would admit their mistake? How lamentable!”

The *Three Commentaries* records Shang-Yang Zi as saying: “Those of superior faculties and keen insight, if they do not meet their master, will inevitably fall into emptiness, recklessness, and dissipation. Those of middling capacity, foolishly obstinate and lacking a teacher, will indulge in wild conjecture. The ignorant and foolish, drifting with the currents, do not believe the Dao exists. As the ancients said: ‘Form is preserved by the Dao; life is prolonged by technique.’ When I first heard Master Zhao’s words, I was firmly convinced. Later, upon meeting the old immortal of Qingcheng, I finally understood the principles of yin-yang transformation—following the natural course gives rise to humanity, reversing it gives rise to immortality. Having received my master’s transmission, I was so vigilant in sleep and waking that I first taught Tian Hou and Zhi-Yang Zi. I traveled extensively through Yelang, Qiongshui, Yuan, Zhi, Chen, and Yang; through Jingnan’s two E prefectures; to Changsha, Mount Lu; and across the regions east and west of the Jiang, teaching over a hundred people—yet all were instructed only in the essentials of preserving form through the Dao. As for the secrets of prolonging life through technique, barely one or two in a hundred were worthy of being told.”

Zhang Zi-Yang says: “Without meeting a perfected one to transmit the oral instructions, even if one were to ponder a hundred variations, one could never successfully apply the method or accomplish the work. If, after this, there are those of keen and resolute nature who encounter this text, they will recognize that Bo-Duan grasped the supreme subtleties of the Sixth Patriarch’s Mahayana teachings, such that a single word may awaken them to the myriad dharmas.”

(Now I also say: “Those who see my book will understand the Golden Balance, grasp the true transmission, penetrate the marvels of yin-yang apertures, and master the pivot of creation. May those destined for this path ascend together to the celestial realms.”)

The *Three Commentaries* records Dao-Guang Zu as saying: “The most foolish among men divide the kidneys and heart to represent Kan and Li, take the liver and lungs as dragon and tiger, use spirit and qi as mother and child, and cling to essence and fluids as lead and mercury. How pitiful!”

Dao-Guang Zu said: “From whence does the body arise? From whence does life emerge?”

In the *Three Commentaries*, Shang-Yang Zi said: “Without a true master to reveal the one true lead, though one may traverse all three thousand six hundred side doors, it is but wasted effort. This true lead—every household possesses it, every person sees it. Yet in the realm of drunken living and dreamlike passing, it slips by unnoticed. Alas! Without encountering a true master, who could recognize it?

Nowadays, learners are unwilling to devote themselves earnestly to seeking a master. Instead, they merely memorize a few cases from the ancients, relying on their quick wit and sharp repartee to display superficial cleverness. They do not consider how their tongues may lead them astray—what use is that? Even if their eloquence flows like a river, it becomes a demon on the path of the Dao, revealing only their shallow learning and narrow vision. How then could they possess the eye of great discernment to bow before a master beneath the bonds of constraint?”

He further said: “Without receiving the oral transmission from a true master, even if one knows the medicine, the elixir will not form. The nine schools and hundred traditions—all such arts—may be preserved in writing, or guessed through cleverness. Only the golden elixir cannot be grasped by force of will alone. Without a true master to guide each step, one may know the vessel but not the moment the medicine arises; know the medicine but not the firing times; know the firing times but not the inversion; know the inversion but not the subtleties of refining the self; or fail to harmonize method and resources—none of these will yield the elixir.

Fools who have never met a true master do not know the world contains the way of the returning elixir. How then do they wander in vain, wielding sharp debate and cunning deceit, blindly misleading their contemporaries? When they err, they refuse to reflect on their missteps or weigh the consequences of sin and blessing. Since receiving my master’s teachings, whenever I encounter such people, I wish to awaken them and guide them back to the true path. Yet the ignorant and shallow remain obstinate and unteachable. Alas!”

Master Zhuang Xian spoke truly when he said, *“Such men will be mutilated by Heaven itself.”*

*“The supreme treasure of the Golden Elixir is not found in remote mountains or secluded valleys—it must be sought within the laws of the world.”*

Master Daoguang of the *Three Commentaries* said: *“Massage and breathwork are called side doors; consuming others’ qi is called the Golden Elixir.”*
*“The Gate of the Mysterious Female is the root of Heaven and Earth.” Yet none in this world understand this—without a true master’s guidance, who could comprehend it?*
*“Latecomers to the Way refuse to humble themselves and ask others. If they could but awaken to the existence of the deathless medicine—this treasure of self-cultivation, this peerless formula for immortality—”*
*“This Dao is wondrous indeed! Without a true master’s oral transmission of the secret instructions, who could attain its marvels?”*

Master Lu Ziye of the *Three Commentaries* said: *“Without a true master’s precise instruction on the true lead and its sequence, do not force the practice.”*
*“This Way is the reversal and union of true yin and true yang, stealing the life-qi from within the mechanism of death—it is not the lascivious art of ‘three-peaked’ sexual cultivation.”*
*“The place of ingress and egress, the site of yin-yang union—without the true oral transmission from a master, how could one guess and know it?”*
*“Without the master’s oral transmission of the essentials, where would one even begin?”*

Master Shangyang’s *Commentary on the* *Triple Unification* said: *“To ascend from the mundane to the sacred, to become a Buddha or an immortal—these secrets of heart-to-heart, mouth-to-mouth transmission dare not be committed to writing. Alas! The world’s people are shallow in virtue and fickle in trust; slander arises easily.”*
*“This Way is the raft for all beings, the bridge for ten thousand generations. How could later generations, each clinging to their own views, fail to resolve themselves to seek a true master, or fail to understand the mutual resonance of yin and yang? Each upholds what they have heard, straying ever further.”*
*“When they see the* Book of Changes*, they take it for a manual of divination and hexagram sequences—how would they know the Way of like attracting like?”*
*“When they hear of the crucible, they assume it refers to smelting metals and firing furnaces.”*
*“When they hear of ‘gathering,’ they assume it means the ‘three-peaked’ sexual arts.”*
*“When they hear of ‘effort,’ they suspect it is a deviant side path.”*
*“When they hear of ‘non-effort,’ they suspect it is mere empty sitting.”*
*“When they hear of the Great Vehicle, they cling to Chan’s emptiness.”*
*“They only engage in idle talk, never examining the Sage’s Way: that one refines with yin and yang to transcend yin and yang, refines with worldly methods to transcend the world.”*
*“The celestial sun has twelve degrees; when it aligns with the sun, the lesser yin of the human realm, in its hidden form, reads the scriptures—this is the norm of yin and yang.”*
*“When yin and yang harmonize, the numinous is born.”*
*“The human body mirrors the moon, giving birth to the Golden Elixir.”*
*The* Canticle *says: “Push emotion to unite with nature, turning to join with one another.”*
*“Qi comes from without; with it, one can refine the elixir and enter the sacred.”*
*“Refining the Great Elixir and the moment of receiving qi at birth are fundamentally no different—only the direction, forward or reversed, sets them apart.”*
*“When female and male of the same kind meet, they invert and stir one another. When man and woman seek one another, they reverse to grasp the mechanism of transformation.”*
*“Fools take non-effort and empty sitting as the Way, drifting through days, resigned to life and death. Such people are the greatest sinners in the teachings—how dare they even speak of cultivation?”*
*“The Golden Elixir requires medicine of the same kind: one yin, one yang, mutually stirring; one female, one male, to generate transformation. If one dwells alone in solitude, how can the qi of generation arise? If many females lack a male, where is the path of ceaseless life?”*
*“To refine the returning elixir, one must seek the primordial qi to complete the elixir. The workings of this practice cannot be understood without a master; even the wise like Yan and Min cannot grasp it on their own.”*
*“The primordial qi is sought where one’s own body was born.”*
*“From ancient times to now, countless have loved this Way. Without meeting a true master, few have succeeded.”*
*“The world’s fools hear that someone has sat in meditation for years or entered seclusion in several places, and they immediately call them enlightened. How would they know the lesson of Mazu and Nanyue grinding bricks? How would they understand the principles of yin-yang, swallowing and slaying?”*
*“The supreme Way is bestowed by Heaven upon sages—how could one awaken to it alone? One must rely on a master’s teaching.”*
*“If one does not seek a master, how could one awaken? If one has a teacher, first test them with the* Book of the Triple Unification*. If they can clarify every line and penetrate every chapter, they are a true master. If even one phrase is vague or ambiguous, do not trust them.”*
*“If one truly receives the transmission of a true master and can practice this Way, then attaining sagehood and becoming a perfected one may be hoped for in days to come.”*
*The* Book of the Triple Unification *says: “Having no prior knowledge, one awakens through the master’s guidance.”*
Master Chen Xianwei said: *“If one’s good roots are ripe, their heart earnestly seeks the Way, studies the immortals’ scriptures, delves into the sages’ classics, humbles themselves to visit friends, and sincerely seeks a master, they will surely meet a perfected one who transmits the oral instructions.”*

Master Bai Yuchan’s *Commentary on the* *Verses of the Mysterious* said: *“To extend years and connect life, becoming a guest of longevity; to return to the origin, one must unite Heaven and Earth, join dragon and tiger, gather the elixir to connect life. Those who know this must never transmit it recklessly. Even if it is one’s own child or kin, if their heart for the Way is not firm, dare not lightly pass on the secret treasure of the returning elixir—Heaven will surely bring calamity, and nine generations will sink into suffering.”*
Master Bai Yuchan said: *“One secret reveals matters beyond Heaven; all side doors vanish without a trace.”*
Ancestor Sanfeng said: *“True scriptures are transmitted by true masters; the supreme Way is passed down by supreme beings.”*
Master Shangyang’s *Commentary on the* *Book of the Triple Unification* said: *“To practice the Way without mastering its words is to fail to stir the feelings of human nature.”*

To pursue the Dao without understanding transformation is to fail in the alchemy of metal and water. To pursue the Dao without skill in crafting instruments is to fail in the use of the crucible and furnace. To pursue the Dao without discerning fortune and misfortune is to fail in grasping the principles of sequence and reversal.”

Master Shangyang said: *“When the world’s people’s qi and blood are about to decline, they must seek the Dao of returning to the root—this can reverse aging, restore infancy, and attain longevity.”*

Master Lu Ziye said: *“If the world’s people were not deluded, each could accomplish this matter.”*

Master Shangyang said: *“Those who have not yet heard the Dao must urgently seek a master; those who have heard it must immediately seek the elixir. The length or brevity of a person’s life cannot be foreknown.”*

Master Shangyang said:
*“By karmic conditions, I met a sagely master,
Startled by his words, my doubts arose.
Only then did I know the profound mystery has few phrases—
How could such a wondrous thing be easily understood?”*

*“The superior person, upon hearing the Dao, diligently practices it.
The middling person, upon hearing the Dao, wavers between doubt and belief.
The inferior person, upon hearing the Dao, laughs loudly at it.”*

Master Niwan Zu said: *“The mechanism of binding clouds and seizing the moon—how could cultivation be difficult once the secret is obtained? If you truly bind the clouds upon the mountain and grasp the moon’s essence, why fear not ascending bodily?”*

Perfected One Zixian said: *“The Dao is utterly simple, its practice not remote. Yet without great merit and noble deeds, one cannot encounter a true master.”*

Xiao Zixu said: *“The supreme Dao has always involved few matters—it is only that people of this age fail to comprehend it fully.”*

Bai Yuchan said: *“Only because the celestial mechanism is wondrously simple is it scattered through alchemical classics, unwilling to be revealed.”*

Zhang Ziyang said: *“To the enlightened, it is simple and easy; to the deluded, it grows ever more cumbersome and difficult.”*

*The Wuzhen Pian* said: *“The work is easy, the medicine not distant—revealed, people would surely laugh.”*

Xue Zixian said: *“Immortals refuse to speak plainly; if they did, people would laugh themselves to death.”*

Shi Xinglin said: *“Words of simplicity do not exceed half a phrase; the effect of verification occurs in an instant.”*

Master Shangyang said: *“Before meeting a true master, discussing the Dao is difficult; having heard its mystery, it seems as nothing.”*

Ancestor Zhongli said: *“This Dao is clear and involves few matters—alas, those with meager fortune remain obstinately deluded.”*

*The Huangting Jing* said: *“The supreme Dao is not burdensome; the secret preserves the true,”* and also: *“The Dao of nurturing life is not at all cumbersome.”*

*The Cantong Qi* said: *“Its words are concise and easy to ponder; its affairs are few and not burdensome.”*

Ancestor Qiu Changchun said: *“To gather the medicine, one must rely on a master’s guidance.”*

Ancestor Qiu Changchun said: *“Lead the White Tiger home to raise it; to subdue it, one must seek the orally transmitted method.”*

Ancestor Qiu said: *“The star above Mount Emei, the moon within the Northern Sea’s tide—celestial secrets passed down by the master must not be spoken to the common folk.”*

Ancestor Qiu said: *“If one can obtain the oral instructions, the cultivation of the true is excellent; seek the Lead early to connect with life.”*

Ancestor Qiu said: *“The subtle and wondrous true mechanism lies in oral transmission; one who obtains the method may attain immortality.”*

Ancestor Qiu said: *“Do not mistake non-action for the Dao; only through action does one reach the true.”*

Ancestor Qiu said: *“To surely become an immortal or Buddha, the matter is truly possible—one can indeed transcend the cycle of rebirth; seek a master and companions early.”*

Ancestor Qiu said: *“Passed down is the gold within water; the valley’s echo responds to the call.”*

*The Cantong Qi* said: *“The Three, the Five, and the One are the essence of Heaven and Earth. They may be conveyed through oral instructions but are difficult to transmit in writing.”*

Ancestor Xu’s *Stone Casket Record* said: *“The instructions are most strictly guarded; the secret lies in the mouth.”*

Zhang Sanfeng said: *“A single oral instruction of celestial mechanism is worth ten thousand pieces of gold,”* and also: *“I urge the worthy: do not act presumptuously; without meeting an enlightened master, do not force guesses.”*

Bodhidharma said: *“No expounding of dharma, no discussion of sutras—direct pointing to the source of birth is singly transmitted.”*

Ancestor Ma’s *Song of the Returned Elixir* said: *“The profound and subtle oral instructions are not verbose; they lie right before one’s eyes, yet people overlook them,”* and also: *“Before your eyes, so very easy—those who obtain and ingest it are wondrous beyond compare.”*

Ancestor Niyuan said: *“The path lies before your eyes, yet you know not where; toiling in vain, you perish in darkness.”*

*The Stroke of a Pen to Break Delusion* states: *“True cultivation requires oral instructions personally transmitted by the master. I urge the deluded: strike out your self-willed and obstinate mind with a single stroke.”* And also: *“Follow the Lead and Mercury; the Dragon and Tiger are before your eyes. Only when you know the origin of your born body will you grasp the workings of creation in your hands.”*

*The Treatise on Holding to the Center* said: *“The immortal’s secret of dying to self and living for me, the method of transformation by relinquishing oneself to follow others.”*

Ancestor Lü’s *Three-Character Oral Instructions* said:
*“This Dao is no ordinary Dao.
The root of life and destiny, the aperture of life and death.
Spoken, it seems coarse; practiced, it is wondrous.
All despise it, all mock it.
The great key lies in inversion.
Do not loathe the foul, do not fuss over trifles.
Obtain it, and effects appear at once.
Heaven and Earth in harmony—this is the omen.
Mouth to mouth, aperture to aperture.
Swallow it into the belly, and you will know for yourself.
The medicine is fresh—this is the sign of the primordial.
Examine between the brows, practice the reverse path.
The dregs and matter will naturally continue.
When these two are in surplus, then it is most wondrous.
To practice and uphold it, people of today call out.
Qi must be firm, spirit must not be depleted.
If you do not practice, you will age in vain.
Recognize the true, and the old become young.
To those who do not know, do not reveal it.
This small method accords with the great Dao.
Essence, qi, and spirit are the elixir of agelessness.
Preserved in stillness, repaid in clarity.
Riding the phoenix and crane, heed the celestial decree.”*

Zhang Sanfeng said: “Entering Mount Song, I received the Fire Dragon’s oral transmission, who commanded me to leave the mountain, seek companions, and pursue lead.”

The *Inscription at Qingyang Palace* states:
“The primordial is what immortals transmit by word of mouth.
Immortals, immortals—
they slumber only amid the blossoms.”

The *Jade Thread Classic* says:
“Without true transmission, what is hardest to attain is faith.
Having entered the true lineage, what is hardest to forget is the seed of emotion.”

The *Cavern Mystery Scripture* says:
“Within the household lies the supreme treasure,
yet worldly people are obscured and cannot perceive it.”

Lüzu’s *Song of the Cauldron* declares:
“One must have a true master’s true oral instructions,
who reveals the three-grade elixir of yin and yang—
only then may the heart abide and await the bright moon.”

Lüzu’s *Song of Gathering Gold* says:
“This wondrous formula requires a master’s transmission;
without a true master, all effort is in vain.
Once attained, do not regard it lightly.
The perfected transmit it; the unworthy are far from it.
Not even ten thousand taels of gold would one exchange for it.”

Zhengyang Zu says:
“Within the Hall of Containing Primordiality lies the Crystal Palace,
where the immortal’s cavern is clearly pointed out.
The Dao-heart unwavering, thus it is transmitted to you;
with vows sworn and words pledged, blood is solemnly shed.
When meeting others—do not speak recklessly.
When encountering friends—no need for secrets.
Do not fault me for repeating these words:
carelessness will surely bring karmic retribution from the nether courts.”

The *Song of Knocking on Hexagrams* says:
“When the Yellow Dame matches them in perfect union,
the transmission is passed mouth-to-mouth without a moment’s delay.”

Lüzu says:
“Though dwelling in the world, there is a method—
only that the people of this age do not reflect deeply.”
“True yin and true yang, people do not recognize;
a crescent of pure, limpid moon is revealed.”

The *Essentials of Gathering the True* says:
“Oral instructions must be passed mouth-to-mouth,
for it is through these instructions that the path to the mysterious opens.
When one knows the fire’s arising and the numinous light shines through,
the Azure Dragon is presented, beckoning the wondrous lead.”

Shangyangzi says:
“The primordial qi, like fine rain or dense mist,
or like dust on a bright window, or a grain of millet’s pearl—
its Dao is easy to know, its affair easy to accomplish,
with no difficulty at the outset.
“Only with unblemished virtue of ten thousand good deeds will one meet a master;
one must awaken to the mysterious mechanism at the master’s words.
Without good conduct, encountering one is difficult;
even with a master’s transmission, doubt will remain.”

Ma Danyang says:
“The master’s grace is profound and heavy, impossible to repay;
I vow to refine the utmost truth within the alchemical enclosure until death.”

The *Song of Knocking on Hexagrams* says:
“Life must be transmitted, nature must be awakened—
entering sagehood and transcending the ordinary rests with you.”

The *Admonitions of Metal and Stone* says:
“Without divine bestowal, it is difficult to seek.
To know the true immortal’s secret of mother and child,
first refine the heart before refining the medicine.”

The *Song of Realizing the True* says:
“Truly, compassion is the wondrous secret—
a bright moon wheeling overhead,
a furnace of red flame cradling spring snow.”

The *Admonitions for the Deluded* says:
“A true master is hard to encounter; cultivating virtue comes first.
Only then may one be moved to summoning,
and attain true sincerity.”

Zhang Sanfeng said: “Only today do I realize the Dao lies before my eyes; only now do I trust that the golden elixir has a true transmission.”

*The Orthodox Principle of Heavenly Immortals* says:
“In past kalpas and future kalpas, whether sage or commoner, the seed may be true or false—disciples are never uniform. In my generation, by the shelter of my father’s pure integrity and abundant virtue, I had fields, gardens, houses, and shops to sell. Enduring every hardship and toil, I sought masters day after day, guarding and serving them by day and night. After nineteen years, I obtained the complete teaching. Reflecting on past kalpas, had I lacked such shelter or nothing to sell, had I not met a true master, I would have endured those hardships in vain and been reborn in this kalpa. Moreover, I pity future sages: some may be born into poverty, without a father’s shelter, without property to sell, unable to endure hardship—how could they rouse their resolve to seek the whole? Others may rouse their resolve amid adversity, yet their will cannot remain keen. Thus, I cannot omit this collection, leaving it for future sages of resolve to sharpen their determination. I recount my own苦志勤求 to inspire them: they must rouse their resolve and seek diligently. Let future sages take heed!

“Zhongli Quan tested Lü Dongbin ten times; Qiu Chuji endured a hundred trials under Wang Chongyang. Wu Chongxu questioned Cao Huanyang for twenty years, met his master in the third month of the *jisi* year of the Wanli era, and received the complete teaching in the third month of the *wuzi* year—twenty years in all. At first, I resented my meager good fortune, that my master did not swiftly deliver me. Now I understand: those who wait long for instruction enter the Dao with precision. Otherwise, how could they surpass all ages?”

Bai Yuchan said: “Ten years awaiting the true chariot.”

“Again it is said: ‘The *daogui* was expounded on an autumn evening in the *guiyou* year, and all was revealed beneath the spring rains of the *yihai* year.’”

“‘The great immortal’s secret mechanism is rarely seen by ordinary beings. Sometimes it is transmitted to the world once in a hundred kalpas; sometimes a single phrase is secretly bestowed upon a person. Three mouths do not speak of it; six ears do not hear it.’”

*The Pointers on Nature and Life* states: “The great Dao of pure emptiness is hard to encounter yet easy to accomplish, though its effects appear slowly. Heterodox arts are easy to encounter yet difficult to accomplish, though their effects appear swiftly.”

*The True Words of the Dao-Song* states: “The single word *elixir* conceals a most subtle principle; one must obtain the true master and the true teaching. Even having met the true master and received the true teaching, one must still steel one’s resolve, sever worldly ties, and regard the illumination of the mind and the seeing of the nature as the first-stage endeavor; the water and fire of *kan* and *li* as the second-stage work; and the refinement of the body through division as the third-stage ultimate attainment. As for ascension, one must first complete three thousand merits and perfect eight hundred deeds before any hope may be held. This is no trifling matter for the impatient or the reckless to attain even by the slimmest chance.”

*The Transmission of the Dao Collection* states: “This matter is rare in the world, not something ordinary people may know.”

“Ten thousand volumes of elixir scriptures all emerge from the morning sun.
The essence of yin and yang is none other than dragon and tiger.”

Ancestor Zhongli said: “Few in past or present have known it; the sages do not speak of it. It silently conceals the unfathomable mechanism of heaven and earth—truly the hidden secret of the Three Purities. I fear your resolve is not steadfast, your study not single-minded, your heart not settled, your inquiry not earnest. Should I reveal this sacred mechanism, we would both gain nothing, and I would bear the fault of its leakage.”

Zhang Sanfeng said: “You must understand the inner and outer yin and yang—what they correspond to. One must cultivate the world-transcending within the worldly. Following life produces men; reversing life produces the elixir. A single phrase surpasses thousands upon thousands—no more talk of purity and non-action.”

In *The Secret Song of the Elixir*, Ancestor Lü says: “I reveal to you the great melon of the eastern gate in the year of *jiazi* or *dingchou*.”

*The Essential Principles of Lead and Mercury* states: “The supreme celestial mechanism is not recklessly transmitted. To transmit it to the unworthy is to invite fault.”

*The Mysterious Song of the Supreme* says: “To fail to transmit to the right person is to lose the celestial Dao; to recklessly transmit to the unworthy is to leak the celestial treasure. Transmitting to the right person brings profound merit; reckless transmission condemns seven generations to karmic retribution.”

*The Annotated Classic of the Celestial Pivot* states: “When a determined scholar is to receive the scripture, gold and silk must be offered, and an oath sworn before heaven—such is the law of transmission, not to be lightly bestowed.”

Chongxuzi’s *Analects of the Unity of Immortals and Buddhas* says: “Since ancient times, true immortals have transmitted the true Dao only after purifying themselves through fasting and ritual, presenting tokens of sincerity, cutting their flesh to swear blood oaths before heaven, and memorializing the Three Terraces, the Northern Dipper, the Southern Asterisms, the Three Officials, the Four Saints, and the Five Emperors of Fate. Only after divine permission is granted may it be transmitted. When one person is taught, all gods and sages throughout heaven and earth are notified. Should wicked men recklessly offer wealth or engage in deceitful private transmission, both master and disciple will face divine punishment. How grave! How cautionary!

Thus *The Abridged Bright Regulations of the Four Poles* states: ‘The formula for extending life and reversing the years may be transmitted only to the worthy, who must offer eight taels of gold, ninety bolts each of five-colored silk, and five pairs of gold rings. Master and disciple face each other for ninety days, transmitting the method under the sun and moon. Those who violate the regulations or betray their oaths will be examined by the Three Officials of Left and Right.’

It further says: ‘For the Golden Formula and the Cinnabar Formula, one must swear an oath with a hundred bolts of silk, vowing before the Nine Heavens to guard the secret.’

And: ‘To transmit without an oath is to subject both master and recipient to the examination of the Three Officials.’

And: ‘To transmit without sincerity is called transgressing the celestial Dao. To transmit without an oath is called leaking the celestial treasure.’

Moreover, *The Supreme Regulations* states: ‘When transmitting to a disciple, one must undergo rigorous purification and fasting. To transmit without scrutinizing the recipient, or without fasting, will result in the master’s death and the loss of the disciple’s eyes. If the fasting is not rigorous, the master will fall ill, and the disciple will lose their speech.’

The *Scripture* of the Supreme Three-in-One Qi says: ‘The perfected immortals possess the Nine-Turn Dragon-Embryo Golden Elixir, which grants long life and enduring vision. There is a forty-year covenant for its revelation—none may violate the regulations and recklessly leak it. Those without immortal records may not hear of it. If one presents sincere offerings and gold, and proves unwavering through trials, the method may be entrusted. If there is hesitation or doubt, keep it secret. Only when encountering a sincere, oath-bound seeker will the Supreme command the Emperor Lords and other deities to bestow talismans. Those who wish to learn the Golden Elixir of the Perfect Realization of the Immortal Dao will receive talismans and seals from the Jade Emperor of the Purple Tenuity, personally dispatched by the Supreme. Thus, those with talismans may be further promoted to receive seals. Only those with seals may be secretly taught the alchemical fire. This is why it is so difficult to encounter and comprehend.

Upon achieving the Dao and ascending, one’s talismans are verified to restore original rank, while seals confirm one’s place among the immortal perfected.’”

The Master of Supreme Yang composed a poem:
*“To gain the method yet lack wealth, affairs remain incomplete;
When both method and wealth are fulfilled, one ascends as an immortal.
The Patriarch Dan Yang was rich in the eastern lands,
Yet cast aside his countless treasures and vast fortune.”*

The Master of Following the Center said: “As for the meaning of *wealth*, there are two aspects. Generally, sacred wealth arises from the wealth of the method, becoming the ladder and raft to Dao. Before the Dao is achieved, one must rely on wealth; after the Dao is attained, wealth becomes useless. Worldly people, failing to grasp the subtleties of wealth-bestowal and Dharma-bestowal, compel those of humble means in mountain forests to depend on households of virtue and power. These two offerings—of wealth and of the method—mutually sustain one another. On the day the Dao is accomplished, all the alchemical chambers, vessels, and implements remain undamaged, left behind without attachment.

Alas! There are those in the world who hoard gold to fill their coffers and amass money like mountains, yet disbelieve in the Way of longevity, content to become ghosts beneath the springs. They spend a thousand taels on funerals—what benefit does it bring? Nevertheless, if a wealthy household is disloyal, unfilial, unkind, or unjust, those of the Dao will hear of it and withdraw, daring not to approach their gates. Thus, the Nameless Master’s warning: *‘Amid piles of gold and jade, one must not partake’*—lest they be tainted.

The Master of Supreme Yang said: “When yang qi lies hidden, only those with power can seek it; those without power will never obtain it. The Perfected One of Purple Yang relied on Ma Chuhou, while Wang Chongxi depended on the strength of the wealthy Duke Han.”

Stone Apricot Grove instructed Xue Zixian: *“This matter, without the protection of a great household, easily invites slander. You should go to the bustling metropolises and rely on those of power to pursue it.”*

Xue Daoguang said: “Nothing is harder than encountering the right person; nothing easier than attaining the Dao. Now, if one appears in the form of a high official or elder, gathering friends who cultivate the great Dao and refine the elixir, forging the millet-grain pearl in an instant, achieving the Dao on the spot—this is what makes attaining the Dao so easy. Yet, clad in purple and bearing gold, with gates as deep as the sea, those of the Dao turn away at the mere sight—this is what makes encountering the right person so hard.

Nothing is easier than encountering the right person; nothing harder than attaining the Dao. Now, if one carries a hundred coins on a staff, wandering the world alone, having long nurtured the spiritual root and received the direct transmission of the great Dao—yet the bonds of dragon and tiger are easily untied, while the lock of the medicinal spoon is hard to open; one may obtain the medicine but forget the years, or refine the lead without a plan—this is how encountering the right person is easy, yet attaining the Dao is hard. How can one achieve both at once, secretly knocking at the mysterious pass, seizing the once-in-a-millennium opportunity, dwelling on the Isles of the Immortals?”

*Baopuzi* said: “The nine elixirs and golden liquor are the foremost among immortal arts, but the undertaking is vast and the costs heavy—hard to accomplish in haste. Treasuring essence and cherishing qi is the most urgent task.”

*Baopuzi* said: “To seek a master who knows the method, one must use these funds to purchase the medicine. Those who possess the true secret arts will surely attain longevity and transcend the world.”

*Baopuzi* said: “My teacher did not speak idly, yet I am poor and lack the means, and have also suffered many hardships.”

*Baopuzi* said: “Merely knowing the method is no different from not knowing it at all—how lamentable! Those who possess the method may suffer from hunger and cold, unable to prepare it. Meanwhile, the wealthy and noble do not know the method. Even if they did, they would not believe in it. Suppose they did believe—would they, so rich in gold and silver, be willing to spend their present wealth to purchase the medicinal ingredients? Fearing future regret, they would not act.”

*Baopuzi* said: “To refine the golden elixir and ascend to heaven, the great medicine must all be bought with money—it cannot be readily obtained.”

*Baopuzi* said: “I have studied this Dao for over twenty years, yet my resources are meager, and I have no means to pursue it—only endless sighs. Those who hoard gold to fill their chests and amass wealth like mountains do not even know of this deathless method. Even if they heard of it, not one in ten thousand would believe.”

*The Preface to the True Transmission of the Golden Elixir*:
Master An said to Sun Jiaoluan, “If you can resolve life and death for me, I will not begrudge revealing it to you.” Yet Jiaoluan doubted whether the funds for the elixir were sufficient, so he again enlisted his friend Daoxuan Chen to assist what he could not. Jiaoluan said to his son, “In your efforts for me, must you not be as I was for Master An?” His son then gathered Messrs. He and Jiang to supplement what was lacking, barely preparing the crucible, furnace, zither, and sword.

*The Gourd Song* says:
“Bow to the enlightened master, seek the oral formula—
Without moving the ritual wealth, he will not speak.
Set up the furnace, erect the crucible, employ the ritual wealth,
Prepare the ritual wealth to purchase the golden liquor.”

In *The Triple Commentary*, Lu Ziye says: “Though one knows the subtleties of refining the self, without the dual use of ritual and wealth, the elixir will not form. Having received my master’s formula, I know there is no other method beyond this—yet what is difficult is my meager strength and weak resolve, which prevent me from practicing it. I have observed that among the ancients, *Baopuzi*, who attained this Dao for over twenty years, lacked even a shoulder-pole’s worth of savings and could not pursue it, only sighing endlessly. Thrice pondering these words, how truly lamentable!”

In *The Triple Commentary*, Master Shangyang says: “If one wishes to practice this, the essentials are ritual and wealth.”

Master Shangyang says: “The poor fear lack of wealth; those with wealth fear lack of land; those with land fear lack of materials; those with materials fear lack of companions. Companions serve as external protection—one must seek them with intent, first gathering ritual wealth before selecting a site.”

Master Shangyang says: “With spirit one may move them, but one must also delight them with treasures.”

In *The Triple Commentary*, Master Daoguang says: “When Immortal Zhang Ziyang encountered the Great One of Qingcheng, who transmitted to him the wondrous Dao of the Golden Liquor and Returned Elixir, he marveled at the difficulty of completing the medicine and thus composed *The Awakening to Reality*, forging karmic ties with fellow alchemists.”

*The True Principles of Heavenly Immortals* states: “The method by which Master Qiu aided the state is recorded in *The History of the Yuan*. Master Cao Huanyang transmitted the method of assisting the Dao to Wu Chongxu, charging him in secret: ‘If the protection of the Dao requires it, use it; otherwise, set it aside. Do not commit iniquity in the world and incur grave transgression.’”

Master Shangyang says: “To obtain this treasure, one must rely on wealth to sustain it. Great wealth can establish the crucible, benefit others, and accomplish the Dao. By employing wealth to move people, one may surely gain their favor. The Pearl of Maṇi, a priceless treasure, is then not difficult to obtain.”

The Perfected One Wang Ding says: “If the common folk seek the treasures of heaven, they must first seek the rarities of the world.”

Master Yin Zhen’s *Six Subtleties of Refined Discourse* says: “To pursue this Dao, one must rely on resources. Without resources, the Dao cannot be accomplished. Moreover, three alchemical companions are required to refine the elixir.”

*The Golden Strategy of Returning to Simplicity* says: “I wish to return to simplicity, but my strength is weak and the task vast—difficult to plan.”

Master Shangyang says: “Benevolence, compassion, love, clarity, and sincerity—these are the virtues of the highest power. Reverence, magnanimity, trustworthiness, diligence, and kindness—these are the gates to the Dao. One should prioritize kindness and diligence, for kindness suffices to employ others. To seek the supreme treasure, one must rely on the wealth of the world.”

Patriarch Lü says: “If one is stingy in conduct yet miserly in giving, ten thousand immortals will refuse to come.”

Dong Zhongshu’s *Veritable Record of Li Shaojun* states: “Shaojun possessed the formula for immortality but was poor, so he journeyed to the Han court to seek a path, obtaining wealth along the way. Once the Dao was accomplished, he departed.”

The Perfected One Ziyang says: “The wondrousness of the Golden Elixir requires one to encounter those with deep karmic roots, ancestral yang virtue, and vast financial resources before it can be achieved.”

*The Dharma Words of Xishan* says: “Zhang Pingshu succeeded in his affairs only after meeting Ma Duyun; Xue Daoguang completed his elixir only after encountering Zhang Huanwei.”

*The Ratnakūṭa Sūtra* states: “When the bodhisattva mahāsattva practices the pāramitā of dāna, they seek the deathless ambrosia of immortal wealth with the riches of saṃsāra.”

Zhang Daoling instructed his disciples to take turns contributing rice, silk, and utensils. Over time, they amassed great wealth to purchase medicinal ingredients, compound the elixir, practice qi-cultivation, and consume the preparations. Thus, in the methods of immortality, there is no substitute for this approach. He often told his disciples: “You may emulate my practices of qi-cultivation, daoyin, and the arts of the bedchamber, but the Nine Cauldrons’ essentials I entrust solely to Wang Chang.”

Baishi Xian was a disciple of the Central Yellow Elder. His refinement centered on the arts of union, with the Golden Liquid elixir as the highest attainment. Initially, living in poverty and unable to obtain the medicine, he raised sheep and herded pigs for over a decade. By wearing coarse clothes and practicing frugality, he accumulated ten thousand in gold, then purchased vast quantities of medicine to consume.

The Perfected One Ge Xuan said: “For over thirty years after obtaining this Dao, I lamented the lack of the wealth of the method to fulfill this wondrous Way and repay the supreme origin. Later, when I acquired it, all things proceeded as I wished. Those who study later should harbor no doubts—it is just like this.”

The *Divine Mirror of Supreme Medicines* states: “It is often said that the Golden Elixir emerges from the halls of the noble and wealthy.”

Master Lü’s *Rhapsody of the Yellow Crane* says: “Rely on both the method and wealth, seeking a great household to achieve your grand design.”

Sazu’s *Song of Realizing the Dao* declares:
*“If you heed my words,
Study the* Cantong qi *early.
Its explanations are most clear—
Cultivating the inner spirit is not difficult.
First, you must possess the method and wealth,
For there are several aspects to practice.
Repeatedly accumulate hidden merits,
And frequently perform acts of kindness.
Seek it amidst the blossoms,
Not by roaming the mountains.”*

The *Biography of Zhang Sanfeng* records: “Master Fire Dragon was a senior disciple of Ancestor Tunan. Moved by my sincerity, my teacher first instructed me in the work of refining the self, then revealed the oral secrets of obtaining the medicine, and further elucidated the subtleties of the firing times, the nurturing of the embryo, and the principles of transcending into emptiness—all was thoroughly imparted. Thus, I came to understand that this Dao requires the dual application of method and wealth. I have long traveled in search of this, and though I am rather fond of goodness, I have emptied my purse and overturned my coffers—how can I fulfill my long-held aspiration?”

Unconsciously, my distress showed upon my face. My teacher, sensing something amiss, questioned me, and I, wiping away tears, knelt close to explain. Moved once more, he bestowed upon me the elixir of cinnabar transmutation and commanded me to leave the mountain to cultivate it. Thereupon, I built a crucible chamber, relying on these resources to accomplish the great task.”

*The Flowering Branch* states:
“This too was my karmic affinity in this life—
Fortunate to meet Shen Wanshan, who upheld righteousness and dispensed wealth,
Yet his strength was insufficient to fully aid me,
So I could only tend the furnace and refine the fire.”

*The Unmet Patron’s Lament* says:
“Golden blossoms bloom so bright,
Yet without wealth, cultivation is arduous.
I dare not speak of this to others,
Each must scheme on their own.
Seeking a patron, I met a noble sage,
Who guarded the celestial mechanism in his heart for decades.”

It further laments:
“Alas, my deepest regret is having no wealth—
Day and night, I plead to Heaven,
Pity me and lend aid!”

An inscription at Green Goat Palace reads:
“To refine the millet pearl,
Both method and wealth are required.
Fortunate was Perfected Wang to meet the destined Xue Daoguang,
Yet he still had to return to lay life.
Bodhidharma achieved the Dao in the Pear Blossom Courtyard—
Surely it was amidst the flower lanes and willow alleys.
No more boast of pure non-action or withered meditation.”

*The Essentials of the Golden Elixir* states:
“Some succeed swiftly by obtaining the proper companions,
While others fail for lack of elixir wealth.”

Master Shangyang said:
“By the grace of ancestral virtue and Heaven’s compassion, I wandered the world until, at forty, I met my teacher, who bestowed upon me the supreme Dao. Since receiving his instruction, I have feared betraying our vows and disappointing his hopes. Thus, I have purged all former shallow knowledge and vulgar habits, along with the afflictions and karmic consciousness—yet I remain unable to procure elixir wealth, and two harvests have passed.”

Zhang Sanfeng’s *Rootless Tree* declares:
“Seek good companions to furnish both method and wealth.”

Master Shao’s *Poem from the Nest of Peace* laments:
“How might I find time to wander the treasure bazaars?
Loving others’ jewels only deepens my sorrow for lack of coin.”

The *Postscript to the Record of Daoist-Buddhist Syncretism* observes:
“Those with means to sustain the Way may transmit it to like-minded seekers. Those without means may rely on it to encounter patrons of the Way. Otherwise, one may have three generations of accumulated virtue and goodness, along with the ability to assist the teacher in sustaining the Way—or, if one’s strength is insufficient, to aid the teacher in small ways. This is what the ancients meant by ‘method and wealth mutually aiding one another.’”

Longmeizi declares:
“To ride the crane and ascend in roaming, one must rely on the aid of a well-lined purse. The inferior scholar hears this and laughs aloud—this is why the loftiest sages say nothing.”

Longmeizi says:
“I, shaped by the molding of the Perfected, possessed no resources from the outset and thus could not achieve completion. Day and night I hastened, and in a flash three cycles of twelve years passed. Once, moved by the Mid-Autumn Festival, I wrote:
*For sixty-six autumns I’ve grasped heaven’s mechanism,
Yet on this night of nights, my sorrow knows no end.
Divine work lacks three men to see it through,
The sacred millet’s numinous power eludes the twice-eight refinement.
To penetrate the Way, tortoise and snake require a land of blessing;
To know the crane’s flight to Yangzhou, one must first ascend.
Who will lend me the power of the whirlwind,
That in one bound I may rise with all to the Ten Isles?*

The *Baopuzi’s* “Song of the Flowing Pearl” intones:
*Flowing pearl, flowing pearl,
You enslave this body of mine.
Cloud-roaming the four seas,
Traversing ten thousand texts.
Hurried, harried, restless,
Forgetting sleep and food.
I consulted all my wise friends,
Burned through cinnabar and pearl.
For thirty years within,
The sun and moon sighed long.
Now I am sixty,
Anxious to avoid the Three Wretched Realms.
By my teacher’s transmission,
