The primal qi is emptiness and nothingness.
True yin, true yang,
One inhalation, one exhalation.
Jade liquid irrigates,
The Cavern Chamber flows with pearls.
The Perfected deliver me—
It takes a true man of mettle.*

Here follows the translation:

---

As for the alchemical scriptures below that speak of wealth, *The Secret Canon of the Grotto-Heavens* states: “By great fortune, I was shown the learning of long life and enduring vision. My master declared that I must first seek material resources to achieve immortality, or else remain a mere scholar of the Dao all my days. Thus, he taught me the arts of the Yellow and the White, and so on.”

It further says: “I devoted myself to this not for riches or rank, but to procure the myriad things needed to ascend the steps of the Dao. Moreover, inner and outer principles are one, and both converge in this ultimate aim—hence my urgency in this pursuit.”

*“Summer departs, winter arrives, spring returns, autumn follows,
Frost suddenly specks the young man’s hair.
Where now are the palaces of Qin and Han?
Mighty warriors and cunning ministers—all have perished.
Silently I reflect: this body is but dream and illusion.
Why toil so hard for the rank of marquis?
I long to break free from the cage,
Yet lack the alchemical funds—where to seek them?”*

*“I yearn to learn long life, yet my purse is empty,
Pitifully, no path leads to the immortal realm.
For years I’ve roamed the four seas,
My heart ever busy with inquiry.
I seek the Yellow and White to be the mother of the elixir,
Not to covet gold and jewels as a wealthy lord.
One day, by fortune, I received my immortal teacher’s instruction—
His grace is as heavy as a mountain; I dare not forget.”*

The lyrics of Master Azure Mist intone:
*“The immortal’s stipend, Laozi’s elixir,
Aid you in cultivating the Dao to become a transcendent.”*

*The Golden Casket of Hidden Books* says: “The inner Dao requires resources—mere thousands of taels cannot suffice.”

Patriarch Zhongli’s *Song of the True Formula* declares:
*“This elixir is not for ordinary men’s use,
But to sustain those who nurture the Dao in heaven.
If this treasure fell to common folk,
They’d buy estates and bequeath them to their heirs.”*

*The Record of Upholding the Will*’s preface states: “Since ancient times, immortal masters have employed the arts of the Yellow and White as aids to inner cultivation.”

Tao Susu said: “The furnace and fire are not schemes for wealth or rank. Used for self-cultivation, they assist the inner elixir; used for others, they fulfill the work of saving the world.”

*The Record of Upholding the Will* further says:
*“If you seek alchemical funds to aid the Dao,
First cultivate virtue and power to match heaven’s.”*
And:
*“The sagely Dao is no trifling matter for men—
Jingyang used it and became immortal.
Once the elixir is complete, boast not of your skill,
But hasten to dual cultivation and sever worldly ties.”*

Tao Susu also said: “The Yellow, the White, and the golden elixir—countless students have no way to enter. For the patriarchs left these arts to aid the Dao, and High Heaven bestows them upon the virtuous. Lord Xu first achieved the Yellow and White, then instructed Jingyang. Though his merit was vast and his virtue weighty, it was also the sacred medicine of the Yellow and White that provided the resources for his practice.”*

Master Shangyang said:
*“To seek wealth, to seek a companion, to refine the golden elixir—
Wealth is not hard, but a companion is hard indeed.
With companion and wealth, many external protections arise;
Why must one retreat to deep mountains to become immortal?”*

Master Shangyang said:
*“For the practitioner who has received the true master’s transmission,
First gather elixir companions.
Master Xue said:
‘Now that I have gathered the elixir of long life,
Year after year I seek kindred spirits upon the sea.’
And again:
‘For years I searched lakes and seas for immortal peers,
Unwilling to cease until I became a divine immortal.’
The Mud Pill Patriarch said:
‘Without like-minded friends to admonish and awaken,
I fear the firing times in the crucible may go astray.’
Chen Huqiu said:
‘Day after day I urgently seek kindred spirits,
Traversing all of Dongwu yet finding no one.’
For to find a kindred spirit and Dao companion
Is to have one who corrects one’s shortcomings and together achieves the Way.
Yet there are those with fine companions who have not attained the Way,
While their wealth remains abundant—this is fitting for exchange,
So that both may accomplish the work.”*

Patriarch Zhongli said:
*“In the dusty world, true cultivating companions are hard to find.”*
And again:
*“Wealth is not hard, but a companion is hard indeed.”*

Master Lüdü said:
*“A pure and tranquil family, like-minded friends with one heart—
These are most difficult to obtain.
Thus we know that the immortals and buddhas of old
All relied upon Dao companions.
Therefore the Twenty-Sixth Patriarch, taking leave of the king, said:
‘May Your Majesty, in the supreme vehicle, not forget external protection.’
Gushan and Master Xue Zixian both have lines on ‘ten years upon lakes and seas’—
At this I tap in admiration, sighing thrice.”*

Master Xue Daoguang said:
*“Three of like mind must guard against peril,
Advancing the fire’s work with utmost care.”*

The *Qiaoyang Classic* states:
*“When spirit dwells within the crucible and the elixir’s light does not depart,
True companions must be sought to regulate and protect.
Hunger, cold, and heat—all necessities prepared—
Should not disturb the heart.”*

Master Lü’s *Rhapsody of the Yellow Crane* says:
*“When cultivating both nature and life in tandem,
First bind kindred hearts as your support.”*

The *Song of Knocking on the Hexagrams* declares:
*“Seek the ardent knight, find the worthy talent,
Together tend the furnace and crucible to transform the mortal frame.”*

Master Longmei said:
*“Aid and harmony in unison cannot be lacking;
Three of one will mutually sustain.
The stalwart guardian sits as the foremost host,
While the disciple attends the crucible and mold as secondary.
Examine the crucible’s tension where dragon and tiger leap,
Refine the fire’s timing with both martial and civil skill.
From beginning to end, clarity is essential—
All depends on the disciple’s careful call.”*

Master Lü said:
*“To avoid danger, one must be roused by others.”*

The *Unity of Immortals and Buddhas* states:
*“This has two meanings:
First, when first practicing stabilization in the lesser celestial cycle,
Hunger and thirst may arise seeking food and drink—yet vexation does not stir.
Second, during the nurturing of the greater celestial cycle,
One must guard against sinking into torpor through excessive absorption.”*

*The True Principle of Heavenly Immortality* says:
*“The difficulty of companions lies in this:
As days of practice accumulate, the long-term support for preventing peril grows wearisome,
And the protection of the Way may not endure.
Some, after prolonged effort with slow progress, grow doubtful and weary;
Others, facing bodily afflictions or family hardships, diminish their devotion to the Way.
Doubt may arise: questioning whether the method is truly real,
Or whether the work can indeed succeed.
Bodily afflictions may include illness or misfortune in a companion’s body.
Family hardships may involve parents, spouse, or children facing great calamities,
Or entanglement in unjust disputes—
Thus altering their resolve to protect the Way…
Such cases are all too common.
As the *Baopuzi* says: ‘Those who pursue the Way often falter when nearly accomplished,
And their aspirations go unfulfilled.’
This is precisely what it means.”*

Moreover, it is said: “The difficulty of finding companions of like mind lies in their not necessarily hailing from the same family or village, nor being one’s long-familiar acquaintances. Those whose personal virtue and conduct are flawed may remain unrecognized in brief encounters. Those whose hearts harbor deep-seated perversity and deceit may escape detection even in face-to-face dealings. The evil roots and calamitous seeds sown by their ancestors may elude distant observation… All such men are precisely those whom Heaven would never entrust with the Way.

Even if one encounters a man of perfect virtue and steadfast resolve within the master’s household, chance meetings make trust difficult. Without prior knowledge of his moral character—whether he is truly upright or secretly perverse—one dare not lightly place faith in him. This further illustrates the difficulty of finding true companions.”

The *Gourd Song* says:
*“After seven days in primordial chaos, death gives way to rebirth,
All depends on companions to regulate water and fire.”*

The *Rootless Tree* says:
*“Entrust your heart to a knowing friend, guard him with care,
Ever fearing the furnace’s fire and timing may go awry.”*

Master Peng of the Earthly Realm states:
*“Seek the numinous mountain, choose the blessed site,
Build the elixir chamber, erect the stellar altar,
Set the furnace and stove, cast the crucible room,
Gather true companions, oversee the guiding principles—
Only when all is in perfect order may one proceed with the work.”*

Lord Yin of the Hidden Realm says:
*“Without the proper ground, do not act rashly.”*

Keep it secret, examine carefully how to protect and maintain. Guard and preserve the celestial and terrestrial mechanisms without loss—this medicine’s transformations are beyond comprehension.”

Master Zhenyi says: *“Penetrate sound and color, temper desires, abandon fame and profit, retreat to the numinous mountain, sever ordinary ties, forge bonds with immortals. Conceal yourself and cultivate in seclusion, diligent day and night—only then may hope arise. Without such discipline, all effort is in vain.”*

The Mud-Pillow Patriarch says: *“Avoid burial mounds and defiled fields, shun battle-scarred lands where men once slept. Only where numinous qi gathers lies true fortune—this is the lesser grotto-heaven of immortal-seeking.”*

He further says: *“The stillness of mountain forests is most fitting, whether in city or countryside. Where earth is thick, the elixir grows thick; rash action invites swift calamity.”*

And again: *“The chamber should face wood and turn toward the sun, with a bright window in the west facing the radiant light. Let no one know of its fame, and at dusk’s yin, seal not the golden walls.”*

Master Lü’s *Rhapsody of the Yellow Crane* says: *“Choose the auspicious site, guard the secrecy of the work. Prepare the elixir chamber, craft vessels of proper measure.”*

*The Awakening to Reality* says: *“Know that great reclusion dwells in the court and marketplace—why seek solitude in deep mountains?”*

*The Oracle of Metal and Stone* says: *“Neither clamor of the marketplace nor stillness of mountains—those who would know the elixir of immortality find the Great Return in non-attachment to circumstance.”*

*The True Principles of Heavenly Immortality* says: *“A blessed site must avoid the chaos of war, the encroachment of the powerful, the thoroughfare of travelers, and the disturbance of thieves. It should lie near a city for ease of procuring food, yet far from forests to escape the clamor of birds and wind. The house should not exceed a *zhang* in height, its walls double-layered, with balanced light and shade. The bed and seat should be thickly cushioned, and one should enjoy pure vegetables, tea, and simple meals. Nurturing the body and calming the qi is no difficult matter.”*

*Disputations on Cultivating the Real* records:
*“Someone asked, ‘In the marketplace or at court, one cannot escape human affairs—how can one focus solely on cultivation?’
The answer: ‘The marketplace and court are precisely where great function and great opportunity arise—this is the highest method. For the golden elixir exists within humanity and is sought amid the throng. The ancients, even in bustling capitals, relied on the capable—this is the very reason.’”*

The *Ding* and *Lu*

Wu Xiazi said: “For the practitioner, the vessels of the *ding* and *lu* are of many kinds—there are the *ding* and *lu* for refining the self, the *ding* and *lu* for obtaining the medicine, the *ding* and *lu* for obtaining the elixir, and the *ding* and *lu* for gentle nurturing. When applying the firing times and beginning practice, one must dwell in desire yet be without desire, abide in the dust without being stained by it, temporarily rely on the place of *Li* and *Gou*, and assume the body of the Dharma King.”

Someone asked Baopuzi: “I have heard that the Way of seeking life requires knowledge of the Two Mountains—is this true?”
Baopuzi replied: “It is so, but they are not Hua or Huo, nor are they Song or Dai. The Great Yuan Mountain is difficult to know yet easy to seek. It is neither heaven nor earth, neither sinking nor floating. Surpassing all in remoteness, towering and rugged, harmonious *qi* billows forth, and spirit and intent roam together. Jade wells run deep, their waters ceaselessly irrigating. The one hundred and twenty offices and courts abide there, with *Li* and *Kan* arrayed in their positions. Ten thousand stalks of the dark mushroom grow, and crimson trees rise alone, their treasures all rare. Gold and jade stand in jagged splendor, sweet springs flow from the corners. Those who seek longevity draw from their pure streams. If you can cultivate this, you may join Peng and Wang in companionship. This is the first mountain.

The Mountain of the Long Valley is dim and towering, its dark *qi* drifting, its jade liquid misting. The golden pool and purple chamber lie within its bounds. Fools rush madly toward it, yet all perish in the end. Those of the Dao ascend without decline. They gather and consume yellow essence to attain celestial flight. This is the second mountain. These have been secrets since antiquity—ponder them deeply.”

Someone said: “I wish to hear of the Realized One’s art of guarding the body and refining the form.”
Baopuzi replied: “A profound question indeed! Beneath the First Green, the moon and sun unite as one. Emerging from that jade pool, they enter the golden chamber, as large as a pellet and as yellow as a tangerine. Within lies a fine flavor, sweet as honey—if you obtain it, guard it well. Once gone, it does not return, and the body will perish. The pure white *qi* is most subtle and dense, ascending through the secluded pass in three winding turns. The inner elixir shines brilliantly, peerless in splendor. Establish it in the Gate of Life, and the form will not decay. Profound indeed—difficult to describe in full. This is the oral instruction of the master. Those who know it fear neither the ten thousand ghosts nor the five weapons.”

Baopuzi said: “The world is vast beyond measure; even what the eye can see remains incomprehensible. How much more so the mysteries within mysteries, the subtleties beyond subtlety?”

Baopuzi said: “Of the arts of the dark and the white, only the art of the bedchamber can transcend the world; only circulating *qi* can prolong life; only guiding and pulling can stave off old age.”

Baopuzi said: “The arts of the dark and the white may be likened to water and fire—water and fire kill men yet also give them life, depending on whether one can wield them or not. The methods of Pengzu bring benefit, though not necessarily as described in his books, for few can truly practice them. In general, their essential method holds that the more women one engages with, the better—yet if one does not know the Way and employs it recklessly, even one or two partners are enough to hasten death.” (Jiyizi said: “Those who today practice the ‘Three Peaks’ and ‘Battle of Plucking’ falsely adorn it with the name of Pengzu’s bedchamber arts—deluding others! Deluding others!”)

Baopuzi said: “In Wu there was a Daoist who, wherever he went, would acquire concubines, only to abandon them upon leaving—truly a strange case.”

Baopuzi said: “Long ago, Round Mound abounded with great serpents and also bore fine medicinal herbs. The Yellow Emperor was about to ascend it.”

Baopuzi said: “In the arts of the bedchamber, those who can fully master the Way may attain immortality, and may also avert calamities, absolve transgressions, and transform misfortune into blessing.”

Shangyangzi said: “Long ago there was an immortal named Song Xuanbai who cultivated the great Way of the golden elixir, ever fearful that the arrow of twilight would hasten his days.”

Fei expended every effort, refining the mundane alongside the dust, practicing grain avoidance and qi-absorption. Wherever he went, he might use gold and silk to acquire several concubines, only to abandon them upon departure. His strange ways were manifold, yet the world could not fathom them.”

Ge Hong’s *Traditions of Divine Transcendents* states: “Man and woman complete one another, just as Heaven and Earth engender each other. Thus do spirit and qi guide and nourish, ensuring that one does not lose their harmony. Heaven and Earth, having mastered the Way of union, know no end; humans, having lost the Way of union, meet with injury and decay. To avoid the harms of the multitude and attain the arts of yin and yang is the Way of undying.”

Ge Hong’s *Book of the Pillow* says: “The Primordial Lord then joined with the Sagely Mother of Great Mystery in the communion of qi and the conjoining of essence, summoning them back to the Upper Palace. At that time, the two qi intermingled in misty fusion, the breath of the encompassing and the sustaining harmonized, yin and yang aligned and completed one another, naturally reaching fullness. The flourishing of the Great Dao surpasses nothing more than this.”

*The Master Who Embraces Simplicity* states: “Though one consume a thousand medicinal herbs and the nourishment of the three sacrificial beasts, without the arts of the bedchamber, it will be of no avail.”

The immortal Liu Gen said: “Without knowledge of the bedchamber arts, along with the practices of circulating qi, guiding and pulling, and divine medicines, one cannot attain immortality.”

Wu Xian addressed the Martial Emperor, saying: “This Way is indeed the natural affair of yin and yang, a practice of the inner chambers—yet it is that of which I dare not speak. Moreover, its execution runs counter to human sentiment, and few are those who can perform it.”

In Zhang Liang’s *Commentary on the Yin Convergence Classic*, it is written: “Guiguzi said, ‘A humble life may yet be prolonged to undying, as the Yellow Emperor was moved by the qi of the youthful maiden.’” It further states: “Its mechanism lies in the maiden’s timely response. Guiguzi said, ‘When the moment arrives, not even a breath’s pause is permitted. To precede it is excess; to follow it is insufficiency.’”

Cao Pi’s *Treatises* records: “Zuǒ Cì cultivated the arts of the bedchamber, by which one may preserve life to its full term. Yet without utmost sincerity, none can practice it.”

Chungchang Tong said: “Gan Shi, Zuo Yuanfang, and Dongguo Yannian practiced the method of Rongcheng for controlling women, and all were recorded by the Chancellor.”

In Dongfang Shuo’s *Classic of Divine Marvels*, it is written: “When man and woman do not act as mates, the Dao of immortality naturally forms.” Zhang Maoxian said: “This means they do not become husband and wife.”

The *Classic of Divine Marvels* further states: “When the Queen Mother wished to journey east, she ascended and spontaneously united. Yin and yang depend on each other; only in their union does skill improve.”

The *Scripture of the Yellow Court* says: “The Dao-Father and Dao-Mother face each other, the Master-Father and Master-Mother in cinnabar mystery.”

Shangyangzi said: “Without true father and mother, all that is born is false.”

Zhang Sanfeng said: “Heaven exists only because the Mother exists; without the Mother, there would be no Heaven.”

The *Baopuzi* states: “Revere it as a mother, fear it as a tiger.”

The *Vajracchedikā Sūtra* says: “The ‘one-union form’ is precisely that which cannot be spoken. Yet ordinary beings cling to the act.”

The *Great Cavern Scripture of the Immortals* says: “A thousand harmonies, ten thousand unions—naturally they become real.”

An ancient gatha says:
*“When feeling comes, the seed is sown,
By ground the fruit again is grown.”*
And further:
*“Originally there was the ground,
By ground the awakened flower blooms.”*

Tao Hongjing’s *Declarations of the Perfected* states: “In profound accord they meet, the true Dao uncorrupted. Though named as paired counterparts, there remains no trace of defilement.”

The *Rhapsody of the Yellow Crane* says:
*“Set the furnace, erect the tripod,
Within the method, two Qian-Kuns—inner and outer.
Refine the self, lay the foundation,
Secure the nation of body and self as one.”*

Again it says: “Though divided into self and other, this is no chamber art of cinnabar or bedroom techniques. If one clings to singularity, how can one grasp the mechanism of the roc’s southward flight?”

Zhang Sanfeng says: “One must understand the inner and outer yin and yang, and what their counterparts of the same kind are. One must cultivate the world-transcending within the ways of the world. Following the birth of man, reversing the birth of the elixir—just this single phrase surpasses thousands upon thousands.”

*The Rootless Tree* says:
*“From ancient times to now, flower-wine immortals—
Open the gate and tell you plain:
Without flower or wine, the Dao cannot be achieved.”*
And further:
*“Born in the Kun direction, Kun is the human.”*
And further:
*“Borrowing their lead cauldron and precelestial medicine,
It transmutes my decrepit body into the foundation of the sage.”*

Zhang Sanfeng’s *Ode to the Precelestial* says:
*“Who is the maiden of two sevens?
At her brows, radiant colors shine.
Others see and crave desire,
I see her as my own dear mother.
A single drop of numinous elixir emerges,
Her whole body fragrant with powdered sweat.
In an instant, she dries my mercury,
Transforming my bones into pure yang.”*

*The Single Branch Flower* says:
*“I await only the maiden’s unfolding lotus.”*
And further:
*“I do not envy her beauty or her blossoming grace,
I wait only for her sweet dew to well as a spring.”*
And further:
*“How dare I act recklessly?”*

Amidst the blossoms, I strike the bamboo and play the zither—my heart as clear as water.”

*The Sacred Mirror of Superior Medicines* says:
*“Breath stills, flowers bloom in cinnabar,
Before my eyes appears a jade-like one.”*

Lüzu’s *Hundred Stanzas* says:
*“Seek the vessels for the elixir chamber,
Five thousand four eight springs.”*

Lüzu says:
*“The precelestial qi is called Emptiness and Nothingness,
Its circulation keeps the bones from withering.
To know the root of mercury, seek the Son of Heaven;
To find the origin of lead, ask the immortal maiden.”*

*The Song of Striking the Hexagrams* says:
*“One man and one woman mirror heaven and earth,
One male and one female unite Qian and Kun.”*

*The Ode to the Cauldron* says:
*“The cauldron is none other than the male and female body,
The great medicine is originally essence, qi, and spirit.”*

*The Cultivation of the Real Poem* says:
*“Within the chamber of man and woman lies the embodiment of the Dao,
In the realm of the colored body rests the foundation of lead.”*
And further:
*“The true body’s flowers and fruits hide within the cave.
If one can find the path to the mysterious,
In an instant, the poor arrive at the treasury.”*
And further:
*“Recognize the true seed of your homeland,
And well gather the white lotus from the sea’s depths.”*
And further:
*“Take the medicinal ingredients as they come from your own house.”*

Master Yuchan says:
*“Originally, true gold lies within your own home.”*

*The Four Hundred Characters* says:
*“The homeland’s scenery is fair,
Amid spring’s depth, wind and rain.”*

Lu Ziye says:
*“This lead is possessed by every household,
Yet alas, people do not recognize it.”*

And further:
*“Every household possesses what every household possesses,
Yet how few know it, how few return to it.”*

Zhang Sanfeng says:
*“Simply take it from within your home—
Why seek it wearily without?”*

Bai Yuchan says:
*“Truly affirming that man and woman are it,
Truly declaring that Kan and Li are not.”*

Iron Crutch Patriarch says:
*“Attend carefully to the furnace, without greed or attachment.
No loosening of robes, no untying of sashes—
Pluck the peach and willow blossoms, the lamp’s flowers, in due season.
Now I reveal the celestial ladder’s secret,
Pointing afar to the White Clouds’ realm of self-mastery.”*

And further:
*“A white-haired elder,
Facing that rosy-cheeked maiden—
Within this artful union, immortals meet.”*

*The Knocking on the Hexagrams Song* says:
*“Hold fast amid the mist and flowers, sever lust.
Color is the medicine, wine the blessing—
Within wine and color, no restraint.
Only through flowers and wine is long life awakened,
Drinking wine, wearing flowers, even ghosts and spirits weep.
Break no precepts, commit no lewdness.
Break precepts, and true nature sinks;
Commit lewdness, and the treasure of long life is lost.
Those who attain it must be people of contrary force.”*

And further:
*“Seek the true person in the willow lanes and flower streets—
The true person only plays amid the flowers.”*

*The Stroke of a Pen to Break Delusion* says:
*“True cultivation walks the willow lanes and flower streets.
I urge the deluded: strike out this ‘entering mountains to cultivate’ with a single stroke.”*

An inscription at Green Goat Palace reads:
*“It must be in the willow lanes and flower streets—
Never again speak of ‘pure stillness’ or ‘non-doing’ in withered sitting.”*

*The Kinship of the Three* says:
*“Work is easily done with those of the same kind;
Without the proper seed, skill is in vain.”*

Thus the swallow and sparrow do not hatch phoenixes, nor do foxes and hares nurse horses.”

Zhang Sanfeng said: “Of the same kind, they readily apply effort; when the inner elixir flows, the outer elixir flows as well.”

*The Awakening to Reality* says: “When bamboo splits, mend it with bamboo; to hatch a chick, use an egg.”

Ziyang said: “When bamboo splits, mend it with bamboo; when a person declines, restore them with lead.”

Zhang Sanfeng said: “When clothes tear, patch them with cloth; when a tree withers, nourish it with soil. With what does one mend a damaged person? The mechanism of yin and yang’s transformation.”

Lü Zu said: “When a pot breaks, mend it with iron; when clothes fray, hold them together with cloth. If an elder lacks the true qi of metal, how could one in ten thousand deaths ever live again?”

The *Classic* says: “Yang arises at *yin* (3–5 a.m.), the essence of pure Wood. Yin arises at *shen* (3–5 p.m.), the essence of pure Metal. When Heaven casts Wood into Metal, nothing remains unharmed. Thus yin can exhaust yang. The reason women apply powder and rouge is to imitate Metal’s whiteness—hence true persons and Daoist adepts all devote careful attention, discerning its subtleties, examining its waxing and waning. I move as the Azure Dragon; they move as the White Tiger.”

"Seize that Vermilion Bird to refine my Dark Warrior—this is the Way of immortality. Moreover, it is the nature of yin persons to be ever hasty in seeking yang. Yet outwardly they restrain and suppress themselves, refusing to invite yang: this makes clear that Metal will not yield to Wood. Yang’s nature is fierce and impetuous, its will and resolve careless and rough. But when it comes to social gatherings, its words grow gentle and mild, its speech humble and lowly—this makes clear that Wood stands in awe of Metal. The Great Gate Master practiced this Way and lived to two hundred and eighty years, yet still bore the complexion of a youth."

The *Triple Commentary* records Lu Zi-ye as saying: "Without the Golden Elixir, one cannot become a Heavenly Immortal. But what, then, is the Golden Elixir? Ah! Clearly it is nothing other than my own family’s treasure, merely lodged in the house of Kun. Kun is the human. What are these two things? Myself and the other. When the intent of the other and myself unite, then the affection of husband and wife arises, and joyfully one attains it."

The *Triple Journey* records Dao-guang Zu as saying: "True yin and true yang are beings of the same kind and mutual affinity. This supreme treasure exists in every household, yet because it is too near at hand, people lightly cast it aside, never realizing it is the numinous ladder to ascension."

The *Triple Commentary* records Shang-yang Zi as saying: "Who would believe in the word ‘subtle’? The world is deluded by love and desire, yet I make distinctions within love and desire. The great medicine of the Golden Elixir is possessed by every household, not confined to market or court—yet how is it that people see the dragon and do not recognize the dragon, see the tiger and do not recognize the tiger? How few are those who cultivate it in reversal!

"This elixir exists within the human kind and may be sought even in the marketplace. The supreme treasure of the Golden Elixir is possessed by every person, every household. Fools are lost in delusion and do not awaken; those of middling capacity may occasionally hear of it, yet still do not believe or accept it, and instead slander it.

"In following the natural course, one becomes an ordinary father and ordinary mother; in reversing it, one becomes a numinous father and sagely mother. The qi of ordinary father and ordinary mother forms a human—this is called the common Way. The qi of numinous father and sagely mother forms the elixir—this is called the true source.

"Only when yin and yang are of the same kind do they interact and respond. Being of the same kind means, for instance, Heaven and Earth as one kind, the moon and sun as one kind, woman and man as one kind, mercury and lead as one kind.

"If one clings to cultivating only oneself, then the thousand and hundred paths are nothing but side doors. The Immortal Elder, moved by compassion, directly points to the place from which one’s life was born—is this not too bold a revelation of Heaven’s mechanism?"

He further says: "If one clings to the self alone, how can one return to one’s origin and revert to one’s root? And by what means could one then reverse yang and transform the bones? The great cultivator, seeking the primordial true lead, must seek it from the place where one first received qi and was born—only then can one obtain that primordial true unity of qi."

The *Triple Journey* records Lu Zi-ye as saying: "The south, as Li, is myself; the north, as Kan, is the other. Take the middle line of Kan and restore it to the center of Li, thus forming Qian."

“The heavens and earth, Kan and Li—all are in truth the human being. The elixir emerges from the southwest, the position of Kun; yet in seeking Kun’s position, how could one depart from the human? Clearly I have revealed this—you must remember it, lest when you encounter it, you fail to recognize its truth.

“The union of yin and yang lies in finding the proper kindred. The balance of two and eight lies in finding the proper person. Find the kindred, find the person. Find the person, find the kindred.

“The *Book of Changes* says: ‘When male and female unite their essence, the myriad things are born in succession.’ The beginning of this body of mine likewise arose from the union of father and mother. If there were father without mother, or mother without father, how could this body exist? The essential method of making the elixir is the same as the meaning of being born, only differing in whether the process is sequential or reversed. Following the natural order produces a human being; reversing it produces the elixir. Between reversal and sequence, heaven and earth are as far apart as can be.”

The *Triple Commentary* records Dao-Guang Zu as saying: “The couple within the pot are the steps to the Purple Palace; the immortals are present before your very eyes, yet those who are deluded see them as distant as grains of sand.

“That true unity of qi is the mother of heaven and earth. This true unity of qi is the child of heaven and earth. Using the mother qi to subdue the child qi is like a cat catching a mouse—so that it does not escape.

“Qian and Kun are the true dragon and true tiger. The sun and moon are the bowstring qi of dragon and tiger.

“Take heaven and earth as your model: unite by kindred to complete the work of creation.

“The dragon is not in the eastern sea; the tiger is not in the western mountains. Even in heaven they do not exist—how could they be found in the mountains? Every household possesses them; reverse the process and cultivate, and the returned elixir may be hoped for.

“Zhen is the eldest son, the dragon. Dui is the youngest daughter, the tiger.

“How lamentable that people of this world, face to face with it, do not recognize it.

“Heaven gives birth to human beings; human beings give birth to treasures.

“This Dao is very near, present in your own garden—hasten to apply effort. If you seek it among those not of its kind, the more you pursue, the less you will obtain. If you find one of the same kind, what effort need you exert?”

White Jade Toad said: “Encased in thick blood and skin lies a priceless reality—once entered, it becomes numinous.”

Peng Zu said: “To heal a person with a person is to truly grasp the genuine.”

In his self-account, the Master Embracing Simplicity sighed: “Within mountain forests, there is no Dao.”

White Jade Toad said: “There are foolish and vulgar men who, ignorant of the Dharma beyond the world and unaware of the supreme principle of the returned elixir, recklessly voice opinions. They all claim that to cultivate the Dao and refine the elixir, one must dwell in remote mountains and secluded valleys, must abandon wife and children—how pitiable are such people! What mountains contain are grasses, trees, birds, and beasts, all of different kinds—how could one cultivate the Dao and attain the returned elixir there?”

In the *Three Commentaries*, Master Shangyang said: “The world’s foolish people, who do not study the elixir classics, assert that practitioners must reside in deep mountains, must distance themselves from courts and markets, must leave behind wives and children, must embrace non-action, and must engage in seated meditation before they can be considered cultivators of the Dao. How could they know the function of true yin and true yang?”

Moreover, it is said: “Nowadays, people regard solitary yin and orphaned yang—sitting alone in deep mountains—as the practice of the Dao, hoping thereby to attain longevity. How greatly mistaken they are! Do they not know that when yin and yang are blocked and separated, creation cannot be accomplished?

“People see only a stretch of extraordinary mountains and beautiful waters, and all claim that such a place is suitable for cultivation. How many have been misled through the ages! Do they not know that in great rivers and secluded valleys, all that exists are trees, rocks, elk, and deer—none of which are of the same kind, and thus cannot be used to refine the Great Returned Elixir? If one wishes to refine the Returned Elixir, one must seek those of the same kind, concealing oneself in the bustling marketplace.”

The *Wuzhen Pian* states:
*“Before refining the unformed elixir, do not enter the mountains—*
*Within and without those peaks, none is true lead.*
*Such a supreme treasure exists in every household,*
*Yet foolish people fail to recognize it in full.”*

It further says: *“Why must one dwell in deep mountains to guard solitary stillness?”*

In the *Three Commentaries*, Lu Ziye said: “Preserve my life, perfect my form, harm none, and benefit myself. How wondrous! Is this not the gold within water?”

“Mercury is what my household originally possesses;
Lead is the deathless formula of another’s household.
He is the position of *kun*;
I am the household of *qian*.
Drawing upon the generative *qi* within *kun*,
I plant the numinous root beneath my own garden,
thereby forming the embryo.

Call the tortoise—it belongs to me;
Summon the phoenix—it belongs to him.
*Kan* calls, *li* gathers, and receives the medicine—
*li* is none other than myself.

When the upright practices deviant methods,
all deviant methods return to uprightness.
When the deviant practices upright methods,
all upright methods return to deviance.
Such is the general principle of the Golden Elixir.”

In the *Three Commentaries*, Master Shangyang said:
“The crucible is the numinous father and sacred mother,
the *qian* male and *kun* female.
The medicinal substances are the *qi* of the numinous father and sacred mother,
the essence of the *qian* male and *kun* female.

The furnace and crucible are self and other;
*qian* and *kun* are male and female.
Refining within the mortal husk of father and mother to form the elixir—
this is emulating the creation of Heaven and Earth.

A solitary *yin* does not produce;
A lone *yang* does not generate.
Only when *yin* and *yang* are true
does one obtain the seed.
Ah! How wondrous!”

“Of *Qian*’s eldest son, *Zhen*, who governs the production of mercury. Of *Kun*’s youngest daughter, *Dui*, who governs the production of lead.
‘If the other remains unharmed, I too shall accomplish the task.’
If the two families do not each combine their respective earths, how can the *qi* circulate? How can the Golden Elixir return?
*Zhen* is the eastern household; *Dui* is the western. If one seeks the position of *Dui*, how can one depart from the person?
The mercury of *Zhen*’s palace belongs to me; the lead of *Dui*’s palace belongs to the other.
If one does not embrace it with virtue or bestow it with benevolence, how can it follow one’s use when the moment arrives?”

In the *Three Commentaries*, Master Daoguangzu said:
“To cultivate the celestial immortal, one must seek the same kind.
As the *Canticle* states: ‘Work is easily done with the same kind; skill avails little with the wrong seed. To become an immortal through ingestion, one must use the same kind.’
For humans receive the upright *qi* of Heaven and Earth, entrusting it to things of the same kind, conceiving and possessing it. Thus, true lead is the mother-*qi*, and my essence is the child-*qi*—are these not the most wondrous of the same kind?
When the two substances depend on each other and the two affections yearn for one another, only then can they transform and communicate with the numinous.”

In his *Commentary on the Canticle of Unity*, Master Shangyang said:
“Following the course of *yin* and *yang* gives birth to humans and things. Reversing the course of *yin* and *yang* must produce the Golden Elixir.
The ancients took the sun and moon as the character *yi* (change), for *yi* is *yin* and *yang*.
*Dui* receives the fire of *ding*, acting on *Kun*’s behalf to carry out the Dao.
When the sage and worthy practice this Dao, they transcend the mundane and enter sageliness. If the deviant practice this Dao, they lose their lives and forfeit their bodies.
Those who perfect its beauty are rewarded; those who ruin its work are punished.
The alternation of *yin* and *yang*—this is the Dao of *Yi*.
Cultivating concentration in the palace of *Li* is the essence of meditation.
Seeking the mysterious in the watery abode is the treasury of the elixir.
Though their names divide into three, the Dao is one.
Observing the origins of cultivation in the Three Teachings, only when their essentials are of the same kind can success be achieved.
When the *qi* of true *yin* and true *yang*—things of the same kind and mutual affection—are matched, how can the numinous elixir fail to form?
The lesser *yin* of *Dui* transmits and perpetuates the great thousandfold world, giving rise to humans and things.
The sun and moon adorn the heavens, waxing and waning in union. *Yin* and *yang* dwell in the world, generating and transforming in sequence and reversal.
Confucius, in ordering the *Book of Songs*, placed husband and wife first—this is the upright Dao of *yin* and *yang* without deviation. In assisting the *Book of Changes*, he placed *Qian* and *Kun* first—this clarifies the principle that hardness and softness must be paired.
To become an immortal or Buddha without the same kind, even if one enters the furnace a hundred times or sits in meditation for a thousand years, one will ultimately fall into emptiness and perish.”

In his *Commentary on the ‘Verses of Pointing to the Mystery’*, Bai Yuchan said:
“If one seeks the great medicine, it has feet and can walk—it is a living thing. If one seeks metal and water, it has hands and can grasp—it too is a living thing.
This treasure exists in every household; every person can cultivate it.
It is neither metal nor wood nor cinnabar—this thing was originally at home.
When Śākyamuni first appeared, he fully revealed it; why then did he later hold up a flower?
The Queen Mother was originally the daughter of an ordinary person; Ge Hong’s family was exceedingly poor.
These two immortals set examples for all to follow—why then do few heed their earnest words?
Without affection, what fear is there of a body like *su*? Forgetting both emptiness and form—this is the true man.
Recognize the method of hardness and softness aiding each other, and the spring *qi* of a single *yang* will revive the withered.
Flowers and fruits are not beyond Heaven and Earth, yet they do not depart from the human body.
The infant and the maiden of mystery will not unite without a matchmaker. If one has the karmic affinity to awaken, one can become an immortal.
Ah! Only wait for the day when the Earth Mother’s flowers bloom, and the Yellow River will run clear to its depths.”

The *Verses of Pointing to the Mystery* states:
“‘I earnestly exhort all gentlemen who study the Dao: take care to lead the hairless fierce tiger.’
The commentary says: ‘To know how to lead the hairless fierce tiger is to be not far from the Dao.’”

*The Gourd Song*
Composed by Ancestral Master An for his master and father.
Along with a gourd, bestowed upon his master and father.
Called the "Masculine Sword," it is the instrument for entering the chamber, descending to work, refining the elixir, and obtaining the medicine. The instrument is not transmitted to those unworthy of it.
This song is passed down for all who study the Dao to know.

Sun Ruzhong records:

The gourd is clever, the gourd is clever,
Two gourds run back and forth.
Within the gourd lies the golden elixir—
Those who consume it attain longevity and never age.

Neither too large nor too small,
A single inch holds Heaven and Earth.
Through the gourd, *Kan* and *Li* are inverted,
The eldest son seizes the maiden’s treasure.

Discern the old and tender, know dawn and dusk,
Do not err in the fire’s timing or the weight of a *zhu*.
Dragon and tiger mate in the Yellow Court—
To falsely practice the Three Peaks is to forfeit one’s life.

Within lead lies *gui*, hidden in the prior Heaven.
Even if you gather lead and *gui*, the elixir will not form.
The civil and martial fires clarify the six-six,
Before and after the crescent, recognize the three-three.

The bamboo must be struck, the zither must be played,
Count three hundred, seventy-five from the beginning.
Lead comes to seek mercury, forming the immortal embryo—
I become the guest, and it takes the host’s place.

Bow to the enlightened master, seek the oral transmission,
Without moving the dharma-wealth, they will not speak.
Set up the furnace, erect the tripod with dharma-wealth,
Prepare the dharma-wealth to purchase the golden liquid.

Cultivators must know their goods—
From the Divine Continent, nine are chosen.
The Old Mother of Li Mountain on the turtle altar,
The Ageless Old Mother ascends the jeweled throne.

Bestowed is the sacred elixir, a single pearl—
Swallowed into the belly, life rests in my hands.
For seven days in primordial chaos, death gives way to rebirth,
All depends on companions to regulate water and fire.

Yin gradually recedes, yang gradually grows,
Reversing age to youth is as easy as turning a palm.
I have heard the elixir can preserve one’s countenance—
Only now do I believe immortals do not lie.

Acting subtly, speaking crudely,
It provokes fools to split their sides with laughter.
This gourd is directly transmitted—
Without the gourd, one cannot begin.

This gourd is worth a thousand gold,
Since ancient times, even immortals and buddhas dare not treat it lightly.
If by karmic affinity you encounter its true transmission,
Together we shall become companions in the Dragon-Sand Assembly.

Lüzu’s *Song of Gathering Gold* states:
“Before gathering the medicine, establish the framework,
At the time of union, use the bellows and key.
Use the bellows and key, draw near to my body.”

*The Essentials of Gathering the True* states:
“A flute without holes needs no reed—
Simply blow, and the qi flows freely.
Directly employ these one or two things,
And wind will naturally arise atop the Mud Pill Palace.
Pressing chest to thigh stirs the heart,
Shoulders aligned, true qi descends.
This is the true secret of playing the zither—
No need for fingers on the frets to produce pure sound.”

*The Rootless Tree* states:
“Gathering must rely on the ferryboat of the method.”

Zhu Yuanyu says:
“In the language of the *Yi*, it is called a hexagram;
In the language of the elixir, it is called a talisman.”

*The Orthodox Principle of Heavenly Immortals* states:
“Disciples who receive talismans and lead the ranks
Are authorized by the celestial decree of the Supreme Emperor.”

*The Origin of the Records of the Union of Immortals and Buddhas* states:
“Moreover, the correct talismans and seals from Qiuzu’s lineage were also transmitted.”

Lüzu’s *Scripture of Verifying the Dao* states:
“The wondrous aperture of harmony,
The dharma assembly’s mysterious mechanism,
Abiding in the central Dao to attain illumination.
Presence and absence correspond,
Vacuity and fullness lie in central equilibrium.”

Lüzu’s *Scripture of Gold and Jade* states:
“Transmit the reed pipe to clarify the mechanism,
Understand the earthly killers to forget ambition.
A single tune in the land of intoxication—
*Shen* and *Zi* mark its end.
Three calls in the dream realm—
*Geng* and *Shen* mark its beginning.”

*The Seal of the Unity of the Three* states:
“Conceal the vessel and await the time,
Do not violate the hexagram’s month.”
It also says:
“These two apertures follow the method,
The golden qi also requires them.”
And:
“At the boundary of *Mao* and *You*, host and guest are named.
The dragon calls to the tiger, the tiger inhales the dragon’s essence.”

*The Awakening to Reality* states:
“First model the furnace and vessel on Qian and Kun,
Then gather the crow and hare to cook the medicine.
Once you drive these two things into the Yellow Way,
How could the golden elixir fail to be born?”
It also says:
“Strike the bamboo to summon the turtle to swallow the jade mushroom,
Play the zither to call the phoenix to drink the knife’s tip.
Lately, golden light appears throughout my body—
I do not speak of this principle to ordinary people.”

Tao Susi said: “For the great cultivator, within the division of the one aperture into two, if one knows the method of pursuit and gathering, then both apertures open. If one does not know the method of pursuit and gathering, then both apertures remain closed.”

Shangyangzi said: “The subtleties of the Golden Elixir’s method and the functions of the vessel’s aperture—how could they number fewer than a hundred?”

Zhu Yuanyu said: “The movements of the Zhou Tian’s celestial cycles are ceaseless, yet only the Celestial Pivot remains utterly still. In man, this is the primordial spirit of the Celestial Valley, ever responsive yet ever quiescent. All progressions and withdrawals of the firing times are nothing but alignment with this unmoving pivot.”

*The Record of the Unity of Daoist and Buddhist Cultivation* states: “The Celestial Pivot is also called the Central Yellow Golden Star, the Dipper’s Handle, and the Heart of Heaven.”

*The Precious Record of the Golden Casket* says:
“The Dipper’s Axis establishes the four seasons,
The eight nodes all follow its course.
The Dipper’s Axis stands truly still,
While the Dipper’s Bowl moves of itself.
One must only join the two eyes,
Exchanging above and below in mutual transmission.
This must be practiced in stillness,
Never rushed in haste.”

The *Canon of Union* states:
“Beside it stand ramparts and watchtowers,
Shaped like Penglai’s gourd.
Encircling gates seal fast,
Four pathways meet in hesitation.
Guard and defense are firm and tight,
Barring all wickedness and deceit.
Winding galleries connect,
To ward against the unforeseen.
Here one may be free from thought,
Yet hard to bear with care and toil.”

The *Awakening to Reality* says:
“The Gate of the Mysterious Female—few in the world know it;
Do not mistakenly treat mouth and nose as the true locus.”

“The Dipper serves as Heaven’s throat and tongue,
Measuring and harmonizing primordial transformation,
Governing the revolutions of the celestial sphere—
Like the main cord of a net, or the knot of a robe.”

The *Rootless Tree* declares:
“Revolve the Dipper’s pivot and ladle,
Tempering in one furnace the true sun and moon.”

The *Guidelines for Centering* states:
“A substance of inch-long measure,
Merging the Three Powers.
The Mysterious Pass—a single aperture,
Precisely at the center of Heaven and Earth.
Left and right divide the Two Modes,
Above and below fix the Three Powers.
To the left it connects with the Mysterious Gate,
To the right it reaches the Gate of the Female;
Above it pierces the Celestial Barrier,
Below it joins the Earth’s Axis.
Eight-sided and exquisitely wrought,
Resembling Penglai’s isle in form.”

The *Four Hundred Characters* says:
“One aperture—the Mysterious Pass,
Formed by the union of Qian and Kun.
Called the Cavern of Spirit and Qi,
Within it lies the essence of Kan and Li.”

The *Essence of Dragon and Tiger* states:
“Rising high at its center,
Shaped like Penglai’s gourd.
Gates sealed with subtle tightness,
Where spirit moves within.”

The *Scripture of the Hidden Talisman* declares:
“Behold the wondrous vessel,
From which all phenomena arise.
The Eight Trigrams and the sexagenary cycle—
Divine mechanism, ghostly concealment.”

The *Scripture of the Yellow Court* says:
“Crimson brocade robes with tiger tally.”
And again:
“Clad in phoenix robes, bearing the tiger tally.”
And again:
“Entering and exiting through one aperture, uniting with the Yellow Court.”

The Ancestor of True Yang says:
“Quickly lay the mountain-man flat,
Hastily strike through the Cavern of Dragon and Tiger.”
And again:
“Who lends the power to pierce heaven and earth?
The wondrous workings of spirit must be the means.”

Master Shangyang says:
“Spirit is a thing—
It must be employed as the instrument for gathering.”
Master Shangyang asks:
“Now, those who speak of gathering—
With what should one gather? What is the spirit that gathers?”

“This antique treasure—profoundly wondrous,
Its wonder lies in ever observing its aperture.
This aperture stands clearly before the eyes,
Yet lesser scholars, upon hearing of it, laugh aloud.”

Tao Susi says:
“Between heaven and earth—is it not like a bellows?
For the waxing and waning of yin and yang, the circulation of true qi,
The wondrous workings of medicine and fire, the ascent and descent, the coming and going,
Enveloping yin and yang to communicate the qi of heaven and earth—
This must rely upon the bellows.
Thus, the bellows is the gateway of yin and yang.”

Master Shangyang says:
“The bellows (*tuo*) resembles the gate of yin,
The key (*yue*) resembles the door of yang.”

The *Pulse Aspirations* says:
“The Mysterious Female (*xuanpin*) is the undivided Great Ultimate inherent in the human body,
Within it lies yin and yang—hence it is called the Mysterious Female.
Spirit and qi return to their root here,
Sun and moon unite as a single disk here.
If one can establish their foundation upon this,
Then the Valley Spirit (*gushen*) shall not die.
Yet there is also the gate of the Mysterious Female,
Rarely known to the world—
This is the root and stem of cinnabar refinement,
The dwelling where true essence returns.
The Valley Spirit is the name for the prior-heavenly, empty, numinous responsiveness,
It is our original nature.
Transcendent and solitary, it abides beyond decay.
Yet to cultivate it in stillness—this is no small task.”

Departing from distraction, one falls into dullness. Though right mindfulness arises, the moment it clings to anything, it falls into locality. If it clings to nothing at all, it becomes mere dead emptiness. Here, one must find the subtle mechanism: the mind rests upon the breath. When the breath is regulated, the spirit naturally returns; when the spirit returns, the breath naturally stabilizes. Spontaneously, spirit and qi intertwine, revealing the aperture of emptiness-and-nothingness, and the Mysterious Female manifests its image. Only upon witnessing this work can one refine the self and gather the medicine.

The *Pulse Aspirations* says:
“The gate of the Mysterious Female is the place of egress and ingress, the site where yin and yang converge, the locus where the Golden Elixir transforms and takes form, where the medicinal substances are stored within. As the *Canticle* states, ‘These two apertures follow the method; the metallic qi, too, requires them.’ The great practitioner, within the one aperture divided in two, knows the method of pursuit and absorption—then both apertures open. Without knowing the method of pursuit and absorption, both apertures remain closed. What the Golden Elixir values is the metallic qi, yet the metallic qi must rely on this method of pursuit and absorption to complete its transformation.”

Master Shangyang says:
“The external crucible is also called the Valley Spirit, the Spirit Vessel, the Mysterious Pass, the Gate of the Mysterious Female, the Gate of Myriad Wonders, or the Wondrous Aperture of Being-and-Nonbeing. All these names are like a deaf man listening to pipes and keys—utterly unaware that the Mysterious Female consists of two things. Without these two, how could the ten thousand things arise?”

The *Guidelines for Centering* says:
“Above, it props up heaven; below, it props up earth—this alone is the crucible. Once you know this, the work becomes easy.”

The *Guidelines for Centering* says:
“The Mysterious Female is the source of yin and yang, the dwelling of spirit and qi. Spirit and qi are the medicine of nature and life, the root of embryonic breathing, the origin of respiration, the Dao of deep-rooted stability. The embryo is the repository of spirit; the breath is the source of the embryo’s transformation. The embryo arises from the breath; the breath abides through the embryo. Without breath, the embryo cannot form; without spirit, the breath has no master.”

Xiao Zixu says:
“Midnight, noon, dawn, and dusk are the four cardinal points; the Mysterious Pass is the single aperture governing them.”

Zhang Ziyang says:
“Last night I seized it and brought it here, threading it through the nostrils to hang upon my staff.”

Master Shangyang’s *Five Poems on the Staff*:
“Who knows you possess such numinous power,
Propping earth and propping heaven to stand in great achievement?
Since ancient times, saints and mortals endure in the world—
Without you, immortals could not accomplish their work.

Mercury is like an iron rod, lead like brocade,
Turning the axis of Kun to pull back Qian.
One thing serves two—no more than this—
It goes to the Western River to buy black lead.

All the buddhas in the stone chamber are thus,
The Lord of the Lotus Palace carries it slantwise.
At the Yan-Yang Assembly, none recognize it—
Only offering it to the plantain for evening instruction.

Who knows the living use of the staff’s tip?
Lightning darts and stars fly—already too late.
The Northern Dipper and Southern Asterisms array as a pole—
Hiss!—at the demons, lest they raise their brows.

Born, it exhausts ten thousand kinds of ingenuity,
All for this single black caltrop.
Who grasps this bit of numinous power?
The immortals use it as a ladder to ascend heaven.”

Quanzhenzi’s *"Rhapsody on the Gate of the Mysterious Female"*:

“One aperture—the Mysterious Female—is the root of the Great Elixir,
A valley of emptiness and nothingness, mutually serving as the gate of ingress and egress.
The cauldron and vessel are set in noble and base,
Clearly opposed in their standing.
The mechanism of their opening and closing is profound,
Subtle beyond all speech.

Tracing back, the immortals establish the foundation of cultivation here,
Where primordial qi perpetually circulates above and below.
The lead furnace and mercury tripod are built upon this.
The Jade Palace and Golden Gate—few recognize them.
Vast is the Mysterious Female, beyond all naming.
Permeating yin and yang, it is thus called the *Gate*.
This is the cauldron and furnace, concealing within lead and mercury,
Eastward connecting to the Valley of Fusang,
Westward linking to the summit of Mount Taihua.
Grasping the essential marvel of the Two Earths, they merge as one.
Bordered between the two crescents, evenly bisecting them.
Great beyond all exterior, small beyond all interior.
Below it is called the *Female*, above it is called the *Mysterious*.
The cinnabar tripod, the recumbent moon furnace—
A single mechanism operates in secrecy.
The Gate of Returning to Life, the Aperture of Returning to the Root—
All marvels are complete herein.

This Gate—yang opens and yin closes,
Opening and closing without end.
The sun departs and the moon arrives,
Coming and going unceasingly.
Above is the Celestial Gate, receiving Qian and Jia within.
Below is the Earthly Portal, concealing Kun and Gui inside.
Boundless and without sides, it is not a form.
One closing, one opening—this is called the *Gate*.
High and low in harmonious union—how vast!
How complete!
Coming and going, circling in their rounds,
Exiting here, entering here.

Let us speak of this aperture:
All possess it alike, yet though it is not a gate, it is called the *Gate*—
Few in the world know it.
For heaven and earth perpetually unite in their ceaseless coming and going,
While spirit and qi ever merge in their continuous flow.
Now this aperture, hewn from the primal chaos,
Is built into the foundation of the One.
Judging by the celestial stems, the lower Female resides in *zi*.
Observing through the eight trigrams, the upper Mysterious belongs to *li*.
The Gate is thus divided, while the aperture remains undifferentiated and whole.
Thus did Master Ziyang exhaustively expound these rarely known words—
Otherwise, why would the Old Master have uttered those words of identical origin?

It has been said:
The obscure Female Portal lies deep within the azure sea,
The towering Mysterious Gate stands far atop Kunlun.
One yin, one yang—black and white are distinguishable.
Neither form nor emptiness—cinnabar and ink struggle to depict it.
The Four Directions are arrayed here, aligning with *zi*, *wu*, *mao*, and *you*.
The Two Luminaries revolve here, clustering at the dark moon, crescent, and full moon.
Subtle! Wondrous!”

The two characters "Mysterious" and "Female"—gather and refine them, and the work is but a moment’s effort. This is akin to the White Tiger below, serving as the pivot for kindling the fire; above, the Azure Dragon stirs the winds and waves of ascending clouds. Alas!

Minor arts of side gates have long misled the multitude, while those who claim exclusive mastery of the tradition pride themselves on their worthiness. Yet if they fail to elucidate the principles of the Learning, how can they align with the immortal scriptures? To name the Mysterious and Female as yin and yang is but a waste of contemplation; to regard mouth and nose as the Mysterious and Female is to labor the breath in vain exhalations.

Should one abandon the perverse and return to the true, gaining knowledge of the path’s authenticity, then delving into the subtle and entering the wondrous—how could this lie beyond the gate and walls?

Consider this: the single aperture of spirit within qi—where is the root of its gathering and storing? The inner circulation of primordial harmony—what governs their union and exchange?

Moreover, let us examine: if the White Tiger and Azure Dragon exist, why speak of a Black Tiger and Red Dragon, or of the Mysterious above and the Female below? Why left as Mysterious and right as Female? Know that wood and fire are companions, with wood abiding within fire to be nurtured; metal and water share a palace, with metal concealed within water. This is what is called "the Mysterious of the Mysterious, the Wondrous of the Wondrous"—its transformations, when expounded, are inexhaustible.

Fire!

Master Xue Zixian the Perfected One said: “The sages transmit the medicine but not the fire—few have ever known the firing times.” Master Chongxu replied: “Who says the firing times cannot be transmitted? They follow the moment in silent motion, entering the Mysterious of the Mysterious. The enlightened sages of ages past—with each breath clearly discerned—attained the immortal fruition.”

Yet the essence of the firing times must be sought within the true breath. For breath arises from the heart; when the heart is still, the breath is harmonized. As each breath returns to the root, it becomes the mother of the Golden Elixir. This is what Ancestor Hai Chan meant by “opening and closing the mechanism of Heaven and Earth’s transformation, forging within the furnace the true sun and moon.”

What is meant by “the true person abides in the deep abyss, floating and roaming while guarding the compass within”? It is to drive qi with spirit and stabilize the breath with qi. The bellows’ opening and closing, the ascent and descent of yin and yang—let the ebb and flow of breath proceed naturally. Concentrate qi to attain suppleness, embracing radiance in silence. In movement and stillness, sitting and lying down, maintain continuity as if it were ever-present. Like a woman with child, like a young dragon nurturing its pearl—gradually gathering, gradually refining, gradually congealing, gradually coalescing—until the work is pure and fused into one. In activity and repose, one must regulate with care. Thoughts must not arise; if they do, the fire blazes. Intent must not scatter; if it does, the fire cools. Simply ensure no excess or deficiency, holding and releasing with balance. Let spirit embrace qi, and qi embrace spirit, with a single intent of harmonious equilibrium, enveloping the primordial chaos.

This is called the continuous kindling of the fire, the constant warmth of the elixir crucible—without a single breath’s interruption, without the slightest deviation. Thus, refining for one moment completes one celestial revolution; refining for one hour completes one hour’s celestial revolution; refining for one day completes one day’s celestial revolution. Refining for a hundred days is called “establishing the foundation.” Refining for ten months is called “the fetal immortal.” Even when yang arises from the primordial sea and fire kindles within water, when Heaven and Earth cycle and the cosmos turns back upon itself—all remains inseparable from a single breath. Moreover, in all processes of bathing, nurturing, advancing, retreating, withdrawing, and adding, the inner workings subtly align with the celestial mechanism and silently accord with transformation—never relying on one’s own effort. How, then, could the fire not be transmitted?

The *Scripture of the Golden and Azure* states: “At the first kindling of the fire, it is gently warm, like the stirring of a hexagram.” Wang Dao said: “Fire is the parent of the medicine; the medicine is the offspring of the fire.” Master Shangyang said: “The firing times are most secret—sages do not transmit them. Now, a brief revelation: without fire, the medicine does not arise; when the medicine ripens, the fire is transformed. Without medicine, fire does not ignite; when the fire arrives, the medicine is complete. Yet the subtleties of the firing times cannot be discussed in a single stroke. Within them lie sequential stages and specific methods.”

Bai Suqing said: “The shallow understanding of the vulgar and the common learning of ordinary men—how could they know the Primordial Heavenly Worthy from the celestial immortals and earthly immortals? Day after day, they gather medicinal substances without cease, yet the closer they draw to the medicine, the more inexhaustible it becomes. How could they know the mountains and rivers, the great earth, and all sensate beings? Moment by moment, they practice the firing times without the slightest pause, yet the more they proceed with the firing times, the more unceasing they become.”

Tao Susi said: “The firing times are fundamentally one, yet when divided, they comprise several kinds. The fire within lead is the qi of the White Tiger at the first crescent. The fire within mercury is the qi of the Green Dragon at the first crescent. The fire of the two sevens is the first channel of the White Tiger. The fire of the celestial cycle is the drawing and adding over ten months. There is the martial fire of beginning and end, used for refining the self and gentle nurturing—this is the posterior yin fire. There is the civil fire of the middle, used when the talisman yields the elixir—this is the prior yang fire. There is the external fire of the three days when *geng* emerges, when *zhen* arrives to receive the talisman—this is the harmonious qi of Heaven and Earth. There is the internal fire of leisurely dwelling in an empty chamber, balancing and adjusting the superior and inferior—this is the original qi of the entire body. There is the fire of the wondrous union at the end of *ren*, when mercury is cast into lead, used in the first two periods of refining the medicine. There is the fire of raising water to extinguish fire, when lead is welcomed to restrain mercury, used in the remaining four periods of obtaining the medicine. There is the fire of the *Wei Ji* hexagram, with fire above and water below, the ordinary course of forward progression, used in seeking the medicine. There is the fire of the *Ji Ji* hexagram, with water above and fire below, the alchemical method of reverse progression, used in conjoining the elixir.”

*The Pulse of Longing* states: “There are external firing times and internal firing times. The *Canticle* says, ‘On the third day, the moon emerges at *geng*’—this is the external firing time. Master Cui’s ‘Heaven responds to the stars, Earth responds to the tides’—this is the external firing time. Patriarch Lü’s ‘At the first stirring of yang, the midnight clepsydra flows long; gently warm the lead crucible, light piercing the curtains’—this is the external firing time. Guangchengzi’s ‘The cinnabar furnace and river chariot rest not, the crane embryo and tortoise breath stretch on and on’—this is the internal firing time. Master Zhang’s ‘Idly guard the medicine furnace, observe the firing times; simply settle the spirit and breath, entrusting to naturalness’—this is the internal firing time. Before refining the elixir, the most difficult thing to grasp is the external firing time. This is the work of deliberate action, the task of establishing the foundation. The internal firing time, however, comes after obtaining the elixir, simply entrusted to spontaneity—this is the great rest, the great ease, the achievement of non-action.”

*The Pulse of Longing* further states: “Fire and timing are never separate; fire must accord with timing. When the timing arrives, the fire also arrives. Yet one must also know where the firing times diverge. Speaking solely of timing, there are the timings of the two sevens, of one year, of one month, of five days, of one hour and half an hour. Speaking solely of fire, there is civil fire, martial fire, fire within water, fire within mercury, fire of *Wei Ji*, fire of *Ji Ji*, and fire of the celestial cycle. The two characters ‘internal’ and ‘external’ encompass them all. Yet those who do not distinguish the firing times keep them secret.

“The external fire is the qi of the White Tiger. The internal fire is the spirit of the Green Dragon. Whether or not the elixir has been obtained, they are never separate. Only when internal fusion and external connection occur together can the two fires transform and communicate.”

Master Shangyang said: “The method of concentrating the firing times gathers the seventy-two seasonal nodes of a year into a single day, clusters the three hundred sixty hexagrams into a single month, and reckons the thirty-six celestial tally-marks for one day and night. Divided among the twelve hours, each hour contains six nodes—yet in seeking the elixir, only the fire of two nodes is employed. Each hour contains one hexagram line—yet in seeking the elixir, not even half a line’s duration is needed. Each hour contains three tally-marks—yet in seeking the elixir, only the speed of one tally-mark is used. This is what is meant by ‘single tally-mark, single technique.’ Thus the Yellow Emperor spoke of the *Yin Fu*: this is it. Therefore it is said: ‘People know the numinous, yet the numinous does not know; it is the non-numinous that is truly numinous.’ In this single tally-mark’s instant, the immortal elixir-seeker compresses the three thousand six hundred breaths of upright qi and reverses them into the womb. At this moment, one seizes the creative power of Heaven and Earth, steals the essence of the sun and moon. The earth’s axis lies in the heart, the celestial gate rests in the hand. The qi of the Dragon and Tiger’s two arcs are conjoined, the true essence of Metal and Water’s unity is pounded. Tortoise and Snake coil within the elixir furnace, Crow and Hare traverse the Yellow Way. Black and white intermingle, hardness and softness alternate in rise. The Jade Gate stores auspiciousness, purple radiance shines upon the sun, Mars guards the western pole, the Vermilion Bird flames in the void. Water hastens Metal’s motion, fire is urged into the crucible, the qi of the Great Yang is subdued and steamed, coalescing the Yellow and Crimson Elixir.”

*The Immortals’ Mirror* states: “The wondrous application of firing times requires season after season, only with long practice can one attain mastery.”

The Ancestor of Mud-Pill Palace said: “The eight gates transform and open in due time, advancing and retreating with Metal to fix their coming and going.” He also said: “Within the twelve hours, one must recognize the Zi hour; the wind from Xun stirs the lamp upon the water.”

Xiao Zixu said: “Fix the intent as it is, proceed with the firing times, then begin from the first line of the *Fu* hexagram.” He also said: “When this heart is lustrous as the moon at the pool’s center, unobstructed by the slightest thread, the true self is naturally thus.”

「A faint, gentle fire nurtures the hidden Dragon—
when the Dragon appears in the *Tian* hexagram, all must proceed together.
When the three Yang meet at the *Tai* hexagram, only then may one advance the sacred method of fire-refinement.»

The Mud-Pill Ancestor said:
«The fire-star ascends from Kunlun Mountain,
when Metal and Wood meet at the *Kan* thunderbolt hour.
When the medicine reaches the full moon, weigh it precisely—
urgently refine it, lest the timing be delayed.»

*The Mirror of Supreme Medicine* states:
«The Southern Cloud’s fire-wheel must be turned by man.
The Northern Cloud’s river-chariot moves of its own accord.»

The Master Wang Chongyang said:
«The Spirit does not depart from the qi, the qi does not depart from the Spirit.
Inhalation and exhalation flow forth and back, rooted in the two primal sources.
«Set the will to emptiness, serene and ever-present.
The body and mind act without contrivance, yet essence and qi naturally act of their own accord—
just as Heaven and Earth act without contrivance, yet all things naturally transform and are born.
«When qi and Spirit merge, the Five Phases and Four Symbols naturally gather,
and essence-qi congeals.»

The Master Lü said:
«When obtained, fuse and refine with diligence—
once *Ji Ji* is complete, cease work and hold in silence.»

*The Ancient Record* states:
«Six hundred fire-records exist, each resembling the other in refining true lead.»

*The Essentials of Refining True* says:
«First subdue the Dragon, then the Tiger; the Tiger, then the Dragon.
When Dragon and Tiger intermingle, true qi intensifies.
«Yet transmit this through oral instruction and mental transmission—
oral instruction and mental transmission require diligent practice.»

*The Three Commentaries*—Master Shangyangzi said:
«The Golden Elixir is the primal qi of yin and yang,
the very first of the Great Polarity, the root of the Great Earth.»

*The Three Commentaries*—Master Lü Ziyě said:
«Fire is the qi of yin and yang.
When merged and circulating within, it is warm and harmonious,
thus able to melt the true essence of things and cause their union.
If the qi of yin and yang does not merge, it is not fire.
Only when yin and yang merge does one apply the fire-refinement.»

*The Three Commentaries*—Master Daoguangzu said:
«The *Chong* qi is harmonious.
Before it takes form, the harmonious *Chong* qi is invisible.
Once formed, clear qi is Yang, turbid qi is Yin.
The two *qi* rise in vaporous interplay—
called Heaven, called Earth, called Man—
the Three Talents are complete.
*The Classic of Change* says:
*‘Heaven and Earth in vaporous interplay, all things transform and are born.
Male and female unite in essence, all things transform and are born.’*
The Sage penetrated this mystery and knew its source,
exhausted its divine principle and understood its transformation,
thus able to return to the origin and restore the One,
reverse the workings of Nature,
deem the Mother-gas of Heaven and Earth as base for the Elixir,
and steal the essence-qi of yin and yang as fire.
«Refining the form returns it to a single qi,
refining the qi re-enters it into the Void—
thus attaining unity of body and Dao,
subtle, rounded, and boundless in transformation,
hidden yet manifest, unfathomable.
«The Tiger’s fire, hidden within Yin, illuminates the dry Dragon;
the Dragon then emits the fire of Kunlun in response.
When these two fires merge and harmonize,
the true One’s essence naturally congeals.
«The two fires intermingle, lead and mercury unite.
«Fire is not the vulgar fire of the world—
it is the primal qi of the Original Beginning.»

Yin Qinghe said:
«Refine the primal qi of the Great Brahman,
extract the golden essence from the elbow’s posterior.»

*The Pulse-Gazing* states:
«When it moves, one may obtain the medicine.
When it is still, one may nurture the Elixir.
This is the dynamic and static ebb and flow of fire-refinement,
cycling endlessly.
My reason for internal use and internal listening,
seeking silence and breath-regulation,
is to align with the true One’s *Hongmeng* qi,
awaiting its transformation.»

*The Knocking on the Stems Song* says:
«If the qi flows, true fire refines—
do not let the black pearl depart from the treasure hall.
Increasing the fire’s intensity must be cautious—
the first line of *Qian* (Potential), the hidden Dragon, must not be refined.»
Again it says:
«After fasting and purification, await the birth of one Yang,
then proceed with the *Zhou Tian* method of equalization.»
Again it says:
«Inner and outer harmoniously interface.»

*The Essentials of Refining True* says:
«The three Tigers pay homage to the Dragon in irrigation—
always treat the two Tigers as *Zhun* and *Meng*.
The *Zhun* and *Meng* hexagrams govern morning and evening;
one Tiger must beware of monthly redness.
«The Elixir’s method, from beginning to end, hinges on a single principle:
contain the gaze, condense the hearing, seal the tongue’s qi,
rectify the heart and sincerely intend—
so that inner thought does not stray outward, nor outer thought enter inward.
This is the incantation for advancing fire and performing the ritual.»

*The Scripture of the Unified Dao and Buddhist Tradition* says:
«Most difficult to clarify are the True Person and the True Medicine.
Those who regulate the True and observe the fire have two theories:
one of breath-regulation, the first adjustment.
One without breath-regulation, another adjustment.
Know this: those who breathe should appear as if not breathing,
those who do not breathe should not force non-breathing—
forcing non-breathing while appearing to breathe,
if not properly adjusted, I reject it as oppressive and unbearable.
Not forcing but adjusting in accordance with the seasons,
I name this as *‘like emptiness, like nothingness.’*
This is the eternal secret of the Saints and the strict prohibition of the Celestial Court—
thus it is difficult to clarify.
Students should follow this teaching,
cultivate virtue and ally with Heaven,
to seek the degree of the Immortal Teachers.»

*The Scripture of the Unified Dao and Buddhist Tradition* says:
«Breath-regulation must regulate the true breath;
refining the Spirit must refine the non-Spirit.
«The heart and breath depend on each other—
adjust the breath until it reaches *Chonghe*.
If not *Chonghe*, danger ensues.
For harmony means not falling into forced constraint,
while *Chong* aligns with the principle of *‘not-empty yet empty.’*
Refining medicine is thus, alchemical transformation is thus,
wild battles are thus, defending a city is thus,
conceiving the embryo is thus, nurturing the embryo is thus—
thus the Long-Life True Person said, *‘Chonghe forms the Kan-Li,’*
speaking of the hundred-day critical phase.
Again he said, *‘Chonghe qi nurtures the Spirit,’*
speaking of the ten-month critical phase.
Wang Chongyang said:
*‘To fully preserve breathing and stabilize panting is not difficult—
but to nourish qi and regulate the Spirit, achieving *Chonghe*, is truly easy.’*

Again he said:
*"The Spirit and qi in Chonghe produce the Great Medicine."*

The Master of Upper Yang said:
*"Chong qi is the furnace of the Great Transformation for harmony."*

The *Union of Daoist and Buddhist Essentials: Dialogues on the Way* states:
*"What is meant by Chonghe is harmony yet capable of Chong,
Chong without limit—
this is the ‘ever as if intoxicated’ from *The Mirror of Entering Medicine*.
The *Lingguang Collection* says:
‘The inverted and revolving cycles resemble the intoxicated,’
and Cui Xu says:
‘Bone and flesh blend harmoniously, yet one knows not of it.’
This is truly the one who can cultivate the essence of harmony."*

The Patriarch of Zhengyang said:
*"Circulating the Microcosmic Orbit raises fire to consume the body,
filling heaven and earth, permeating the whole person."*

*"In the subtle principles of the Microcosmic Orbit,
there are also those who align with the Great Orbit’s attainment of medicine."*

The *Union of Daoist and Buddhist Essentials: Dialogues on the Way* states:
*"What is called the Great Orbit and the Small Orbit?*
The reply is:
*The Small Orbit is the moment when the Kan-Li interact—
the twelve hours within a day,
whenever the mind directs,
all may serve as that moment.’*
Within a single day,
one knows not how many Orbits may be completed.

The essence of the subtle principles lies in this:
Eating when hungry, sleeping when weary—
if awareness is present, use it; if not, let it be.

The Great Orbit is the moment when *Qian* and *Kun* unite,
when yin and yang merge as one—
the fire of the *Dharma Wheel* slow and steady,
endless and dim, like a drunken man all day,
endlessly guarding the spring within the cave.

Zhu Yizheng said:
*"Even this single Great Orbit is fraught with peril."*

As White Crane said:
*"No coming, no going, no advance, no retreat—
