no increase, no decrease, no subtraction or addition."*

At first, one moment is one Orbit.
Gradually, it becomes a day, a month, even ten months—
yet still, it is but one Orbit.
If it is slow yet complete, it is called Great.
Naturally, the subtle principle aligns with slowness,
and thus it must be slow.
If it is swift yet complete, it is called Small.
Naturally, the subtle principle aligns with speed,
and thus it must be swift.

Yet one must also know:
The Small Orbit has no Orbit to complete,
yet it is established as having one—
this is called *entering from non-being into being*.
If the mind follows the breath,
all departures return to unity,
and when mind and breath are perfectly still,
*Nirvana* is attained, and one returns to non-being.
This is the differing application of the Orbit,
giving rise to the names Great and Small.

Xu Zhengyang Patriarch said:
*"The spirit moves *qi* and transformation—
above, it spans the heavens; below, it weaves the earth."*

Yu Yuxu said:
*"If one can reverse the Heavenly Pass and turn the Earthly Axis,
and if the upper and lower do not correspond,
then one Orbit is completed with each breath."*

He also said:
*"Rising and descending, emerging and retreating—
wandering between *Zi* and *Wu*."*

*The Transmission of the Dao Collection* states:
*"The *Dharma Wheel* must always turn—
yet it turns unseen within the body."*

It also says:
*"The *Dharma Wheel* must turn without ceasing—
each thought must not depart from it, and it turns of itself."*

*The Union of Daoist and Buddhist Essentials: Dialogues on the Way* states:
*"Advancing fire, retreating talismans—
one must reach the place where one should stop."*

*The Yellow Court Classic* says:
*"Inhaling and exhaling, both return to the *Dan Tian*—
this is where one should stop."*

*The Yellow Court Classic* also says:
*"The dragon banner spreads across the heavens, casting the fire bell—
commanding all *qi* forces to gather the tiger soldiers.
On Kunlun’s heights, no mistakes are made,
veiled by the Purple Palace, the elixir tower is built.
If the sun and moon were strung like pearls,
I would soar above them on the Way.
The *Yu Yi* seals the *Lian* to preserve itself—
then the Jade Purity of the Ageless One is seen.
Breathing in the sun, breathing out the moon,
the elemental *qi* unites with the stars.
All are within the heart, communicating with the Heavenly Canals—
day and night, existing eternally, granting longevity."*

Chongxu Zi said:
*"Without the fire’s moment, the Dao cannot be completed—
I speak of its root, believe and practice it.
To seize true transformation from the world,
do not depart from the waxing and waning of the heavenly moon.
Subtracting or adding by such fractions,
advancing or retreating as Scripture dictates—
this is the ladder to the heavens in one’s grasp,
let it lift me to the Three Pure Ones."*

*The Rectification of the Heavenly Dao* states:
*"Refining fire to cultivate the seed is called *adding cinnabar*.
Cinnabar is the original spirit within the heart.
What is meant by *adding* is that it must arise from the fire of the Great Orbit.
Fire enables the elemental *qi* to nourish the original spirit,
assisting in the attainment of great awakening—
if the original spirit does not depart from the two *qi*s,
it will not be dull and unstable.
Thus it is said: *‘Adding cinnabar, refining fire—only the enlightened understand.’*"

White Crane said:
*"Enter the void and refine the fire’s moment."*

Entering the void is when the spirit-*qi* enters *samadhi*,
without clinging to forms—
as Master Qiu truly said, *‘the true emptiness.’*
Even when practicing the Great Orbit,
one sees no trace of the Great Orbit’s form,
and thus attains the subtlety of the void.

Chen Chaoyuan said:
*"When refining the elixir, if one ignites the fire at the *Zi* hour when yang is born,
the fire’s power will be complete.
Igniting at other times will yield no medicinal effect."*

Péng Hèlín said:
*"Fire and elixir originally dwell in one place—
when observed, they seem present; when sought, they vanish."*

Lǚ Zǔ said:
*"The drinker of the sea turtle’s elixir knows not the man,
the burner of the elixir’s talisman baffles even the ghosts."*

*The Scripture of the Unified Dao of Immortals and Buddhas* states:
*"All that can be spoken of are but the coarse traces of fire’s moment,
yet the profound and mysterious subtleties,
those in harmony with the natural workings of Heaven,
must be tested upon the meditation cushion—
only then will true understanding arise.
Verbal teachings alone can never exhaust the Way."*

*The Chant of the True Dao* declares:
*"The fire’s moment is nothing but the concentration of the spirit.
Where does this concentration lie?
It lies in the place of birth and life’s command.
When does this concentration occur?
It occurs at the moment of the true breath returning to its origin.
The true realm of stillness,
when conveyed by the pen,
cannot compare to its verification through the body."*

*The True Principles of the Celestial Immortals* say:
*"Returning the spirit and gathering the *qi*—
the marvel lies in the void."*

And again:
*"Taking the awakening of the spirit as the essence of elixir refinement,
using harmonization as its application.
To refine this *qi* and transform the spirit,
one must first unite this *qi* with the spirit in refinement."*

Chén Xīyí said:
*"The *Zi-Wu* practice is the fire’s moment—
two hours of life’s vitality, neither dusk nor dawn."*

Xiāo Zǐxū said:
*"Beware of fire’s moment’s deviation,
avoid the confusion of dreamlike torpor."*

*The True Principles of the Celestial Immortals* say:
*"Employ the original spirit of the primal, thoughtless Dao as the essence,
returning its reflection to inner observation,
concentrating the spirit into the *qi* and fire."*

An ancient hymn states:
*"The spirit returns, the *qi* of the body naturally revolves."*

*The True Principles of the Celestial Immortals* say:
*"The most wondrous truth lies in
one breath permeating the true *qi*,
without losing its dual threads.
One spirit governs the two *qi*s,
yet never straying from other perceptions.
A warning, a warning."*

And again:
*"The single breath—
the *qi* of inhalation and exhalation
permeates and connects the true *qi*,
from beginning to end without separation.
If separated, it becomes intermittent and then reconnects—
this is the dual thread.
It arises from a spirit-clouded and scattered mind.
In extreme cases, three or more threads—
all are fires that fail to perfect.
Beware, beware."*

*The True Principles of the Celestial Immortals* say:
*"The breath’s *qi* must permeate the true *qi*,
commanding a single spirit—
concentrating the mind to govern it without separation.
If one thinks of another matter internally, it departs;
if one fixes on another perception externally, it departs.
Departed, there is no fire, no response.

One breath thus, three hundred breaths thus—
only then can one unite with the natural Dao’s fire and response of profound function."*

*The True Principles of the Celestial Immortals* say:
*"When movement begins, the two fire responses of inhalation and sealing arise—
this is the origin of the small Heavenly Cycle.
When stillness occurs, the small Heavenly Cycle’s response is complete, and the fire ceases."*

*The Mirror of Alchemical Refining* states:
*"When the fire’s response is complete, do not harm the elixir,
for Heaven and Earth are subtle, and transformation is frugal."*

The **Zhengyang Ancestor** said:
*"When the elixir is ripe, one need not practice fire response—
to practice fire further will harm the elixir."*

*The Awakening to Its Essence* states:
*"Before refining the prenatal elixir, refine swiftly;
after completion, one must know when to cease.
If one clings to the mind of unfulfilled excess,
one risks sudden ruin and disgrace."*

**Xiao Liaozhen** said:
*"Beware: one must not practice fire response,
nor must one fail to cease when due—
otherwise, peril will ensue."*

*The True Principles of the Celestial Immortals* say:
*"When fire is complete and the elixir ripe,
there arises the response to cease fire.
When this response comes,
one must be able to remove it from the crucible
and transfer it into another crucible.
The essence transforms into *qi* at the *qi* cavity;
the *qi* transforms into spirit at the spirit chamber—
thus it is called ‘another crucible.’"*

*The True Principles of the Celestial Immortals* say:
*"When the *qi* is complete, one must guard against the danger of fullness and overflow.
The Master once instructed:
‘One must not use fire,
nor must one use it at all.’

If one uses fire without ceasing,
the elixir’s completion gains nothing further—
doubt and negligence
will only risk the overflow of the already full primordial essence.
Yet there is no true overflow,
for it has not yet transcended this realm of potential overflow—
this is the path dividing the ordinary and the sacred."*

**Shi Xinglin** said:
*"One need not practice fire response,
yet must fear harming the infant.
The infant—this is the elixir.
When the fetus is formed, the infant is also formed,
and when it is about to manifest externally,
there is no fire.
If one uses fire again,
it is as if the infant’s unfinished matters
were being damaged—
how could this not harm the infant?"*

**Zhu Yuanyu** said:
*"The essence of fire response lies entirely in one movement, one stillness.
The Heavenly Sovereign, dwelling in the sealed chamber,
is motionless and profoundly tranquil—
washing the heart, retiring the mind.
When movement arises, it responds and thus penetrates,
issuing commands and decrees.
It follows nothing but the rhythm of one yin, one yang,
the one cold and one heat of *zi* and *wu*,
the one life and one death of *mao* and *you*.
The division of yin and yang must not err by a hair’s breadth.
If one harmonizes with its laws,
then internal fire and external talismans
will naturally correspond."*

**Zhu Yuanyu** said:
*"The movement and stillness of fire response
must not be violated like laws and decrees.
The scholar must follow them in practice and experience.
When observing progress and retreat,
the comings and goings at the boundaries of the two extremes and two divisions,
one must be utterly sincere and focused—
the slightest deviation from the norm
will cause the fire’s response to fail like a misfired clepsydra.

Blind phoenixes, monstrous rains, droughts, and floods bring disaster.
The minor: locusts arise instantly,
and the jade furnace with the golden crucible boil over.
The major: mountains and rivers collapse,
and the golden tiger and wooden dragon gallop together.
All arise from the Heart-Sovereign’s laxity,
the spirit chamber’s lack of governance—
thus, misfortunes are invited and transformations called forth."*

**Zhu Yuanyu** said:
*"At the winter solstice, when one yang begins,
the law requires advancing the fire,
yet one must nurture the germ of the hidden dragon—
the fire must not be excessively fierce.
At the summer solstice, when one yin first descends,
the law requires withdrawing the fire,
yet one must guard against the gradual approach of frost—
the fire must not be excessively cold.
If one applies heat when it should not be applied,
then even in the height of winter, it becomes great summer.
If one applies cold when it should not be applied,
then even in the midst of summer, frost and snow descend.
When encountering the spring and autumn equinoxes,
where yin and yang are balanced,
water and fire are equal—
here, one must bathe,
wash the heart and purify the mind,
adjust and harmonize the transformations,
and only then will the true *qi* in the crucible congeal."*

**Zhu Yuanyu** said:
*"The fierce belongs to martial fire,
the gentle to cultural fire.
Before the body and mind are united,
one must use martial fire to forge and temper them—
no hint of gentleness may be involved.
When the spirit and *qi* have been harmonized,
one must use cultural fire to consolidate and complete them—
no hint of fierceness may be involved.
Water and fire now balanced,
stand in the realm of perilous emptiness.
When emptiness reaches its utmost and stillness its depth,
spirit and clarity naturally arise—
this is the ‘one moment when true obscurity and illumination occur.’"*

**Zhu Yuanyu** said:
*"Cultural fire nurtures within the spirit chamber,
martial fire defends at the gateways."*

**Zhu Yuanyu** said:
*"Fire response has cultural and martial aspects.
Martial fire governs refining,
cultural fire governs bathing.
Their applications are distinct in Heavenly Cycle phases.
First, one must engage in open warfare,
finally, one must defend the citadel—
both are times when martial fire is employed.
Know that martial fire’s refining
lies in the convergence of one south and one north.
Cultural fire’s bathing
lies entirely in guarding the central palace,
where thought must not arise and intent must not scatter.
The secret of fire response is found in a fleeting instant."*

**Zhu Yuanyu** said:
*"What is called ‘bathing’?
All ties are utterly severed,
not a thread remains.
Preserve the true intention within the rule,
and harmonize the golden emotions with the wooden nature.
Head and tail balanced,
equally divide *kan* and *li*—
adjust and harmonize the two families,
never straying from the central true earth."*

**Zhu Yuanyu** said:
*"The subtlety of transformation lies entirely in the hours after noon and before midnight.
One must linger with true intention between them,
for which reason the ancient sages called it ‘stopping at noon.’"*

**Zhu Yuanyu** said:
*"The movement of fire and spirit knows no greater marvel than the return of light to its source."*

**Zhu Yuanyu** said:
*"What is the true fire?
Is there another?
It is simply the breath returning to its root,
awaiting the true seed’s self-transformation and self-nurturing—
how could one rely on dross,
a hair’s breadth of aid or artificial contrivance?
How could one expend a moment’s effort?"*

「Lu Zu said in the *Golden Jade Scripture* (*Jin Yu Jing*): *"To clarify the Dao/Way of primordial harmony,
one must first gather the scattered *qi* of the post-heaven body.
If there is any perverse impulse,
the original essence will be lost without recourse."*

Lu Zu said in the *Scripture on Verifying the Dao* (*Zheng Dao Jing*): *"Motion brings continuity,
stillness brings union—
let yin and yang respond to each other,
and the marvel of transformation will arise.
Once *qi* and essence are constrained by emotion,
it becomes falsehood."*

The *Scripture on Verifying the Dao* (*Zheng Dao Jing*) further states:
*"The true marvel revolves within oneself,
pure *qi* emanating from the source.
When the source is pure and still,
it marks the beginning of clarity in principle.
Though the heavenly mandate flows through time,
there remains distinction in passage and blockage,
opening and closing."*

The *True Sayings on Chanting the Dao* (*Chang Dao Zhen Yan*) say:
*"The method of fire and spirit
is nothing more than maintaining inner stillness and observation,
allowing true *qi* to move ceaselessly.
Refining lead and adding mercury
is merely the constant ascent of true water
and the constant descent of true fire."*

The *True Sayings on Chanting the Dao* (*Chang Dao Zhen Yan*) say:
*"The fire and spirit’s movement is achieved through:
the body’s heat like fire,
the heart’s cold like ice.
*Qi* flows like a spring,
the spirit steadies like a mountain.
The spirit overflows—thus it is,
the *qi* sinks—thus it is.
Spirit and *qi* interdependent,
observing inwardly at all times,
returning to contemplation in every moment.
The furnace fire spans the heavens,
gold fills the earth."*

Lu Zu said in the *Scripture on Verifying the Dao* (*Zheng Dao Jing*):
*"Only with sincere resolve, unflagging,
will the subtle marvels of the orifices open to the numinous."*

Sun Budui said:
*"Without the true essence hidden within,
the essence, though present, is as if nonexistent."*

The *Records of the Fusion of Daoist and Buddhist Schools* (*Xian Fo He Zong Yu Lu*) state:
*"Let the fire move of its own accord;
do not contrive any effort toward it,
and you will align with the profound and marvelous Dao/Way of fire.
Most importantly, when entering stillness (*ding*),
focus solely on the function of the gaze.
Thus, by day, use the light of both eyes
to gaze fixedly upon the central field (*zhong tian*).
By night, use the light of both eyes
to guard and preserve without dissipation.
If you adopt this method,
the great medicine will spontaneously arise—
just as the *Yin Fu Scripture* (*Yin Fu Jing*) says,
‘The marvel lies in the eyes.’"*

The *True Sayings on Chanting the Dao* (*Chang Dao Zhen Yan*) say:
*"The ancients’ four characters—‘restrain anger, suppress desire’ (*cheng fen zhi yu*)—
are the essential keys to bathing and refining.
If anger is not restrained,
the fire should descend but instead flares upward.
If desire is not suppressed,
the water should ascend but instead drains downward.
Even if one devotes tenfold effort,
reaching nine parts out of ten,
the elixir furnace will still fail to ascend,
and the true essence will leak away.
Once a miscalculation occurs,
the work will neither complete nor succeed."*

Xiao Zi Xu said:
*"The celestial and terrestrial keys of the *tuchui* [1] have their appointed numbers,
the *li-kan* [2] knife and jade must be gathered at their proper times."*

Chong Xu Zi said:
*"The movement of *qi* has its appointed numbers—
beware of excess.
The movement of *qi* has its appointed times—
beware of duration.
Too long, too much—
lest it exhaust the primal *qi*’s vital impulse,
hence the *zhou-tian* [3] numbers are set as limits.
My master Cao Yuan Yang said:
‘*Wuzi-Weyou-Mao-You* [4] determine the true mechanism—
reverse yin and yang in three hundred breaths.’
The *Yu Ding Zhen Ren* said:
‘If the cauldron lacks the water clock,
the numinous sprout will not grow.
The water clock—
that is the inhaling and exhaling of breath.’
The *Jin Gu Ye Ren* said:
‘Count the *zhou-tian* breaths subtly,
the jade water clock’s cold tones drop by drop in harmony.’
Chen Ni Wan said:
‘Heaven’s twelve *chen* [5] are clearly divided,
on earth they form the alchemical stages.
If one says the water clock lacks foundation,
one will never grasp the mysterious mechanism—
the medicine remains unformed.’

Chen Xi Yi said:
‘Thirty-six and twenty-four—
the *zhou-tian* degrees are similar in number.
*Mao* hour for bathing, *You* hour for unity—
when the fire’s sufficient, rest at will.
The *Gan* [6] strategy has two hundred sixteen,
subtract the thirty-six *Mao* yang bathing—
one hundred eighty remain in use.
The *Kun* [7] strategy has one hundred forty-four,
subtract the twenty-four *You* yin bathing—
one hundred twenty remain in use.
Combined, they yield the three hundred breaths of the *zhou-tian* count.
The surplus numbers lie outside.
Practicing this *zhou-tian*,
accumulating dynamic *qi*,
if not exceeded in a hundred days,
the essence will not leak—
the *qi* will return.

*Mao* and *You* mark the bathing to nourish it.
*Xie huo*, *ting fu*—
this is called bathing.
Today, perform bathing—
do not act upon what should be done,
but act upon what should not be done.
Li Xu An said:
‘Where *yang* first stirs, the fire begins—
*Mao* and *You* sealing the furnace share the same warmth.’
Again he said:
‘Bathing and rebirth divide at *Mao* and *You*.’
Lu Zu said:
‘Advance and retreat must discern the *Mao-You* gate.’

If one does not know the *Mao-You* bathing,
one falls into emptiness and cannot complete the medicine.
For bathing is the true alchemical work—
advancing fire and withdrawing *fu* [8] are merely auxiliary,
serving to adjust and assist the bathing.

There are *Mao-You* of years and months,
and *Mao-You* of day and hour.
Before attaining the elixir,
one must distinguish the central *Mao-You* of the hour,
knowing the six *hou* [9] of each hour—
the critical passage’s subtle mysteries.
Bathing—
when *Mao* month’s wood flourishes and *bing* fire corresponds,
bathing here, *geng* metal receives the embryo,
without advancing *yang* fire to nourish the metal embryo.
When *You* month’s metal flourishes and *ren* water corresponds,
bathing here, *jia* wood receives the embryo,
without withdrawing the *yin fu* to stabilize the wood embryo.
The tenth month’s *fu*—
excluding *Mao* and *You* months—
thus it is called the annual fire regimen.
The *Wu Zhen Jing* says:
‘Annual bathing guards against peril,
ten months of adjustment must be observed with caution.’
But *Mao* and *You* must be taken at the moment the medicine’s fire arrives.

The *Mai Wang* says:
‘When *xing-de* [10] stands at the gate,
*Mao-You* bathing—
the great principle is all about nourishing the elixir.
Yet the bathing at the moment of elixir formation—
the ancient sages kept this secret and did not speak of it.
Only my master’s *Huan Dan Huo Hou Ge* [11] elucidates the subtle mechanisms of fire-advancement,
and I now reveal the alchemical core,
unveiling it here so that all ages of confusion
may be fully resolved.

The *Fire Regimen Song* says:
‘Recall my immortal master’s Dao-methods,
all are from my family’s techniques.
There is no *zi-wu* [12] refining,
how could there be *tu-ji* [13] *xing-de*?
When do you ask of me?
I reply: at the medicine’s birthtime.
When do you ask of me?
It is no more than the medicine’s dawn at the golden gate.
At what time is *Mao*?
The Red Boy’s fire rages in the Vermilion Cloud Cave—
without the *Guanyin* of Mercy’s Relief,
the great medicine will surely shatter.
This is the bathing hour—
past this, the Yellow River’s vessels are useless.
Again, what is *Mao-You*?
It is the convergence of *Ren*, *Du*, and *Gou*.
If the Yellow Robe is absent here,
how can the medicine achieve perfect harmony?
When this occurs, it is the *Ku-Xu* [14]—
ask of the library’s omens.
This is a direct transmission of the heart’s essence—
the supreme Dao requires no further seeking.’

When the medicine stands at the *xuanmen* [15],
the *Dan Jing* speaks of the nine-layered iron drums,
the three-legged golden toad—
the place where *Ren* and *Du* merge below,
the path where parent and child divide in embryo.
This is its meaning,
hence the Red Boy’s *xianghuo* [16] is compared to it.
The *Guanyin* of Mercy’s Relief—
strict stillness brings the sweet dew’s pearls to descend.
I once asked my master:
‘Entering stillness is the *Ku-Xu* matter—
why speak of it now?’
The master said:
‘This stillness is not the great stillness,
but the *Guanyin*’s stillness.
If that stillness, then it is the *Ru Lai*’s stillness.’

The *He Lin Zhen Ren* said:
‘*Mao-You* are its gates of entry and exit.’
Thus, when *xing-de* stands at the gate,
it is only the gate of *xuan*—
the gate of the female.
It lies in recognizing its subtle mysteries.’

Chapter Four: Illuminating Principle, Practicing Stillness

The Master Upper Yang said:
*"The cultivator must first penetrate the true essence of the twofold yin-yang actions within and without. Only then, upon entering the chamber and applying the work, will success be easy.*

*Inner elixir is what one possesses inherently; outer elixir is what the body produces. Inner elixir never leaves one’s own body, while outer elixir never departs the form and appearance. Inner elixir is solely the matter of *xing-de* [性]; outer elixir is entirely the matter of *ming* [命]. Inner elixir is *jing* [精], outer elixir is *qi* [氣]. Since *jing* and *qi* are inseparable, it is called true seed. The Dao/Way of inner and outer elixirs—both rely on the same principle.*

Xue Zi Xian said:
*The *Po Mi Ge* [破迷歌] states,
‘When the Dao/Way comes from within, the furnace is set up, and the tripod is established—yet this is done externally. When the Dao/Way comes from without, the *kan-li* [坎離] lead and mercury are internal.’ This clarifies the distinction between inner and outer elixirs. Outer elixir is the golden elixir. In the *er-ba* [二八] furnace, the transformation is complete in less than half a day, and success is immediately obtained. Inner elixir is the golden liquid elixir. The transformation occurs within one’s own body, requiring ten full months before the embryo can be cast off and sainthood achieved. Though their actions are somewhat similar, the methods and fire stages differ greatly.’

*When we apply the work, at the moment of merging the outer elixir with the elixir essence—when the dragon and tiger battle—gold and wood attract each other, and not the slightest deviation can be allowed. A slight error, and the great elixir will not be achieved. When merging the inner elixir with the elixir essence, one must most guard against danger and risk. Though inner elixir possesses the natural true fire within the earthen vessel, even the blazing vermilion flame must depend on the external furnace for diligent regulation, adding or subtracting, and skillful manipulation to ensure no deviation—until the point of peril.*

*Yet, the true fires of inner and outer elixirs are boundless in their transformations, truly relying on the marvelous essence of true lead. This substance uniquely restrains mercury, preventing it from fleeing. Over time, when lead is exhausted and mercury is dry, then there is no fire nor gold."*

Jing Chan Zi said:
*"Generally, one must begin with outer elixir before progressing to inner elixir. Inner elixir is the realm of non-action yet encompassing all actions. Outer elixir is the realm of action yet relying on external means. Inner elixir is formless and without substance yet truly existent; outer elixir has body and function yet is truly nonexistent. Outer elixir pertains to the physical body; inner elixir pertains to the *fa shen* [法身]. Outer elixir is the Dao/Way of the earthly immortal; inner elixir is the Dao/Way of the heavenly immortal. Outer elixir perfects *ming* [命], inner elixir perfects *xing-de* [性]. For the Dao/Way belongs to yin-yang, hence the elixir has inner and outer distinctions."*

Tao Su Zhi said:
*"Though the source of the elixir belongs to the *kun* [坤] position, *kun* is aged yin, unable to act on its own. *Dui* [兑] is the maiden, belonging to the same class as *kun*, substituting for *kun* in its function. Thus, the west is the primary *dui* position, where gold finds its true place. Those refining the golden elixir need not seek from *gan* [干], nor from *kun* [坤], nor from *kan* [坎]; they may seek solely from *dui* [兑]. Yet though the work is the same, the methods have their order. Only after the critical juncture is opened can one begin to establish the foundation. Once the foundation is complete, one can obtain the elixir. When the inner elixir is condensed, one may return to the elixir. Before establishing the foundation, all elixirs are post-heavenly within pre-heavenly *qi* [氣]. The stage of returning to the elixir is pre-heavenly *qi* [氣] within pre-heavenly *qi* [氣]. Once the *qi* [氣] enters the abode, one becomes as if drunk or mad, entirely dependent on companions and the Yellow Nurse to aid in performing the rituals and manipulating the fire."*

Tao Su Zhi said:
*"*Gui* within *ren* [壬] is post-heavenly within pre-heavenly *qi* [氣], used for establishing the foundation. Lead containing yang is pre-heavenly within pre-heavenly *qi* [氣], used for returning to the elixir."*

*The *Mai Wang* [脉望] states:
‘Harvesting post-heavenly within pre-heavenly *qi* [氣] prolongs life and benefits longevity. First harvesting pre-heavenly within pre-heavenly *qi* [氣] allows one to become a buddha or immortal.’*

Zhang San Feng said:
*"Harvesting post-heavenly *qi* [氣] establishes the foundation and refines oneself. Stealing pre-heavenly *qi* [氣] achieves sainthood and immortality. Reversing the path to immortality is the dragon devouring tiger marrow. Following the path of life is the tiger seizing dragon’s spittle."*

Tao Su Zhi said:
*"Pre-heavenly gold and water are taken as the elixir mother, used for returning to the elixir. Post-heavenly gold and water serve as the furnace elixir, used for refining oneself and nurturing the elixir."*

Tao Su Zhi said:
*"The elixir is formed from harmonized *qi* [氣]. Within, one breathes, and the spirit follows the breath to condense; the breath lingers with the spirit to settle. At the moment of refining, one harmonizes the breathing, collects the external true *yi* [一] *qi* [氣], and brings it into the *wu-ji* [戊己] palace. There, it nurtures with the accumulated yin essence over time, until the true breath settles and the pulse ceases, and the elixir forms.*

*When the minor yin of humanity receives the embryo, its pulse stops—the sign of earth filling and water not rising. The elixir adept drives the dragon to the tiger, seizes its balance, adjusts its victory and defeat, and ferments it intensely until the fire steams and the water boils, causing the gold to rise with the water. When the water boils to its utmost, its vitality enters the *li* [離] palace. The *li* fire is then extinguished by the *kan* water, subdued and restrained, neither flying nor fleeing. Water meets earth and is concealed; fire meets earth and is hidden. Lead and mercury fear death, returning to the profound earth. The three families meet, and the three lineages unite.’*

Tao Su Zhi said:
*"How does water generate gold? When yin and yang first interact, the *Tian Yi* [天一] produces water as the first of the five phases, the pivot of the Dao/Way and the origin of yin-yang. Water—when combined with earth’s five—achieves its full potential. One is the number of *xuan* [玄], five is the number of *huang* [黃]; is this not the symbol of *xuan* and *huang* containing the embryo?*

*‘*Kan* and *li* [坎離] correspond to the sun and moon. Elixir methods have internal sun and moon, and external sun and moon. To allow the internal sun and moon to shine within, one must first make the external sun and moon shine without. Their brilliance spreads and aids in the transformation—this is where it lies.’"*

「The sun and moon traverse the *Huang Dao* [Yellow Path] above, alternately emerging and retreating, cyclically waxing and waning. They coil and uncoil in turn, each following its own order. At the new moon, it darkens; in darkness, it returns to new. At the crescent, it reaches fullness; in fullness, it returns to crescent. Like spokes converging on a hub, the wheel turns without end. This is the interplay of yin and yang—the sun and moon’s divine transformation is thus, and so too should one recognize the sun and moon within one’s own body, though many remain unaware.

Therefore, those who study the Dao/Way understand the subtleties of waxing and waning in the interplay of convergence and divergence, grasp the timing of elixir gathering, and thus exhaust the divine. They know the precise moments of motion and stillness, early and late, in the phases of emergence and retreat, recognizing the signs for directing the *yun huo* [运火, alchemical fire], for this is to know transformation. It lies also in turning inward to seek it.

*"Unity beyond measure is divine; gradual progression is transformation. The divine is the master of yin and yang, while transformation is their successive interplay. Thus, to exhaust the divine and grasp transformation—does it not lie in the arrival of yang, when yin follows?"*

Tao Su Zhi said:
*"The Great Dao of the elixir is supremely simple and easy, with methods for advance and retreat, and techniques for refining and nurturing. All follow the marvels of natural transformation, requiring no forced arrangement. Yet what is called 'natural' is not mere abandonment to nature without effort. The Ancestral Masters say 'follow nature'—not passively submit to it, but understand the profound truths nature reveals.

'Refine oneself for three years, warmly nurture for ten months; in between, obtain the elixir in an instant.' Master Lü said: *'Three thousand days of accumulated effort to complete the Great Work,' and also: *'The Great Work nears completion at three thousand days; no fixed method in twelve hours of wondrous application.'* The *Huang Ting Jing* [Scripture of the Yellow Court] states: *'Accumulate essence and gather qi to form the True One.'* The Dao of eternal life and prolonged vision arises from the gradual accumulation of even the smallest efforts—unceasing practice, which enables the transformation of form and ascension.

The *Pulse Gazing* [脉望] says: *"This meaning arises from stillness pushed to its extreme, where true earth emerges. Divine qi intermingles through true intention, all governed by the True One’s will. If intention is not singular, the divine scatters without condensation. Without condensed divine qi, the Great Work appears before one yet slips away in an instant—thus, one must cultivate in tranquil emptiness to nourish the divine, honor it as a sovereign of ten thousand chariots, align it with the *Cheng Ji* [辰极, Polar Star] to employ its power, and seal the Three Treasures to gather it. When the divine is luminous, qi responds, and only then may one undertake the methods of ingestion and return—so the divine is the master of the elixir, qi its foundation, and the key to all effort."

The *Pulse Gazing* says: *"The ancient True Ones knew the divine originates from within, while qi comes from without, so they must rule qi with the divine to preserve eternal life. In a human body, the primal divine always governs, and only when filling *Kan* [坎, the water phase] and supplementing *Li* [离, the fire phase] does qi begin to restore itself. The four characters 'emotion, faith' [有情、有信] encompass the essence of *The Three Essentials of Harmony* [参同] and *Awakening to the True* [悟真]. Emotion is the movement of stillness; faith is the sign of motion. The single character 'faith' unites all ten thousand sages and True Ones in one technique.

The interplay of essence and qi, returning to nature, binds soul and spirit, dividing action into before and after. Cautiously guiding the affairs of life, reversing the mechanisms of birth and death—acting yet mastering through non-action, creating yet returning to non-creation. The Dao of nurturing life follows the Way; immortals invert and apply it. They overturn heaven and earth, reverse the five phases, stealing the moment just before motion begins. Concealing emotion and scrutinizing in secret, subtly consuming without letting others perceive—turning death into life, hiding benevolence within harm, all hinged on this delicate mechanism. How subtle and wondrous it is!

The *Pulse Gazing* says: *"The elixir’s completion depends solely on mercury, and directing the fire relies only on the *Xuan Dan* [玄牝, Mysterious Feminine, i.e., the alchemical furnace]. Though the numbers may seem complex, the principle is concise. If fire completes its celestial cycle and gold fills the body, sufficient fire means sufficient gold qi—then the seven phases return and the nine phases restore, and the True One’s transformation beyond measure manifests itself."*

The *Principles of the Celestial Immortal* [天仙正理] says: *"The Celestial Immortal is the primal divine nature; without the elixir, one cannot return to the original state of the Way and attain verification. The elixir is true yang and primal qi—without knowing how to gather and refine it, one cannot forge the elixir."*

It further says: *"The Dao of immortality is simple and easy, relying solely on the divine and qi. Thus, one knows that eternal life depends on qi, while divine communication depends on the divine.

'Without knowing the mechanisms of true motion and true stillness, one cannot obtain true qi. Without knowing the sequential application and the techniques of gathering, how can one speak of subduing qi?'

Initially, refining oneself refers to its myriad opposing manifestations—the application of nature in the world and worldly thoughts, inverted and restored. Ultimately, returning to emptiness refers to nature’s formless essence, alone restored to void and stillness—yet it is but one true nature. Common folk do not realize immortality is nature itself, no different from the Buddha’s Way, so though all speak of immortality, none know what to study, and thus none succeed."*

Shang Yang Zi said: *"All things have a time to return to their roots; the accomplished understand the principles of eternal life."*

*The Contract* [契] says: *"Without attaining the principle, one cannot rashly speak of it."*

「Exhausting one’s family wealth, leaving wife and children in hunger and poverty, yet still failing to meet with success—few can achieve it.»

Stone Immortal Elder said: *"The Dao of immortality is easy to learn, yet few can master it. Escaping the dust is not difficult, yet few can truly do so. Alas, how deeply pitiable!"*

*The Embracing Simplicity* [抱朴子] says: *"Though taking elixirs is the foundation of eternal life, if one can also practice qi cultivation, the benefits come swiftly. If one cannot obtain elixirs but instead cultivates qi to its fullest principle, one may still attain several hundred years. Yet one must also know the arts of the inner chamber—for without mastering the techniques of yin and yang, repeated exhaustion will make qi cultivation difficult to strengthen. For humanity resides within qi, and qi resides within humanity; from Heaven and Earth down to all things, none exist without relying on qi to live. The adept in qi cultivation nourishes the body internally and repels evil externally, yet common folk practice it daily without knowing."*

*The Embracing Simplicity* [抱朴子] says: *"To diminish is easy to understand and swift, but to augment is difficult to grasp and slow."*

「How can one recognize the difficult if they do not even awaken to the easy? To diminish is like a lamp’s flame—its wax is unseen as it gradually consumes itself, yet it is suddenly extinguished. To augment is like sowing and nurturing seedlings—no one perceives it, yet they suddenly flourish. Thus, in cultivating the body and nurturing the nature, one must be meticulous in the smallest matters. One must not dismiss minor benefits as unworthy of cultivation nor minor losses as harmless. For all great things are gathered from the small, and vast sums arise from the accumulation of one. If one cherishes things in their nascent stage and completes them in their subtle form, then one is nearly attaining the Dao.»

Master Liu Changsheng said: *"When the dust of the mind is utterly extinguished, one’s true nature is preserved. When the desire for form is utterly extinguished, one’s life-force is preserved. When the delusion of ignorance is exhausted, one safeguards the harmony of the Primordial.*

Master Tao Suzi said: *"Once the Original Chaos aligns, the elixir’s transformation is complete. One must attain a state of leisurely ease, forgetting both human conventions and the Dao’s methods, with not a single thought arising and all entanglements instantly ceasing. The *Classic of Harmony* says: ‘Surrender the will to the Void, and make non-thought the constant.’ The elixir’s method, from beginning to end, relies on non-thought as its constant. Yet those who harbor thoughts are but engaged in fleeting moments—this must be understood."*

Master Shangyangzi said: *"The two characters ‘non-thought’ are most essential. The adept dwells in the abyss, employing non-thought to respond. Floating and guarding within the *Gui* [规], they employ non-thought to await. Inhaling and exhaling, nurturing each other, they employ non-thought to achieve this. When the Three Natures converge, they employ non-thought to enter. Its efficacy is supreme, hence it is called the constant. Marvelous indeed!

The Daoist ‘non-thought’ does not mean extinction but singular focus—only the present thought manifests, with no other stray thoughts arising. The *Heart-Nature Precepts of Ding Lingyang* state: ‘In stillness, suppressing thought deepens the work; all phenomena appear before you, yet one must not let the heart generate attachment or aversion.’ For practitioners, myriad phenomena arise in stillness, all illusions of one’s own consciousness, emerging from stillness to tempt the mind. Only when the mind remains steadfast, unmoving—seeing without seeing, akin to emptiness, untouchable—do they naturally dissipate.

The *Laozi* says: ‘Attain the utmost emptiness, guard steadfast stillness. When all things act in concert, I observe their return.’ Shangyangzi says: From the Primordial Pole to its return, how many Primordial Poles and how many returns are there? To comprehend this is to exhaust the Dao of the Nine Reversions.»

The *Compass of the Gui* says:
*"Originally, before humanity’s birth, there was only the boundless Void. When male and female essences intermingled, their signs first appeared. A single point congealed—pure essence of nature and life. For three months in the womb, the Dark Mother stood firm. Once the Dark Mother was established, it clung like a melon’s stem. The fetus in the womb silently drew the mother’s qi. When the mother inhaled, it inhaled; when the mother exhaled, it exhaled. All movements, internal and external, resonated in harmony. What knowledge, what awareness? What clarity, what understanding? Heaven’s qi was chaotic, Earth’s qi was turbid—yet a single breath remained."*

The *Collection of Harmony* says:
*"External yin-yang movements are external elixirs. Internal *Kan* and *Li* converging are internal elixirs. External methods have deliberate action; internally, they occur naturally. The functions of essence, qi, and spirit are twofold, yet their substance is one. Nurturing with external elixirs: the seminal essence from intercourse must not be wasted. The breath of inhalation and exhalation must be refined with utmost care. As for the spirit of non-thoughtful contemplation, its essence lies in tranquility.

Speaking of internal elixirs: refining essence is refining the Primordial Essence, extracting the Primordial Yang from *Kan*. When the Primordial Essence is solidified, the seminal essence from intercourse will not leak. Refining qi is refining the Primordial Qi, supplementing the Primordial Yin in *Li*. When the Primordial Qi is steadied, the breath of inhalation and exhalation will not ebb and flow. Refining spirit is refining the Primordial Spirit, uniting *Kan* and *Li* to form the *Gan*. When the Primordial Spirit is congealed, the spirit of contemplation will naturally attain serenity."*

The *Essentials of Nature and Life* says:
*"When emotion aligns with nature, it is called the union of Metal and Wood. When essence merges with spirit, it is called the union of Water and Fire. When the mind is greatly steadied, it is called the completion of the Five Phases.
The Primordial Essence solidified, then the seminal essence from intercourse will not leak. The Primordial Qi steadied, then the breath of inhalation and exhalation will not ebb and flow. The Primordial Spirit congealed, then the spirit of contemplation will naturally attain serenity."*

Master Zhu Yuanyu said:
*"What is nature? A luminous expanse, round as the Void, the very origin of the Primordial One. What is life? A diffused qi, governing all transformations, the very foundation of the Primordial Two. Nature is without coming or going, while life requires cultivation and verification. Life in humanity, being a product of post-heaven transformation, inherently carries emotions and consciousness. Because the original true nature is entangled with the beginningless roots of karma—both arising and non-arising—these coalesce into the Eight Consciousnesses. The subtlest of these is perception, and perception’s wandering is emotion. Emotion begets obscured wisdom, perception alters its form, inverting true nature and leading one astray into the cycle of rebirth.

The *Chant of the Dao’s True Words* says:
‘Within the Great Void, those who obtain its qi form shape, those who obtain its principle form nature. The Great Void acts without doing, yet all things proceed naturally. The Great Void is without thought, yet all things flourish spontaneously.
Cultivate stillness to nourish the heart, clarity to perceive nature, wisdom to observe the spirit, steadiness to prolong the qi, few desires to generate essence, emptiness to establish intent—these are the essential keys.’"*

Master Lü Dongbin’s *Scripture of Verifying the Dao* says:
*"To know the origin of Primordial Beginning, the dynamics of the Primordial Pole, and the ebb and flow of yin and yang—comprehending these three establishes the root, preserves the true principle, and reveals the source of nature.
The Dao-heart is the heart of Heaven and Earth—neither heart nor non-heart, vast and hollow, containing all principles yet allowing no attachment to any thing. It is the singular essence of the Five Phases’ refinement."*

「"The *Song of the Dao’s True Words* states:
*"Alluring beauty and seductive sounds—both ultimately return to my true nature.
Things are not separate from me, nor am I separate from things.
When subject and object are undivided, the spirit remains without departure or stay."*

The *Key Essentials of Nature and Life* says:
*"All things in the world share one spirit; the spirit is supremely empty, the Dao supremely formless—thus the transformations of the *I Ching* arise within it.
Heaven dwells above, Earth below; humans and things reside between, self-blending and self-transforming—thus the *qi* manifests within them.
Standing between Heaven and Earth to establish life, rooted in the original emptiness and responsiveness to form the nature—when nature and life are established, the spirit is within them.
Life depends on *qi*, nature on spirit; to conceal the spirit within the heart, to conceal the *qi* within the body—thus the Dao is within them.
Only when spirit and *qi* unite does nature and life reveal itself; only when nature and life unite do the primordial nature before nature and the primordial life before life manifest.
The primordial nature before nature and the primordial life before life are my true nature and life, the true nature and life of Heaven and Earth, the true nature and life of the void.

*"Nature is the Primordial Beginning’s true suchness—one luminous soul, thus it is.
Life is the preheavenly essence—one *qi* swirling and unfathomable, thus it is.
Nature without life cannot stand, life without nature cannot exist.
In Heaven, it is life; in humans, it is nature—yet they share one source.

*"The boundless expanse of the Potalaka nature’s original face is vast without limit, divine and unfathomable.
This source is complete and great, neither partial nor biased.
This source is pure and supremely good, unadulterated and singular.
Originally luminous and clear, it penetrates all without obstruction.
If one says it has form, one neither sees nor hears it—what form could there be?
If one says it lacks form, it is the most responsive and divine, yet never truly lacks.
This source has no fixed location, no beginning or end—before Heaven and Earth and all things existed, this source was already such.
After Heaven and Earth and all things came into being, this source remains just as it was.
Supreme lack and supreme presence, supreme presence and supreme lack—this is the essence of the *Kan* and *Kun*, the mysterious pivot of Primordial Transformation, the fundamental source of all humans’ nature and life, the great root of all things and events under Heaven.
The *I Ching*’s *Tai Ji*, Four Symbols, and Eight Trigrams all arise from this.
The Great Shun spoke of ‘standing in the middle,’ Confucius spoke of ‘—’ (the uncarved block), and the emperors and sages passed it down in succession.
To grasp this is to attain the virtue of *Ke Ming* and *Jun De*, to know this is to know the *I Ching*, to see this is to see the Dao.

*"Human luminosity and clarity—whether within the six senses or beyond them—is originally without bounds, without obscurity. What prevents it is only the obstruction of form.
The study of nature and life is both one and two.
If one can perceive the true and authentic essence of nature, one can establish the true and authentic root of life.
When purity reaches its full ten months, the yang spirit pierces the crown—though this is called ‘completing the life’s work,’ it is truly fulfilling the affairs of my nature’s share."*

The *Song of the Dao’s True Words* says:
*"The Dao is singular, unchanging and eternally constant.
After the *Tai Ji* has divided, the beginning and end are still this moment.
The beginning and end are still this thing.
From one world to ten million worlds, all are this moment, this thing—never varying or losing its constancy.
The human heart’s essence is originally unchanging and constant; yet it varies and lacks constancy because of false thoughts and dusty defilements—this is not the heart.
Observing the Dao of Heaven reveals the human heart."*

The *Song of the Dao’s True Words* says:
*"Within supreme lack, all things are complete.
Though it may be called ‘lacking essence,’ in truth it has essence.
Though it may be called ‘lacking *qi*,’ in truth it has *qi*.
Though it may be called ‘lacking spirit,’ in truth it has spirit.
In the age of primordial antiquity, the people’s customs were flourishing and clear—no act was without the radiance of virtue and grace. One cannot grasp it with a single name or symbol, yet rituals, music, punishments, and governance were all brilliantly present."*

Master Shangyangzi said:
*"The worldly take this as mere *I Ching* language, yet fail to grasp the trigrams’ function.
If one grasps the trigrams’ function, one does not know the Dao of the *I Ching*.
To know the Dao of the *I Ching*, the Dao lies within the body, not in the trigrams and *qi*.
Always take ‘luminous awareness and tranquil illumination’ as the heart, ‘void and formless’ as the observation—returning to the source, restoring the origin, and reclaiming the *Tai Ji*."*

Zi Si said:
*"The heart’s spirit is called sagehood—
Thus, when the heart is steadfast, wisdom arises;
when the heart is tranquil, responsiveness arises;
when the heart is still, knowing arises;
when the heart is empty, responsiveness arises;
when the heart is sincere, clarity arises;
when the heart is void, awareness arises."*

The *Lengyan Jing* says:
*"Knowing and seeing are the root of ignorance.
When knowing and seeing lack attachment, then the true, unexhausted, and pure enlightenment of *nirvana* is attained—
How could this be compared to the lack of knowing and seeing in wood and stone?"*

The *Dingguan Jing* says:
*"Only extinguish the restless mind, not the mind of illumination.
‘The sage empties the mind yet fills illumination—
all day knowing, yet never truly knowing.’"*

Huzhe said:
*"The heart ever tranquil is the essence of its own nature.
The heart ever knowing is the function of its own nature."*

Master Ma Dan阳 said:
*"The lack of heart is not like the lack in cats and dogs—they are dull and without heart. What is meant is to preserve the domain of a heart free from defilement, without false thoughts.
Thus, the vulgar have no heart of purity and coldness, the Daoists have no heart of dust and filth—not that both lack heart entirely, like wood and stone."*

Master Bai Ziqing said:
*"Nurture me in the void, fulfill me in the formless—
this is to return to the original root of nature, before birth.
Conceal the heart within the heart yet not reveal it, conceal the spirit within the spirit yet not display it—
thus one attains perfect harmony in the three realms, serene stillness in all ten thousand bonds,
purity in the six senses, and luminous clarity in the mind."*

Not clinging to emptiness, nor clinging to nothingness—
emptying all that is emptied, voiding all that is voided,
until emptiness has nothing to empty, nothingness has nothing to void—
then naked purity, stark and bare,
one’s essence stands alone, luminous and self-sufficient.

Master Ma Dan阳’s lineage said:
*"Those who embody emptiness—
their heart-body quells all thought,
severs even the faintest musing,
within knowing nothing, without sensing no *qi*,
its swiftness is like a galloping steed—
only stillness can master it.
First, purge external attachments:
in crowds, be as secluded as in deep mountain valleys—
that is the Daoist’s way.
Without reaching the field of no-mind,
control becomes impossible.

‘Cultivate purity and simplicity to nourish the Dao.
Endure filth and humiliation to cultivate virtue.
Banish wrath and ignorance to nurture true nature.
Moderate food and tastes to preserve *qi*.
Yet when one’s nature is steadfast, emotions fade;
when the form is voided, *qi* flows naturally;
when the heart dies, the spirit awakens;
when yang flourishes, yin wanes—
these are the laws of nature itself.’

‘Too much attachment to worldly affairs,
too little to mist and clouds.
Those newly entering the Way—
from this day onward, sever all ties to the mundane,
fix your heart and resolve in singularity,
remaining steadfast from beginning to end—
do not abandon it midway.
If even a hair’s breadth remains unchecked,
the Dao will not be secure.

Past deeds are not to be dwelled upon,
future deeds not to be anticipated—
merely abide in the present moment,
and you are a person of no affairs.

In outward conduct, avoid condemning others’ faults,
boasting of your own virtue,
envying the worthy,
or harboring ignorant worldly desires—
all these are seeds of defilement.
In inward practice, cultivate true refinement,
untainted and unattached,
harmonizing *qi* and nurturing spirit,
wandering freely yet unseen,
accumulating merit in obscurity,
hoping only for Heaven’s witness.

As the *Shi* says:
*The Daoist’s heart is distant from worldly passions,
effortless, the foundation of wondrous virtue.
Free from worldly attachments,
suffering and delusion do not cling.*

‘Alcohol is the elixir of ruin,
meat the instrument of life’s end—
best to abstain entirely.
Even alcohol and meat, if consumed, may be overlooked,
but to indulge in lust is a crime beyond pardon.
For lust’s harm surpasses that of wolves and tigers—
it ruins noble conduct, undermines good deeds,
dissipates essence and spirit,
and may even destroy the body—
thus it is the Daoist’s greatest sin.’

Wealth, desire, reputation, ego,
right and wrong, self and others,
grief, sorrow, thought, and deliberation,
clinging to attachments and affection—
when these arise in the mind,
sweep them away instantly.
Through the twelve hours of the day,
constantly examine your past actions.
At the slightest disturbance,
correct yourself immediately.

Within the twelve hours, Heaven’s Dao moves,
governing transformation—
does it ever rest?
Those refining the Way must emulate Heaven’s rhythm,
never pausing in the twelve hours,
turning within to cultivate their own transformation,
ever pure, ever still,
without a trace of dust or thought—
this is true practice."

The Barefoot Liu Zhenren said:
*"The disciplined practitioner must govern their body as a strict warden,
never daring to let it roam freely—
the slightest indulgence will break free of shackles,
wandering the mountains and forests beyond control."
Master Ma Danyang said:
*'Even a moment’s freedom lets the elixir leak,
a hint of ease withers the jade-like nature.'*

When first setting resolve,
guard the essence as you would a spring sprout—
sit when you must sit,
cherishing it as tender as a bubble on water,
easily lost if not carefully tended.
All worldly matters—
arts, preferences, honor, decay, gain, loss—
cast them all aside.
Be as foolish, as mad,
as a withered tree or stone.
Treat your own body as a quadruped’s—
only by placing yourself beneath all things can you rise.
Hide your own luminosity deeply,
never revealing it.
If you scatter even a thread of it in worldly affairs,
you lose it entirely.

The practitioner must learn to be foolish and mad,
never opening the eyes of worldly desire,
never doing what brings joy to the heart,
never acting on doubt,
never forcing what feels unnatural.
You must forget both emotion and awareness,
gradually returning to the Dao.
Awareness is the seed of birth and death—
in daily practice, even a thread of merit must be seized.
At the slightest fault, correct it immediately,
slowly exchanging sin for blessing."

He also said:
*"Not one sage in the Nine Heavens lacks fortune,
not one living being on earth lacks sin."*

Master Qiu Changchun Zhenren said:
*"To seek the True and follow the Dao,
one must rely on accumulated merit and effort.
Without resolute will and sincere devotion,
one cannot transcend the mundane and attain sainthood.
Some expend great effort in the teachings,
yet stir up dust and toil;
others focus solely on inner cultivation,
abandoning all worldly affairs—
but if one restrains themselves and acts with sincerity toward the Dao,
this is the foundation of attaining fortune.

Yet the Dao encompasses Heaven and Earth—
its vastness is beyond speech.
Small virtues and minor deeds rarely show immediate effect,
hence it is said:
Instant enlightenment requires eons of refining demons;
sudden awakening demands countless lifetimes of perfect practice.
Today’s enlightenment is the fruit of past merit.
People do not see the causes of past lives,
only the prolonged struggle of this one—
when success is not yet visible,
they deem their efforts futile and lose resolve,
which is deeply regrettable.

Unknown to them,
sitting, lying, standing, or walking—
if the heart abides in the Dao,
even before enlightenment,
every moment accumulates merit.
When the merit is insufficient,
the Dao does not enter.

It is like a person possessing a priceless jewel worth a hundred thousand,
yet lacking the money to buy it.
They must labor night and day,
saving and economizing,
accumulating wealth—
whether three thousand, five thousand, thirty thousand, or fifty thousand—
until the sum is enough.
Though the jewel remains unobtained,
the money they’ve saved can be used in emergencies,
far surpassing the poverty of those who have none.
So too with those who accumulate merit and virtue."*

Though the Dao is not yet attained,
its roots of virtue are profound and weighty,
across this life and the next,
guided by the sages and worthies.
Compared to those without latent roots,
is it not far beyond?

*"Within the twelve times,
if one only internally examines past transgressions,
then the mind’s qi attains true peace.
When qi is at peace,
this is true virtue.
Not seeing others’ faults,
this is true conduct.
Xu Zu said:
*'Hidden actions and hidden virtues bring all spirits to rest.'*

The venerable Master Hao Taigu declared:
*"In daily life—
refining qi in stillness,
refining spirit in tumult—
walking, standing, sitting, or lying,
all are the Dao.
Day and night, it manifests before you;
do not let your awareness falter.
If you sleep for one moment,
you die for one moment.
Each day has its merit;
do not sleep for a thousand days,
for then your labor will be complete.
Do not believe others’ claims of innate merit—
'夙骨'.
'凡人成则忻忻，败则戚戚。
If one regards these two states—
success with joy, failure with sorrow—
as equal,
then they are truly a person of enlightened mind.'*

Master Qi Yun said:
*"Three thousand virtues are easily attained,
but eight hundred conducts are hard to fulfill.
Calming the heart and steadfastness of will are true virtue,
enduring hardship for others is true conduct."*

From the *Xishan Zhi* annotations:
*"With purity as foundation,
non-doing as the nature of qi,
upholding sincerity as practice,
gentleness as preservation,
unyielding perseverance as conduct,
diligence as the heart,
resolute determination as aspiration,
and boundless expanse as principle,
one views heaven and earth, all things—
none lie outside their heart-nature.
One views heaven and earth, all things—
yet none can obstruct their heart-nature.
With my heart’s true purity,
I transform the world’s greed and defilements.
With my heart’s clarity,
I dispel the world’s ignorance.
With my resolve’s unwavering loyalty,
I guide the world’s confusion.
With my effort’s tireless strength,
I elevate my teaching’s endless reach.

I do not covet worldly fortune,
nor do I harbor hidden guilt,
nor cling to material burdens,
nor fear others’ reproach.
In silence, there is natural dominion,
in flourishing and decline, fixed measure—
this is a principle
that cannot be contrived,
cannot be pursued,
cannot be fathomed,
cannot be divided.

The world fails to recognize subtle mysteries,
yet seeks to overpower heaven with delusion,
to compete for life with greed—
none go forth without incurring blame.

*'Do not let the scorching heat exhaust your qi,
nor let the surging waves drown your emotions.
My qi nourishes and flows through all things,
my emotions are concealed in harmony with all life.
How could the innate nature of the Dao
be enslaved by things?
How could the uncarved purity of heart
be enslaved by emotions?
Where the heart reaches,
the qi follows.
Where the form resides,
the emotions are drawn.
If one can place this body in the boundless void,
transform all things into nothingness,
pass through without lingering,
move yet remain steadfast,
interact with all without entanglement—
what need is there for anger?
What need is there for desire?'"*

Zhuangzi said:
*"The Perfect Man moves unseen without obstruction,
walks through fire without heat,
traverses above all things without being harmed.
I ask: how does one attain this?"*

Guan Yinzi replied:
*"This is the preservation of pure qi."*

*The True Speech of Chanting the Dao* states:
*"To refine the elixir, one must first refine the heart.
When the heart is pure, the spirit becomes clear;
when the spirit is clear, the qi congeals;
when the qi congeals, the essence solidifies.
The *Dan Jing* speaks of establishing the foundation, medicinal herbs,
furnace and cauldron, lead and mercury, Dragon and Tiger,
Sun and Moon, Kan and Li—
all these names arise from refining the heart.
As for the methods of combination,
the functions of mutual aid,
the laws of ascent and descent,
the techniques of alchemical cooking—
these are secondary matters.
If the source of the heart is not yet clarified,
and emotions and desires entangle it,
then though the foundation may be established, it will inevitably collapse,
though the medicinal herbs may be gathered, they will be incomplete.
The furnace will crumble, the cauldron will fail,
the Dragon will struggle, the Tiger will roar,
the Sun will be eclipsed, the Moon will wane,
Kan will be empty while Li is false.
Combination will fail to harmonize yin and yang,
mutual aid will fail to reconcile water and fire,
desire to ascend will instead descend—
the Three Corpses will harm you,
the Six Enemies will disturb you.
A single cup of water cannot extinguish a cartload of fire.
Thus, refining the heart is the essential beginning and end of attaining immortality."*

**Volume Five: Refining the Self and Establishing the Foundation**
Shangyangzi said:
*"The Dao of the Golden Elixir requires first refining the self,
so that the spirit is whole and the qi flourishes,
the Seven Emotions remain undisturbed,
the Five Evils do not cause chaos,
the Six Roots are naturally steadfast,
and the essence is difficult to shake—
only then may one engage in the words of the elixir.
The Five Evils are the eye, ear, nose, tongue, body, and mind,
which are Heaven’s Five Evils.
Color, sound, fragrance, flavor, and touch
are the Five Evils of the world.
Love, desire, greed, anger, and delusion
are the Five Internal Evils.
If Heaven’s Five Evils are not guarded within,
then the Five Internal Evils will swarm.
If the Five Evils of the world are not removed from without,
then Heaven’s Five Evils will proliferate like wolves.
Thus, when the eye sees color, love arises and steals the essence.
When the ear hears sound, desire arises and agitates the essence.
When the nose smells fragrance, greed arises and consumes the essence.
When the tongue tastes flavor, anger arises and scatters the essence.
When the body and mind encounter touch, delusion arises and damages the essence.
These five things assail the body day and night—
how much essence can remain?
When the essence departs, the spirit and qi follow,
and the body is lost.
The cultivator treats the body as a kingdom,
and the essence and qi as its people.
When the essence is unshaken, it is said the people are at peace.
When the spirit and qi are abundant, it is said the kingdom is prosperous.
To seek the elixir is like waging war—
only thus can one prevail and obtain the Primordial qi."*

*The True Principles of the Heavenly Immortal* say:
*"Refining the self is rigorous:
To endure what must be endured is refining,
to master what must be mastered is refining,
to forbid what must not be done is refining,
to strive with unwavering resolve to achieve completion is refining,
to sever all attachment while leaving no trace of desire is refining,
to suppress old habits and remain untouched by them is refining.
The ‘self’ refers to the true nature in stillness and the true intent in action—
another name for the Original Spirit.
The ancients said:
‘Before refining the Returning Elixir, first refine the nature;
Before cultivating the Great Medicine, first cultivate the heart.’"*

*The Pulse Mirror* states:
*"Refining the elixir must first involve refining the self,
and refining the self differs from nourishing the self.
Preserving essence and enriching qi is nourishing the self;
confronting phenomena without emotional entanglement is refining the self.
There is a distinction between movement and stillness.
Yet refining the self must begin with nourishing the self—
though the principle of nature is one, the teachings vary in sudden and gradual methods.
The Sixth Patriarch’s *Platform Sutra* says:
‘If one immediately establishes the insight of prajna,
in a single instant, all delusions vanish.
If one recognizes one’s true nature,
one instant of enlightenment reaches the Buddha’s path.’
This is the sudden method.
What is discussed here is the gradual path.
Master Pei Xingzhi said:
‘To keep the spirit within the body from leaving,
do not allow a single thing to linger in the Spiritual Pivot.’
This means dispelling desire and clarifying the heart,
so that only right mindfulness is present—
the inner realm does not emerge, untouched by anything,
the outer realm does not intrude.
Thus, in tranquil stillness, one gradually enters Great Calmness.
The nature of qi and substance, without dependence,
when nothing attaches, the heart becomes as boundless as the Void—
then the true emptiness and reality of the original body naturally manifests.
This is the meaning of tranquil stillness leading to emptiness,
and the Original Spirit as the Sovereign of the Elixir—
yet it is not crude emptiness.
The *Platform Sutra* says:
‘If you do not think of a hundred things,
and constantly sever all thoughts,
this is called bondage by the Dharma,
and is known as extreme views.’
Truly, at the original source where the body receives its breath,
the Mysterious Pass is a single orifice—
within the Six Dusts, without attachment or clinging,
turning the light inward to illuminate—
over time, this becomes thoroughly pure,
and naturally all concerns dissolve,
while the Original Spirit awakens alone."*

*The Awakening to Reality* says:
*"If one wishes to complete the Nine Transformations,
one must first refine the self and steady the heart.
Understand that refining the self is not empty refinement."*
*(Jiyizi said: "True qi permeates and familiarizes one with phenomena.")*

*The True Transmission of the Golden Elixir* states:
*"If asked how to refine the self,
the furnace, cauldron, zither, and sword make no difference."*

Bai Yuxian said:
*"Learning the Dao of the Immortal is not difficult,
but leaving the dust and severing desire is most difficult."*

Yuyang Zhuren said:
*"Following emotions leads to emptiness and ruin,
making the Dao hard to achieve,
the work hard to complete,
and the retribution hard to bear."*

*The Supreme Lord’s Scripture on Protecting Life* says:
*"To see color is to see emptiness,
to see emptiness is to see color.
If one knows emptiness is not empty,
and color is not color,
this is called enlightenment—
only then does one attain the Mysterious Sound."*

*The Supreme Lord’s Five Kitchen Scripture* says:
*"One qi harmonizes with the Great Harmony,
and obtaining One, the Dao is complete.
Harmony is without a single harmony,
and the Mysterious Principle aligns with the Mysterious Realm."*

The Daoist Master said:
*"Do not willfully will,
nor seek to be without thought.
To will yet have no thought—
this is how the Way is upheld."*

*The Zhaoyang Scripture* says:
*"The initial practice lies in quelling emotional ties,
sweeping away all杂念 (zāniàn),
only then may one begin cultivation.
To eliminate杂念 (zāniàn)
is the first step in building the foundation and refining the self."*

*The Chant of the Dao’s True Words* says:
*"Only with the body of a sage
can one perform the deeds of a sage."*

The First Ancestor said:
*"Externally, sever all ties;
internally, let the heart be still.
The heart like a wall—
only then may one advance along the Dao."*

An ancient song says:
*"Before refining the elixir of life, first refine the nature;
before concocting the great medicine, first cultivate the heart."*

*The Heart-Seal Scripture* says:
*"Refine essence to merge with spirit,
refine spirit to merge with qi,
refine qi to merge with the True One.
When the wind returns and blends,
a hundred days’ practice yields miraculous results."*

*The Chant of the Dao’s True Words* says:
*"Guard it with stillness,
unite it with emptiness.
Move it with intent, yet never with intent.
Obtain it in the heart, yet originally without the heart.
When in motion, align with Heaven’s vigor—
this motion is stillness within stillness.
When at rest, align with Earth’s solidity—
this stillness is motion within motion.
The critical point lies at the Mysterious Pass."*

*The Rootless Tree* says:
*"An old tree takes new shoots to graft fresh branches.
Plum to willow, mulberry to pear—
passed down as models for cultivation.
Since ancient times, the method of divine grafting:
even aged mortals have medicine to heal."*

*The Master of Shangyang said:*
*"Abandon color desires, sever affection and love, regard wealth lightly, and be cautious in virtue and conduct—these four are the essentials for self-cultivation. To abandon desire for color and drink is to preserve one’s vital essence and qi, thereby enabling the taming of dragons and subjugation of tigers. Yet it is not enough merely to abandon them; one must also forget them entirely. In the past, the immortal Liu Zhangsheng of longevity dwelled in Luoyang for three years, refining himself. The Master of the Mud Pillars frequented taverns and brothels, exhausting all pleasures—this too was self-refinement. With prolonged practice of self-cultivation, one purges and discards emotional tendencies, naturally forgetting all that is forgettable, until one reaches the state of *forgetting-forgetting* [忘忘].

To sever affection and love means to transcend attachments arising from external stimuli. Clinging to stimuli generates affection, and affection spawns love. If one can forget the stimuli themselves, then the Six Demons [六贼] will not disturb, and the Spirit Sovereign [神君] will reign supreme. Cultivate the mind thus: only then may one pursue this—with half a moment’s effort, entering the realm of vague and boundless obscurity, to seek the primordial *True One’s qi* [先天真一之气]. Otherwise, there is no guarantee of safety."

*The Pulse Gazing* [脉望] says:
*"The essentials of self-cultivation begin with forgetting all attachments; only then will desire for color and drink be extinguished. Next, one must subdue that mind, and affection and love will naturally cease. The third essential is to manage wealth with moderation, so as to attain a state of contentment. The fourth is to diligently practice virtue and conduct, thereby inviting the blessings of the Spirit Sovereign [神明]. When all four are fulfilled, without neglect morning or evening, and after three years of pure mastery, with no attachment to external stimuli, one’s spirit and essence will be whole and secure—only then may one enter the inner chamber and begin the work of extracting the primordial *One Qi* [先天一炁]. 'If delusive thoughts are not eradicated, one will surely deplete the essence and scatter the qi—this is the failure of self-cultivation. Qi is the great medicine; it must be harmonized and tamed before its natural course may be followed. If emotional tendencies are wild and unruly, how can one strike the strings of the zither or tap the bamboo flute? If the timing of the *Fire Sovereign* [火侯] is misjudged, how can one summon the phoenix or call the tortoise? This is when the emotions do not align with nature. Naturally, the Fire Sovereign will be misregulated, and one will act recklessly in the midst of cultivation, inviting only disgrace and humiliation. Students should not neglect to rectify their hearts and sincerity, and proceed with caution in their pursuit!

'My Primordial Spirit [元神], the sovereign of the Dao of the Elixir [丹道]—merely concentrate the spirit and gather the qi, letting the mind rest in dependence upon it. In stillness and quietude, it dwells and moves freely, following its own natural course. When the sovereign and minister unite in virtue, they govern the *Hall of Illumination* [明堂]. The essence returns to its nature, unharmed whether great or small.'"

Shangyangzi said:

"The noble person first secures their body before acting, adjusts their mind before speaking, and establishes their resolve before seeking. The Sage’s foresight into calamity is profound; refining the three movements—*one thought, one word, one action*—is the Sage’s ultimate principle, the true essence of self-cultivation.

To treasure the essence and enrich the qi is to nurture oneself. To forget the self in response to circumstances is to refine oneself. To remain ever-responsive yet ever-still is to refine oneself. To accumulate virtue and achieve results is to refine oneself.

The practitioner of the Elixir Dao must first refine themselves: restraining anger and suppressing desire, enduring hardship and bearing insults, so that when they enter the inner chamber, the six senses are tranquil and steady.

Only then may they achieve purity and forgetfulness of all that can be forgotten, and thus engage in their work.

Common folk do not grasp that self-refinement is paramount, yet they seek to rush through fleeting moments of practice, hoping for swift results—rarely do they avoid ruin.

Shangyangzi said:

‘The Thus-Come One [如来] asks: *"Why does the World-Honored One say this is a difficult matter? It is indeed the most difficult."*

For even a slight lapse in vigilance—if any of the seven emotions or six demons [六贼] are unchecked—the most refined and precious treasure will be lost. How could one dare to be reckless?

At the outset of practice, first expel the Three Corpses [三尸] and Six Demons, refining the mind until it is as boundless as the void, the six senses utterly purified, before entering the chamber to forge the Great Elixir.

The Dao of Returning the Elixir is easy to cultivate, but self-refinement is the most difficult.

The Sage fears that later practitioners may neglect self-refinement, rushing to the furnace at the critical hour, only to gain not even a grain of the supreme treasure, instead falling into peril. Practitioners must first thoroughly investigate the work of self-refinement.

*"Let desire fade to ash while resolve burns bright; let effort be diligent while the external world is forgotten."*

Bai Yuxian’s *Commentary on the Zhi Xuan Chapter* states:
*"When refining the elixir, never forget a single thought. The Dao-heart must be as unyielding as iron, never to be dragged by mundane circumstances or obscured by carnal desire."*

Lu Ziyou said:
*"If one harbors fleeting ambition, the intensity of the moment may make them forget the toil of former days, abandoning the great matter of a lifetime."*

The Chongyang Ancestor said:
*"Only when the body is still and the mind at ease may one perceive the marvelous."*

The Chongyang Ancestor said:
*"Arrange the furnace, tripod, and fire hearth with urgency—
Pure yang-qi will naturally rise on its own.
When the earthly orifice is sealed and the skeletal frame still,
The celestial pass gradually opens of its own accord."*

Master Shao said:
*"The moon shines within my embrace like a dream of willows,
A breeze from the poplars stirs my face as if alive.
Again he said:
When the moon reaches the heart of heaven,
And the wind sweeps across the water’s surface—
Such purity of meaning,
Few indeed would recognize."*

The *Essentials of the Golden Elixir* states:
*"When a single thought is centered, all external ties are released.
The four gates are sealed externally, while the two eyes perceive internally."*

The *Pulse Observations* states:
*"Nurture nature and preserve the spirit, establishing roots through the Mysterious Female.
Cherish essence and enrich qi, fortifying the foundation of the realm through medicinal aids.
To build the foundation, one must advance qi—
Refining oneself through elixirs, then alchemizing mercury into sand,
Thus the land prospers and the people are at peace, while body and mind remain undisturbed.
The essence of self-refinement lies in mastering emotions.
Within the outer realm, there is one rigid and one yielding.
After three years without interruption,
Bone and qi become refined gold-essence,
Flesh and skin transform into jade-like quality.
Only then, when the inner elixir is solidified,
May one harmonize with Heaven and Earth,
Obtaining the golden emotion to perform the Great Elixir’s work—
As in *Awakening to the True*: ‘Only when the people are at peace and the nation prosperous does one seek battle.’"*

*"Entering the chamber to build the foundation—
This is the great cause and condition for us.
Honor the Master of the Chamber as a sovereign of ten thousand chariots,
Comparing the elixir chamber to the nine palaces,
And the fire talisman as decrees—
The utmost care and secrecy.
Though entering the chamber to gather elixirs forbids idle speech,
Yet this sensation responds to its counterpart—
How else might one obtain the true essence of the great elixir,
Save through skillful utterance?"*

**"Why must one first refine oneself thoroughly before gathering the elixir?
For when the mind stirs, the spirit fails to enter the *qi*;
when the body moves, the *qi* does not return to the spirit.
Thus, Master Qiu said: ‘When cultivating the heart’s foundation,
one must cast aside all worldly affairs entirely—
only then may spirit and *qi* unite as one.’

‘The dragon’s roar and tiger’s howl—
when the *yarrow* stalks shift,
the elixir’s essence harmonizes.
This sound has long existed;
it is not born only when the elixir is perfected.
Hence, *Awakening to the True* says:
*“The moon but half-rises in the sky,
yet dragon’s roar and tiger’s howl resound early.”
The marvel lies in that single *“early.”*’

Master Shangyang said:
‘The method of building the foundation
begins with preparing the altar and its boundaries,
then gathering the elixir materials.
Once the elixir is obtained,
entry and exit must flow freely,
and the work of refining oneself proceeds.
Soft warmth spreads gently,
subtle heat penetrates directly—
this marks the first stage of the initial pass.

Encircling the elixir furnace,
laying out the pathways by intention,
opening the gates and roads,
neither reckless nor wild,
blending colors and harmonizing light,
the lower the better, the deeper the descent,
as daylight gradually lengthens—
this marks the second stage of the middle pass.

At the winged days of the *Xian* cycle,
softness ascends while hardness descends;
the two *qi* respond and interact,
stopping and yielding,
the male descending to the female—
thus, *li* is nurtured and *zhen* stands firm.
The golden *qi* moves from small to great,
