as yin and yang intertwine—
this marks the third stage of the lower pass.

“The Three Corpses are all transformations of *qi* and substance.
Those who refine themselves can only submerge and suppress them;
to exterminate them utterly, the elixir alone suffices.
For when one is purely true in nature,
they vanish entirely.”’"

「Peng He-lin said: *"One may not speak of refining the elixir before attaining immortality—
first, one must cultivate the physical frame to prolong life.
How much more so when there is a portion of ascending transformation,
a faint, soaring crane ascending to the clouds of heaven!

Those who study the Dao/Way,
first adhere to the nurturing actions of Post-Heaven,
advancing *qi*, gathering medicines—
the frame is fortified, life extended,
and the True Essence (*zhen*) responds swiftly,
as if a staff were planted and its shadow seen,
or a voice called forth and an echo returned.

Only then does one gather the Great Elixir of Pre-Heaven,
which is readily attainable by drawing from the body itself,
awaiting the moment when the vessel is ready."*

The *Pulse Prognostication* (*Maivang*) says: *"At the outset of entering the chamber,
there are still matters of deliberate action.
The *Classic of Contracts* (*Qie*) states: 'Open with joy, expand with ease, distribute treasures without stint.'
'Open with joy' means delight;
'expand with ease' means fulfillment;
'distribute treasures without stint' means generosity without hesitation.
Follow their inclinations,
and only then will the emotions converge with nature.
Yet the most crucial of all,
lies in the grasp of the *Dou Kui*—
the *Classic of Contracts* speaks of 'holding the pivot of the Dao/Way.'

When the *Dou* points, the *qi* moves;
advancing fire and retreating talismans must align with the *Dou*’s established *zi-wu* (子午),
corresponding to the *gan-yun* (干运) of one’s body—
the interplay of yin and yang,
commanding the myriad transformations within the body.
Like the net’s central rope or the garment’s fastening knot,
the *crawfish* (*yaoxiang*) shifts internally—
seize the moment,
for then fortune or misfortune, regret or remorse,
arise in the slightest breath.
Revere it, be cautious with it."*

White Jade Chan (*Baiyu Chan*) in *The White Day Inscription* (*Bairi Ming*) says: *"Alas!"」

The body is like a rootless tree,
relying solely on breath as its root and trunk.
A hundred years of time,
like a dream—fleeting and illusory.
One exhalation does not guarantee the next inhalation,
today does not guarantee tomorrow.

Wasting the years in vain,
suddenly one meets old death.
The hundred limbs decay and scatter,
the four *dharma* elements separate,
the *shen* chamber and wandering soul are lost,
drifting into the *shu* realms,
unaware in what future life one will take form again.
The wheel of birth and death revolves,
endlessly through *kalpa* after *kalpa*.
Lost in delusion, one fails to awaken;
lazy in practice, one fails to exert effort.
Now that one has arrived at this treasure mountain,
do not depart empty-handed.
To age still burdened by past illness and die in vain,
what a waste of a human life!

Each should strive with utmost resolve,
laboring with life’s last energy.
The ancients said:
*"Toil for two or three years,
and joy will last a thousand *kalpa*."*

From this day onward, gather oneself,
with singular purpose, no other thought.
Eyes gaze inward, ears listen inward,
moderate food and drink, curtail sleep,
forsake idle chatter, still the mind’s wanderings.
Build a thatch roof over one’s head,
do not seek comfort.
Boil rice to ease hunger,
do not discriminate between fine and coarse.
Like a cicada sipping dew,
the body grows light and pure.
Like a tortoise basking in the sun,
life extends its length.

If one can dine on pine and feast on cypress,
wear a straw hat and cloak of reeds,
sleep beneath clouds in rocky caves,
drink clear water before hollow grottos,
then still it is your own kin.
If not yet strong enough,
simply emulate the ancient sages.
If this is not also a path of cultivation,
then such fortune is not yours to claim.

Morning gather, evening harvest,
daily refine and hourly cook.
Like a dragon nurturing pearls,
like a hen brooding eggs.
Pass the flame unbroken,
fuse into one whole.
And when the child and parent reunite—
is not such meeting a joy?"

「The *Baopuzi* says: *"Life is precious, yet death is to be feared. Cultivating longevity and nurturing the nature—there is none who does not begin with diligence and end with prolonged practice. After the Dao is attained, there is little to do. Before its attainment, there is nothing one does not do. Great medicines at first require much money; they cannot be hastily prepared. On the day of preparation, one must fast and keep the body pure and clean, severing all worldly affairs. Focus the mind, preserve unity, repel evil, and safeguard the body. Only then can success be certain—like a sovereign governing his realm or a general waging war."*

The *Baopuzi* says: *"Conserve the prenatal essence to solidify the spirit, safeguarding the primal *qi*. At times of life-giving *qi*, draw it in through the nose. Common folk swallow *qi* with audible noise in the throat—this is not the prenatal essence or primal *qi*, but rather the intake of coarse *qi*. Coarse *qi* lingers in the belly, not harmonizing with the primal *qi*; it is the breath of panting and gasping. Primal *qi*, though slight, is hard to dissipate and cannot be compared to coarse *qi*. Even breathing should not be heard by oneself, let alone swallowed with noise! If one’s *qi* is coarse, it harms the lungs—the lungs are the five viscera’s canopy, and descending *qi* first reaches them. Those who cultivate primal *qi* must not let it ebb and flow with coarse *qi*; then there will be no time of breath-bound life and death. Forcing coarse *qi* inward and mixing it with the primal *qi* viscera only brings harm. When people exert themselves, they use the common *qi*—the *qi* of myriad things, the essence of food and drink. Common *qi* can only lift weights, move bodies, and transport them; preserving it does not prolong life, and losing it does not shorten it. Why constrain it? Moreover, the practice of *qi* cultivation uses primal *qi*, which can shift mountains, split rivers, tame tigers and leopards, and bind thieves and robbers. Thus, common *qi* is inferior to primal *qi*, coarse *qi* can be discarded, but primal *qi* must not be allowed to escape. If one fills with primal *qi*, coarse *qi* will naturally vanish, and true *qi* will permeate, allowing one to abstain from grains. Even if one eats nine meals a day, it will not cause harm; even if one eats nothing for a year, it will not lead to exhaustion. Then one knows the Dao of *qi* is profound."*

The *Baopuzi* says: *"When people practice guiding and drawing, their joints make noise—large movements produce loud sounds, small ones soft. This is due to slackened sinews and unobstructed *qi*. Guiding and drawing can treat latent ailments and harmonize stagnant *qi*; movement makes the hundred passages flow freely, while stillness causes the three palaces’ blood to congeal. This is indeed the great principle of nurturing life and the mysterious technique for dispelling illness."*

The *Baopuzi* says: *"Cultivating *qi* must be done at times of life-giving *qi*, not at times of death-bound *qi*."*

The *Baopuzi* says: *"In the essentials of *qi* cultivation, one must avoid excessive consumption of sour, salty, or rich, fresh foods. Nowadays, *qi* is strong yet difficult to contain. One must also restrain anger—excessive rage disturbs the *qi*, preventing its refinement, and causes coughing."*

Master Lü’s *Song of Gathering Gold* says:
*"Reduce the sour and salty,
constantly chew the bland.
The Yellow Crone attends with care—watch her closely."*

The *Tianxian Zhengli* says:
*"Consume pure, sprouted tea and bland rice,
regulating the palate and body.
Calm the *qi* and settle the essence—
this is an easy matter."*

The Daoist texts say:
*"To attain longevity, the intestines must be clean.
To avoid death, the intestines must have no residue."*

The Ancestor of Dan Yang says:
*"Lighten the tastes to nourish the *qi*,
banish wrath to cultivate the nature.
If a thought stirs, the *qi* follows the heart and scatters,
the essence flees with the *qi*,
and the spirit wanders—
this is why restraining anger precedes suppressing desire."*

The *Tianxian Zhengli* says:
*"Abstain from sweet flavors and meat,
adhering strictly to vegetarianism,
as the *Fourty-Nine Chapter Scripture* of the Primordial Heavenly Venerable decrees.
Fasting and restraint are the roots of the Dao,
the bridges of the Law.
If you seek the Dao, keep pure fasts and follow the precepts.
Common beings who abandon pure fasts,
indulge in meat and fat,
and violate the Law—
it is like a starving ghost devouring a corpse."*

Zhang Sanfeng’s poem:
*"When *qi* is depleted and blood weakens, seek to replenish and restore.
A true teacher instructs the mouth’s secret method.
The elixir of Hua Pool is swallowed at the right hour,
The nectar of Peach Valley is sipped as it flows.
Banish thoughts, forget reflections—
the innocence of an infant’s heart.
Without sentiment, few desires—
the vigor of a manly spirit.
Warm the *Dantian* to nurture and return to youthful bloom,
Laughing at the stubborn child whose head is now like snow.

'Theory of body and spirit is most refined,
The hands act naturally, both in harmony.
Set the furnace and establish the cauldron to seek the true essence,
Face the world without attachment, recognizing one’s native land.
Pluck the dragon’s head to gather the purple mist,
Unleash the tiger’s tail to release the golden radiance.
A single point of true lead is swallowed into the belly,
All things shine brighter—longevity extended.

'Secure the prenatal essence as the foundation,
Let the true spirit always follow the *qi*.
No dust stains the body—
it remains serene.
All thoughts abandoned—
I alone am aware.
Wicked intruders cannot breach my inner realm,
The Master sits all day before his stern teacher.
When thirst comes, drink the elixir of longevity,
Each day, drunkenly intoxicated, like mud.

'Since piercing the opening of the Hong Meng,
I’ve recognized the furnace of Heaven and Earth’s transformation.
No need for divine techniques to refine water and fire,
The primal *qi* naturally enters flesh and skin.
Each morning, the Yellow Crane hides in its golden cave,
Each night, the Silver Hare enters the jade jar.
To recognize the true elixir’s essence,
One must labor where the body has not yet formed.

'I implored the Yellow Crone to act as a skillful matchmaker,
Creating life from nothing through arduous cultivation.
She taught the fair maiden to wait in due time,
Luring the young lord from beyond.
The two openings communicate without obstruction,
Their union in the middle never divides.
Spring’s boundless embrace—
they seal together in bliss.
A child is born, called the Holy Embryo."*

「The *Dao*’s mysteries are not revealed to the world—hard to know.
Gathering dew from Heaven’s secrets to compose poetry.

Of the same kind, forged into a ghostly body—sword of the *Dao*.
Sharing the same bed, rising to Heaven’s ladder.

Humans must be guided by humans to transcend the mundane,
Dragons must consort with dragons to escape the muddy depths.
Do not scorn the *Dao*’s truths all spoken plainly,
For only the lost souls need such guidance.

*The Song of the Cauldron and Instruments*:
Mirror the heart, silent as empty space,
Only then may one stand before the furnace without flaw.
Without flaw, the furnace may be set,
Refining the cauldron’s *qi*—do not let the heart grow coarse.

*The Eulogy of the Yellow Crane*:
The *Dao*’s craft begins with subtlety,
Appearing perverse yet truly upright.
The fire’s timing takes its first cue,
Seeming strange yet wielded with precision.

Master Ma’s *Song of Returning the Elixir*:
Sever emotions, abandon love to temper the *Dragon* and *Tiger*,
Banish thoughts, forget the *Dao*’s artifices to birth the *Phoenix* and *Lynx*.
*The Upper Realm’s Sacred Domain*:
See the new moon,
And the Jade Field arises—
The primal *qi* of *Great Harmony* surges at the sea’s edge.

*The Song of the Great Dao*:
The furnace’s fire must be carefully tended,
Distinguishing phases—
First gather the *post-heaven* essence, then extend life’s measure.
It also says:
*"Establish the foundation, refine the self, and gather the post-heaven."*

*The Collection of Central Harmony*:
Observe spring’s birth in the cold valley,
Confronting the gentle face of the *Dao*.
Master Xu’s *Drunken Musings on the Immortal Song*:
Morning thoughts on the *Dao*, evening thoughts on transcendence,
Secretly practicing *yin* steps—all deities rest in peace.
Within, exchange the true *qi*, preserving breath,
Naturally, the *Dao*’s transformation restores youth’s bloom.

Master Xu’s *Sutra of the Eight Pillars of the Central Yellow*:
Move yet be still—*qi* congeals with spirit as if in silence.
Still yet move—*qi* embraces essence like empty void.
In the three *wu*’s, abandon all return,
The primal spirit pierces through.
In the nine *you*’s, it returns to ruin,
The true breath sinks into depths.
With spirit exchanged for spirit,
Spirit itself attains enlightenment.
With *qi* overcoming *qi*,
*Qi* emerges from the *Great Void*.
Within the *Great Void*,
Its blessings are vast and unshaken.
Unshaken is the nature of the heart—
When the heart is refined,
Talismans and elixirs become mere crutches, cast aside.

*The Commentary on the Adrift Peak Records*:
Grasp the sun’s essence—*yang* *qi* first arises,
Mysteriously uniting the *Dao*’s spirit in all things.
Grasp the moon’s essence—*yin* *qi* grows primal,
Mysteriously uniting the *Dao*’s essence in all things.
Grasp the Dipper’s essence—*xuan* *qi* spreads transformation,
Sun and moon merge in brilliance,
Mysteriously uniting the *Dao*’s *qi* in all things.

*The Classic of Correspondences* says:
*"Push emotions to align with nature,
Turn and unite with the *Dao*.
At the junction of *jin* and *shui*,
*mu* and *huo* stand as companions.
The four blend in chaos,
Ranked as *Dragon* and *Tiger*."

It also says:
*"Separate *qi* to receive the *ying* and *wei*,
*Kan*’s path needs no cleverness.
*Dui*’s union requires no speech,
Silent words follow *Hong Meng*’s flow.
These three are keys—
In a quiet chamber, ease the body’s strain.
Commit the will to emptiness,
Hold no thoughts as the constant way."*

*The Yellow Court Classic* says:
*"Why not consume the *qi* of *Great Harmony*’s essence,
Thus entering *Yellow Peace* and never dying?
The two spirits unite, forming jade nectar,
Subtle, tasteless—food for Heaven and man.
A hundred and twenty years may yet be restored,
Beyond that, clinging to the *Dao* grows ever harder.
Only await the nine-refined elixir of eight jade gems,
The radiance of sun and moon to heal the aged and broken.

The six palaces must be purified, bright as silk,
Empty and natural—by the *Dao*’s own decree.
Things have their natural course, no need for force,
Resting with hands folded, effortless—body at ease,
Dwelling in emptiness within the curtained chamber.

Abandon lust, guard the essence—
A single inch of field, a foot of dwelling, may nurture life.
Seal the path of essence to prolong vitality.
For longevity, the chamber’s mysteries are most urgent.
The Upper Yang Master said: ‘Though gained within the chamber,
It is not the art of consorting with women.’

Master Lü said:
*"Nurture the essence to root the primal *qi*,
Nurture the *qi* to foster the spirit—
This is the true truth; beyond it, no greater truth exists."*

*The Pulse Gazing* says:
*"At the start of establishing the foundation, separate all false thoughts,
Forget self and world alike.
Focus the *qi* to attain softness,
Return the light to illuminate.
Long practice in stillness,
Like motionless water, no ripples.
When ordinary breath halts,
The true breath moves naturally.
But when one sense arises from the *Gui*’s rule,
Mingling and unbroken,
Rising steadily—
At the peak of stillness, yearning for motion,
The *Mystic Pass*’s aperture appears:
Its vastness knows no outer bound,
Its depth no inner measure,
Entering without accumulation,
Exiting without dispersion—
This is called the true *Holy Embryo* breath."*

*Zhuangzi* says:
*"Let the heart wander in simplicity,
Unite the *qi* with the boundless.
Follow nature effortlessly,
Without contrivance or favor—
And the world shall be at peace."*

《Zhuangzi》 says:
*"If the scheming mind dwells in the chest,
Then the pristine purity cannot be cultivated.
When pristine purity is not fully maintained,
Then the spirit’s emergence becomes unstable.
The spirit’s emergence unstable—
This is what the Dao does not carry."*

《Zhuangzi》 says:
*"When the body is whole and the essence restored,
One unifies with Heaven.
Heaven and Earth are the parents of all things—
In union, they form completion;
In dispersion, they return to origin.
If the body and essence remain undiminished,
This is called ‘able to transform.’
Refining essence ever more,
One returns to align with Heaven."*

《Zhuangzi》 says:
*"Extreme yin is solemn and quiet,
Extreme yang is radiant and fierce.
Solemn and quiet arises from Heaven,
Radiant and fierce emanates from Earth,
And when the two interact in harmony,
All things come to life."*

《Zhuangzi》 says:
*"If the will is not divided,
Then the spirit becomes concentrated."
And again:
*"If one’s Heavenly Guardian is intact,
And one’s spirit has no gaps,
What space is there for external things to enter?"*

《Zhuangzi》 says:
*"All under Heaven is but one *qi*."*

The Master of Upper Yang said:
*"The cultivation of self begins with virtue and conduct.
Virtue can move Heaven and Earth,
Conduct can influence spirits and gods—
Thus, with such a mind,
One may then draw upon the *qi* of the Primordial Heaven,
The *yīn* essence of True Unity,
And the supreme treasure of the Golden Elixir,
Only then may one perform this work of one moment, two phases."*

The *Jīnshí Gāo* states:
*"Swiftly nurture the elixir field, swiftly nurture the body,
Cherish to use the virtue of yin to benefit the people.
If this body does not attain transcendence in this life,
Then in what life shall it transcend?"*

Chen Xīyí said:
*"Retain the yang essence—
Then eternal life is certain."*

Li Xū'ān said:
*"Once the yang passes through the gate,*
*Each may attain eternal life.*
*When essence is full,*
*The gate closes by itself,*
*No longer leaving any orifice.
*How do we know the essence is full and transforms into *qi* without leakage?
*Chōngxū Zǐ said:*
*'When self-cultivation through stillness has refined the essence into *qi*,
*Then the sign of fire-stopping appears.'*
*This is the response of the essence-less spirit—*
*Then there is no orifice.
*Only this—no orifice, no leakage—is true."*

The *Qìao Cháo Gē* sings:
*"Three leadings yield but one lead—
When lead is perfected,
The golden fruit, the immortal sprout, still take no form.
Reignite the furnace,
Reestablish the cauldron,
And the moment you mount the tiger, ride the dragon,
The vision of this realm vanishes."*

The *Tiānxiān Zhènglǐ* states:
*"When breath is stilled, essence returns—
This is called the foundation of non-leakage.
If there is leakage,
Then it cannot serve as the basis for the embryo-spirit.
The *True Self* is*
*The original face,*
*Another name for the Primordial Spirit, the inherent nature.*
The *Tiānxiān Zhènglǐ* also says:
*"A hundred days to establish the foundation,*
*Refining essence into *qi*—*
*This is the general principle."*

「Sometimes it takes seventy or eighty days to attain sufficient *qi*, or fifty or sixty days—those who are diligent in their practice achieve it more easily, as do the young.»

*The Tiānxiān Zhènglǐ* states:
*"In the first phase of refining essence into *qi*, if essence is already depleted, one must gather and refine to supplement it. Only when essence returns and *qi* is sufficient does the true *qi* elixir begin to form. If one is already aged, they cannot be bound by the hundred-day limit to complete the work, hence the distinction between those who succeed within the set period and those who do not. Those within the period—like our teacher, who achieved it in fifty days—may take seventy or eighty days, as I did in two and a half months, though I still required a month of preliminary adjustment. Those outside the period may take two hundred or three hundred days—this cannot be fixed."*

*The Tiānxiān Zhènglǐ* also says:
*"A cultivator must first cultivate pure virtue in the mundane world, then have faith in a true master, carefully select worthy companions, and wholeheartedly refine themselves—only then can success be measured in days."*

In the *Xiānfó Hézōng Lúnyǔ*, Chōngxū Zǐ says:
*"In the early years of the Wanli era (1573–1620), during the year *RénYín* (1596), I first practiced the hundred-day method at home, refining essence into *qi*. In the first month, I adjusted my breath; in the second, I made steady progress. When the time came, my spirit knew intuitively—turning the celestial stem-and-branch markers—silently comprehending the World-Honored One’s enlightenment upon seeing the morning star, resonating with my profound insight. Since then, in a single night, I traversed three to five microcosmic orbits, then seven or eight, and finally over ten, until my practice became uninterrupted throughout the night. With the fire’s intensity sufficient, I attained the stillness of the fire’s cessation, and the method of cessation itself took about two months, completing the great elixir by the end of three months—truly, ‘a hundred days to establish the foundation!’*

*When the Returned-from-the-Dead Teacher activated his *dàgōng* (great work), he was only thirty years old, with clear spirit and abundant *qi*. In quiet nights, diligent in his practice, he required no more than fifty days for the fire to be sufficient, and five days to gather the great elixir. His eyes emitted golden light, his nose exhaled *qi*, wind stirred behind his ears, a crane’s cry echoed at the back of his head, his body trembled, and a fire-pearl surged in his *dāntián*, ascending and descending like a galloping steed—these six signs confirmed its natural passage through the passes."*

Master Chíyáng said:
*"To undertake the great work, one must strictly adhere to the hundred-day period in a secluded chamber. Detached from external concerns, the mind empty of thought, the body like withered wood, the heart like cold ashes—all entanglements cease, merging with the void. Using the swiftness of lightning, day and night without respite, within three or five days, the mind naturally settles and the *qi* harmonizes, bringing boundless joy."*

Táo Sùzhuó said:
*"The three luminaries all reflect inward; the spirit does not stray. When the spirit condenses and the *qi* harmonizes, essence is internally guarded, and *qi* arises from without. Naturally, essence is refined into *qi*, irrigating the three palaces. When *qi* fills and roots take hold, leakage below ceases, and the foundation is established."*

The Níhuán Zǔ said:
*"From clinging to form to transcending form, refining essence into *qi* and returning *qi* to its root. When the fundamental *qi* condenses into spirit, only then does one speak of effortless communion with the numinous."*

*The Màiwàng* states:
*"If true lead is indeed refined by the solar fire, the foundation becomes unshakable. *Qi* is supplemented, essence is replenished, and yin essence is gathered and subdued, transforming into true mercury. Gradually, the principles align, nourishing the flesh, and one’s self-refinement reaches purity. Once self-refinement is complete and the six senses are perfectly still, only then can the One be attained. The critical moment between *Dīng* and *Rén*—this is the fire’s intensity."*

Shào Zǐ said:
*"Heaven’s spirit manifests in the sun; humanity’s spirit manifests in the eyes. Great indeed! Humanity’s spirit manifests in the eyes—where the eyes gaze, the heart follows. Thus, the internal alchemical method involves gazing with the eyes at the nose, aligning the nose with the navel, and descending the heart-fire into the *qìhǎi* (sea of *qi*). This requires no more than a brief instant."*

Bái Yùchán said:
*"First, one must practice stillness, condense the spirit, restrain anger, and suppress desire—only then do water and fire harmonize. When water and fire harmonize, metal and wood intermingle. When metal and wood intermingle, true earth returns to its place. When true earth returns to its place, the true elixir naturally forms like millet grains, growing one grain daily, as spirit returns to *qi* and fills the heavens and earth."*

Zhāng Sānfēng’s *Jīndān Jiéyào* states:
*"First, select three to five precious cauldrons, each weighing sixteen to seventeen *liǎng* (two-thirds of an ounce), or ideally two *liǎng*. They must be of pure, lustrous quality, with floral patterns—no impurities allowed. Place them together in a secluded inner chamber, regardless of day or night. The two bodies sit facing each other, their forms manifesting. First, strike the bamboo to raise the tortoise, then pluck the zither to harmonize the sound—each performed three times—before merging in unity and igniting the killing intent without indulgence.

When the critical moment arrives and the moon is in the *Gēng* position, one may fan the fire. Once the lead is complete, it lasts no more than an instant, but even three or five degrees of ordinary lead can extend life by two or three hundred years. In action, there are subtle applications: often drink the Daoist wine, never pluck the falling blossoms. Idly strum the silent-stringed zither, slowly blow the unholed flute. Such practice is supremely profound and wondrous—yet if pursued with haste, it harms rather than benefits. The great Dao of the golden elixir lies entirely in spiritual union; the mysteries of the jade liquid have no other techniques. Hence it is said: gathering the elixir is easy, but self-refinement is most difficult. One must ensure the soul’s essence and spirit merge, the heart turns to ash, and the mind becomes still. When the hundred-day foundation is complete, its marvel surpasses the microcosmic orbit. The Dao of returning the elixir has no greater method; the technique of grafting is no different. Though boldness brings swift results, negligence leads to failure. This is indeed the pivot of refining the jade liquid, the essence of forging the golden sword with water and metal."*

「Now, the *Heavenly Sword*—this is the very essence of my body’s yin and yang, the primal bones of vitality, not something forged from gold, silver, copper, or iron. It is the sacred root of Heaven and Earth, the ancestral framework of yin and yang, inherent since my birth, borne upon my person.

At the onset of the Three Heavens and Five Phases, its divine edge is sharp and keen—capable of bending and straightening, yielding and hardening, striking forth without return, and vanishing or revealing itself beyond measure. Should yin and yang stray from their proper degrees, the edge’s vigor falter, or when surpassing the Five Nines and Six Nines, the root and bones wither and lose their sharpness—how then could it attain spiritual resonance? Without this forging of the Heavenly Sword, how could one ever master the art of refining the True?

The *Classic* says:
*"A sword three feet long—striking forth without return,*
*One pill of elixir—eternal life without end."*

And again:
*"A single breath awakens the Heavenly Sword’s two horns,*
*Yet the elixir’s return lies in its falling edge."*

When its radiance is honed to brilliance, then it may soar with spirit and ascend to sainthood. *"The art of wondrous application is most critical when entering the chamber—one must select three fellow Daoists of the same school to aid and uphold each other. They must rely upon a wealthy and influential family, both as inner support and outer protection.

Establish the elixir chamber, vast yet precise, its breadth and length exceeding a single *zhang*—within it, place the golden *xiàng* and the numinous spirit. Sever all carnal indulgence and desire; prepare the chamber’s implements and provisions to ensure the elixir’s needs are met. Then journey to the Divine Land of the Red Realm, seeking the elixir cauldron and divine furnace.

Whether four or nine, pair them to generate mutual harmony—ideally, the two *sevens* (i.e., 14 and 28), but most wondrously, the fifty-four and forty-eight (i.e., 54 and 48). Avoid the five flaws; purify the body as a whole. Let the desire and spirit be pure, and the flesh and bones harmonize to aid one another.

Choose the season of Yang Spring, select the auspicious hour of the Two Eights (i.e., 16th day of the lunar month), and return together to the quiet chamber. Practice the method of the union of sun and moon, focus the mind and still the breath, and activate the mechanism of the *Kun* and *Bi* (i.e., the interplay of Heaven and Earth). Drive the Dragon and Tiger to guard the central void, manifest the *tuóluò* (i.e., the sealed alchemical vessel) and extinguish all thought—let the heart be like spring warmth, the intent like autumn frost.

First, attune the Tiger’s string, awaiting the clear note to arise on its own. Next, blow the Dragon’s flute, setting the elixir cauldron in place. Attune the Dragon and blow the Tiger—each for four *li* and six *li* (i.e., 24 and 36 breaths)—as the *qi* and spirit merge, this is the method of *zhùjī* (i.e., "establishing the foundation"), the practice of self-refinement, and the extraction of lead to add mercury.

The Dragon’s four wings span while its shoulders curve, using two clasps to press against the liquid. The two *sevens* (i.e., 14 and 28) move in concert, their *qi* resonating in harmony. Then settle the floating and sinking, and divide the ebb and flow.

Such is the alchemy of creation, exhausting all heavenly mechanisms. Guard the spirit with morning clarity, never let drowsiness cloud the day or night—only then will the primal yang solidify, and the foundation become unshakable.

When the time is ripe, gather the great elixir; when the pairing is complete, refine the great *Dan* (i.e., elixir).»

The *Mirror of the Immortal* says:
*"The spirit has no fixed form, yet it takes form with the *qi*.
*The essence lacks a set shape, yet it takes shape with the mind.
If the heart is not steadfast, the *qi* of the whole body will boil like water in a cauldron or burn like fire in a furnace, unable to be stilled—then the *qi* will scatter, the spirit will waste away, and the essence will have no means to generate. If the essence does not generate, the innate nature will grow dim and confused; even if one seeks to establish the foundation, how could it be possible?"*

The *Scripture of the Daoist-Buddhist Synthesis* says:
*"If the lustful thoughts and deeds of sentient beings are not eliminated, whenever one thinks of lust, the same-sexed essence enters the female root of the body. When greed and love touch the emotions, and infatuation touches the senses, those who practice with resolve, wisdom, and restraint—should even a fleeting lustful thought arise, they must extinguish it with a resolve of restraint."*

The Buddha says:
*"Lustful thoughts unchecked, one cannot escape the dust of rebirth."*

The Mistress Wei of Nan Yue says:
*"If one harbors lustful desire while pursuing the Dao of the Highest Truth, the Pure Palace will lose its name, and one’s birth records will be seized by the Three Officials (i.e., the celestial bureaucracy) for punishment."*

Chen Xianwei says:
*"When encountering phenomena or circumstances, one must gather them within a single breath, so that no mechanism of arising or ceasing remains—this is the wondrous application that avoids rebirth and escape from life."*

The *Great Return Elixir Song* of the Lord Wu Mengzhen says:
*"I urge you: when refining the elixir, know the Tiger well—
Yang meets yin, and they naturally combine and transform.
Three hundred sixty breaths seem like frozen jade,
A virtuous woman becomes the mother of eternal life."*

Zhongli Zu says:
*"A true man, when encountering the genuine alchemical precepts, must hold fast with a resolute and fierce heart."*

Zhongli Zu says:
*"If one truly guards against danger for a hundred days,
The blood will transmute into a silver-like substance.
If one truly lacks no flaw for a hundred days,
The jade-like essence will flow, radiant and luminous.
When the *qi* is steamed and perfused without cold or heat,
It becomes the method of the Highest Dao for the loftiest adept."*

The *Scripture of the Daoist-Buddhist Synthesis* says:
*"At the start of the hundred-day period, only a faint and subtle primal yang *qi* returns. When the hundred-day practice is complete and its function sufficient, the foundation is established—then one may proceed with the seven-and-a-half-day heavenly mechanism, and the great elixir will come when summoned.

Having crossed the Magpie Bridge (i.e., attained spiritual union), one may practice the True Mechanism of the Five Dragons Upholding the Sacred, and then take the elixir."*

The *Scripture of the Daoist-Buddhist Synthesis* says:
*"The innate nature and primal spirit within the heart govern the breathing, forming the fire of the Microcosmic Orbit. Steaming and perfusing, they aid and supplement, filling the primal *qi* until it overflows—like a sixteen-year-old boy, this is called the foundation complete."*

The poem of the Returned Yang Sage says:
*"Piercing the inverted Heaven and Earth,
One grain of elixir is a Heavenly Immortal."*

Seeking need not be in deep mountains—
what is gained lies ever before your eyes.
Amidst the busy, steal leisure to refine external elixirs,
from the void, cultivate the primal to manifest the first heaven.

When trust arrives and the birthplace is known,
the initial practice must be passed on by mouth.

*The Scripture of the Daoist-Buddhist Synthesis* says:
*"The two lines on stealing leisure amid busyness—
this is the art of refining the cauldron.
The cauldron must first be refined to purity,
its mechanism set before the proper time for extraction."*

*The Scripture of the Daoist-Buddhist Synthesis*:
A disciple asked Chongxu Zi: *"Yesterday, I observed Master’s *Direct Treatise* where you spoke of refining essence into qi—how does one know when qi has truly been refined?"*
He replied: *"Refining essence into qi is but the name for the initial stage of practice.
Originally, essence transforms into qi when, at the moment of qi’s activation, one does not allow it to revert to essence but instead preserves the true qi whole—this is called returning primordial qi to primordial qi, and speaking of refining qi.
This primordial qi is the formless primordial essence, which, if not guided to transform into form, is called refining essence into qi.
When activated, let the fire of the Microcosmic Orbit steam and perfuse it.
If steamed and perfused correctly, the qi returns to its root, growing ever more vigorous.
Today, when activated, refine one portion of qi;
tomorrow, when activated, refine another portion—
until movement reaches stillness, and supplementation becomes unnecessary.
When ten portions are refined, the primordial qi overflows with vitality—
then qi is truly refined, with no essence remaining, no orifices left."*

*The Scripture of the Daoist-Buddhist Synthesis*:
A disciple asked Chongxu Zi: *"How does one attain essence fullness without lust, qi fullness without hunger, and spirit fullness without sleep? How does one know when fullness is achieved?"*
Chongxu Zi said: *"Steaming and perfusing is supplementation.
When this qi is pure and no essence remains to generate,
then one knows true fullness—this is the work of a hundred days.
Once essence is full, the orifices close naturally.
When the great elixir arrives, the root of lust withers,
becoming like a child.
Even if one desires, it cannot be obtained—
why then think of lust?
The Buddha spoke of perfecting the hidden organ of the Tathagata’s horse,
what the world calls returning to youth—
this is it.
Once the root of lust is severed,
one attains the minor fruit of longevity,
rising from the desire realm into the form realm.
When the heart enters meditation and refines the spirit,
lustful thoughts do not arise.
At the stage of transcending and passing through the barriers,
the earlier qi returns to the primordial sea as the solid *kan*—
gradually, the solid *kan* separates from the void,
and the void, receiving the solid, becomes entirely solid.
When solid, there is no hunger—
why then think of food?
Yet, when the ten-month embryo is complete,
one truly does not eat.
From the first month, food intake decreases;
by the third month, grains reject the body;
after the fourth month, fire-foods are abandoned—
this is true non-eating, hence *qi fullness without hunger*.
If one still eats at this stage,
they remain a mortal bound by birth and death,
lacking steadfastness—
this cannot be called qi fullness.*

*Spirit fullness* is pure yang without yin.
The ancients said: *"So long as yin is not fully exhausted, one cannot become immortal.*
If even a portion of yin remains,
there is a portion of drowsiness and sleep demons.
Within the twelve hours, the luminous light does not shine of its own accord—
how then can the spirit be full?"
For when the spirit dwells in meditation, the qi follows and also settles.
When the spirit fears meditation,
from the first day of the first month,
one can refrain from sleep,
remaining ever-awake day and night, never dim.
Within the twelve hours, not a moment passes without meditation.
Thus, the work of ten months achieves *spirit fullness without sleep*.
At this point, the heart knows neither birth nor death,
breathing neither enters nor exits—
the yang spirit has shed its mortal shell,
ascending from the form realm into the formless.
Without clinging to perception or knowledge,
it returns to non-action,
refining the spirit back to the void—
this is the nine-year face-to-wall practice after spirit fullness."*

《The True Principles of the Celestial Immortal》 states:

*"Establishing the Foundation* is to settle the spirit and stabilize the breath.
Before the Foundation is established, the original spirit wanders beyond the realm,
the original *qi* dissipates, the original essence decays,
and the Foundation collapses.
One must forge the Three Treasures in unity—
essence refills essence, *qi* refills *qi*, spirit refills spirit.
When they merge as one, the Foundation is complete;
if they fail to merge, the passage remains blocked and cannot be formed.
With the Foundation complete, the fruit of becoming a human immortal is attained.

This is done to transcend the Realm of Desire
and open the passage to the Form Realm.
This is the basis for it.
This is the foundation for the ten-month spirit meditation.
And this is why one can remain unperturbed for ninety months*—
because of this Foundation.
This is why one can endure ten months without food or drink,
without feeling cold or heat*—
because of this Foundation.
This is why the spirit does not wander outward
and attains Great Meditation*—
because of this Foundation.

When refining *qi*, the breath becomes still,
and through countless billions of trillions of *kalpas*, not a single breath is drawn.
When refining the spirit, the spirit returns to the void,
and through countless billions of trillions of *kalpas*,
there is no dimming, no sleep,
nor does it stray even once.
This is the Foundation of the yang spirit,
stemming from the undefiled original essence,
known as the Perfection of Exhaustion*—
the external elixir is thus complete."*

**Volume Six**
*"Knowing the Times to Harvest Medicinal Herbs"*

The Buddha said:
*"This is the true and rare wondrous truth."*

The *Huangting Jing* states:
*"Who will contend with you against the sun and moon?
Embrace the jade, cradle the pearl—
master this secret, and all things are accomplished.
Again it says:
'Granted the elixir of return and the primal spring,
the tortoise draws the breath to the root of life.
Within lies the True Person, wrapped in golden cloth,
bearing armor, holding talismans at the seven gates—
this is not the branch, but the very root.'*

The *Yinfu Jing* declares:
*"Its mechanism is stolen—
none beneath heaven can see it, none can know it."*

The *Ruyao Jing* proclaims:
*"Steal from heaven and earth,
plunder creation’s work,
concentrate the Five Phases,
harmonize the Eight Trigrams."*

Zhenyi Zi says:
*"The essence of True Unity is the mother of heaven and earth,
the root of yin and yang,
the origin of water and fire,
the lineage of sun and moon,
the source of the Three Powers,
the ancestor of the Five Phases—
all myriad beings are born from it,
and the ten thousand transformations unfold and retract through it.
Even before the signs appear—
whether in the lofty heavens, vast earth, cavernous palaces, or sacred peaks,
whether in celestial omens, spirit officials, or divine assemblies—
the winds and rains, the eclipses and clarities,
the seasons of spring, summer, autumn, and winter—
all arise from this leaden *qi* and manifest their transformations.
Those who cultivate the elixir,
who obtain this water of True Unity,
shall accomplish all things."*

The *Daode Jing* teaches:
*"Heaven, obtaining the One, is clear;
Earth, obtaining the One, is tranquil;
The Valley, obtaining the One, is full;
The spirit, obtaining the One, is numinous;
The sovereign, obtaining the One, makes the world sincere."*

The *Canton of the Three* states:
*"The One is used to conceal the idle—
none in the world know it."*

Jú Yuányù said:
*"This single point of True Seed—
it is the root of all life upon the Great Earth,
not merely the source from which we draw our vital *qi* for birth.
Even down to writhing, creeping things,
none escape its origin—
by this single point they are born and nurtured."*

Shàozi said:
*"At the Winter Solstice, when the hour of *zi* reaches its midpoint,
the Heavenly Heart does not shift.
When the first stirrings of Yang begin,
before all things take form—
the *xuán* wine’s flavor is yet faint,
the Great Sound’s voice has not yet ascended.
If you doubt these words,
then ask Fúxī himself.

What is called the *jī*?
The Heavenly Root’s principle is most subtle.
Now, at the year’s end,
when the first light of dawn is about to break—
this moment is easy to grasp in intent,
yet hard to articulate in speech.
If one can know this intent,
what is there one cannot know?

Suddenly, at midnight, a single thunderclap—
ten thousand households, a thousand gates hear it in sequence.
If you recognize that the Void contains an image,
I grant you a vision of Fúxī himself."*

Shàngyángzi said:
*"To enter the chamber and gather the medicine,
to seal the Three Treasures,
to focus the mind with single-minded devotion,
to humble oneself and await the command—
at this time, the Heavenly Pass lies in the hand,
the Earthly Pivot follows the heart.
The adept descends into the abyss unseen,
while the sword soars toward the Moon’s cavern."*

The waters and fires copulate along the Yellow Dao,
while the Dragon and Tiger wage battle at the Magpie Bridge,
seizing the seventy-two critical passes in an instant.
They plunder the three thousand six hundred measures of true *qi*,
reversing it into the womb—
without divine power, how could one succeed?

Lǚ Zǔ said:
*"Creation’s forces race in contention,
Dragon and Tiger in union—
advancing fire’s practice at the Bull’s peril."*

This is the affair of half a moment.

*The Cùixū Piān* states:
*"Essence’s birth has its appointed time;
when the time arrives, the spirit knows."*

*The Wùqí* says:
*"When lead meets *geng*, one must swiftly gather."*

The True Person of Zhengyang declares:
*"The interplay of having and non-having forms the alchemical foundation.
According to the *Dūzǐ*:
*'When the soul’s luminous awareness stirs—
this is non-being, the spirit.
When the misty, vital motion arises—
this is being, the *qi*.'"*

Zhāng Sānfēng’s *Dao-Emotion Song* declares:
*"Where lightning blazes, seek the true seed;
when the wind’s omen comes, find the ancestral lineage.
A million rays of crimson mist enfold the golden cauldron,
thousand-foot purple clouds shroud the Celestial Gate.
If you arrive here, do not be alarmed—
steadfastly guard the original spirit at the cave’s threshold.

Like a cat stalking a mouse, a hare facing an eagle,
urgently, tightly, fiercely press on.

All phenomena are unlike;
one crimson light is the true one.

This crimson light bears spring’s intent,
within which lies dust like light through a window.
Suspended at its core is a primordial elixir—
from afar, like grapes; up close, like gold.

When you reach this point, rely on utmost caution:
a single stray thought will forfeit the Heavenly True."*

*"The One-Branch Flower"* declares:

*"Dare I pluck the fresh blossoms from another’s wall,
hanging my mother’s iron-faced mask instead?
I teach him not to stir—
his coquettish, bewitching form,
his slender fingers—
cannot move my wandering mind or restless heart.

The moon’s fullness lies in the oral secret,
its child’s marvel in the heart’s transmission.
I raise my bodiless blade of sharp intent—
only fear the rapid current where ships founder,
only dread the Yellow Wife’s seduction,
only wait for the maiden’s lotus to bloom—
this matter is beyond words.

Five thousand days of unyielding resolve,
thirty hours of silent calculation.
I straighten the dragon’s head,
while he suspends the moon’s hollow void.
Displaying my divine power,
I plant the lotus in fierce flames.
With masterful skill,
I steer the boat against the current.

I envy not his lovely, delicate blossom,
only await his sweet dew to spring forth.
Assaulting the Celestial State,
shattering the Red County,
I seize the golden essence in delicate traction,
delivering it to the elixir field.
Averting peril, dispelling risk, banishing stray thoughts,
I bathe in nature’s purity,
face the wall for nine years,
before becoming a transcendent beyond the Penglai’s groves.

‘In the Hall of Lovely Spring,
I gathered herbs and inscribed talismans for five years.’"*

The **Zhongyang Ancestor** said:
*"The divine illuminates the **Kun Palace**—true fire arises spontaneously.
If the **Kun Palace** is not refined, then **metal** and **water** grow turbid.
If one does not focus with unwavering resolve,
then **water** and **fire** scatter wildly,
and the **Great Elixir** will never form—
how then could **Pretian qi** emerge?

When refining endures,
**water** perceives **fire**,
and spontaneously transforms into a single **qi**,
steaming and ascending.
The **River Chariot** turns of its own accord,
flowing ceaselessly without pause.
From this, **True Essence** generates **Yuan qi**,
and the embryo nurtures itself through breath.
When the pulse halts and **qi** stalls,
stillness begets **Great Stillness**.
Within **Great Stillness**, **Pretian qi** returns to its natural state,
arising from emptiness itself.
Thus, **child qi** responds to **mother qi**,
following nature’s course—
no haste may be forced,
just as at the dawn of **Hun Dun**,
**Xuan** and **Huang** intermingled.
When the time comes, **qi** transforms of itself,
and from utter stillness, motion spontaneously arises.
Within the depths of **Great Stillness**,
even as motion stirs—
this is **Pretian** creation.

Suddenly, a **thing** appears,
now clear, now obscured,
neither within nor without—
this is the **Great Elixir** sprouting,
its first omens.
From this point, guard the **Gan Palace**—
do not pluck recklessly.
If even a thread of thought arises,
**True Primordiality** is lost."*

The **Zhongyang Ancestor** said:
*"**True Lead** flickers like the moon’s form,
**Mercury’s qi** soars like the sun’s radiance.
When the two **qi** merge,
a single luminous point—
round and dazzling,
illuminating above and below.
**Inner Truth** and **Outer Response** align—
**Yang Elixir** comes from without.
Thus, **mother qi** subdues **child qi**,
and they unite naturally.
With my **qi**, I respond to the **Heaven-Earth’s most refined qi**,
as in the **Yangui Mirror**—
the principle of **water and fire** communicating through reflection—
this may be inferred by oneself.

When the sun and moon converge,
and **Pretian qi** arrives at its due time,
the **Nihuan Phoenix** is born,
the **Jiang Palace** glows with moonlight,
the **Dan Field** blazes with fire,
the **Sea’s depths** grow clear.
The body seems immersed in a sea of flame—
only fire is known,
no longer earth, no longer self—
all is as in drunken dreams.

This is the moment when **Dragon** and **Tiger** clash,
**Metal** and **Wood** intertwine,
**Water** and **Fire** collide—
their spectacle flashes forth,
swift as lightning and thunder—
seize it urgently.

The art of seizing it is this:
though a thousand-catapult force is unleashed,
only a single inch of mechanism suffices—
it seems plucked, yet is not plucked."*

The **Zhongyang Ancestor** said:
*"The spirit guards the **Xuan Palace**,
the mind welcomes the **Female Treasury**—
**Pretian qi** drifts in hazy obscurity,
dim and murky,
a single spark descending to the **Lower Yuan**.
My **True qi** draws it in response,
and **yin** enfolds **yang**,
while **yang** stirs **yin**.
The most refined essence gushes forth,
waves surge in the **Sea**,
rising from the **Tai Xuan Pass** into the **Nihuan**,
transforming into **Golden Elixir**—
fragrant, sweet, and crisp.
Swallowed into the abdomen,
ten thousand pores bloom with spring,
and radiance spreads across the body.
This is the union of **Heaven** and **Earth**—
once attained, it is attained forever.
Beware the perils."*

Lu Zu said:
*"At the right moment, the Golden Buddha appears,
Afterward, the Jade Maiden is hard to meet.
When flowers bloom, pluck them with care,
When the moon is full, admire it without delay."*

The *Bai Ju Zhang* states:
*"First observe the third night,
When the crescent moon begins to show the *Geng* mark.
To see the *Geng* flower bloom,
Look backward toward the crescent moon—
Thus, you gather the true lead,
Passing it mouth-to-mouth in true transmission."*

The *Cai Jin Ge* sings:
*"The medicine sprout is fresh,
Observe it with focus—
The lead’s radiance appears three days ahead."*

The *Dao Sui Ge* declares:
*"The crow’s essence,
The hare’s marrow—
Orifice meets orifice, mouth aligns with mouth."*

The *Huang He Fu* recites:
*"Steal the vital breath from the *Sha* center,
To drip into the yin-essence within my yang."*

*"Bright Moon Hall, jade petals fragrant.
Laughing under moonlit flowers."*

The *Qiao Yao Ge* instructs:
*"Guard the hour, fix the day, mark the moment,
Devote your heart with sincere intent.
When black lead passes,
Gather the pure essence—
A clash of forces seals eternal peace."*

The *Cai Zhen Ji Yao* warns:
*"The dragon dwells in the tiger’s den—
Worldly passions are the same.
At this moment, practice *xia si gong*.
Reverse actions to stir their movement—
In an instant, a drop passes eastward."*

Again it says:
*"If they grow ardent while I remain unaware,
Empty and transparent, I await their time.
Bow my head, close my eyes—the true lead arrives,
Swiftly it flies in, like fire’s rush."*

The *Gui Zhong Zhi Nan* teaches:
*"When the season arrives, the subtle principle reveals itself.
Lightly, silently, move and lift—
Gently steady the mind to still the breath,
Respond to Nature’s pivotal mechanism,
Then gold and water merge naturally,
Water and fire rise and fall in harmony.
Suddenly, a single point—
Large as a millet pearl—
Drops into the Yellow Court within.
This is the moment true lead meets mercury,
Forging one day’s elixir in a day."*

The *Fu Ming Pian* declares:
*"Last night, chaos scattered to the earth,
Ten thousand forms arise, yet none are known.
At this moment, my body blends with emptiness,
Equal to the void—
I know not spirit as qi,
Nor qi as spirit.
Such transformation requires no contrivance,
No artificial effort—
All unfolds naturally,
Beyond knowing how."*

*"In essence, the medicine’s birth—
Small, it aligns with the creative cycles of *Kan* and *Li*,
Great, it mirrors the movements of Heaven and Earth.
The elixir’s intent holds no excess."*

The *Xian Fo He Zong Lun Yu* states:
*"To gather the medicine, one must be free of desire—
Only then is it the pure essence of the ancients.
The slightest attachment, the faintest calculation,
And it becomes turbid.
Mindful of the Dao in every thought,
Pure and true it remains."*

A questioner asked Chong Hu Zi:
*"How does one concentrate the spirit into the qi orifice?"*
He replied:
*"The sun moves into the moonlit glow,
The golden crow flies into Chang’e’s chamber.
This is the meaning.
Rising and falling are the keys to gathering and refining,
Concentrating and returning to the root—restoring life’s command.
Spirit and qi merge as one,
With spirit dwelling within qi."*

*"When first refining gold and water,
Beware measuring time in years.
At the moment of merging the elixir,
Only a single breath’s effort is needed—
Prolonged labor ruins nature and harms the elixir.
Students, take heed."*

Shang Yang Zi cautioned:
*"The mechanism of drawing lightning
Cannot endure long—
Prolonged use weakens the spirit’s power."*

The *Mai Wang* explains:
*"Yang departs, yin arrives.
Yang must go first, yin must surge in response.
Only the minor yang first shoots a point of yin-fire light
Into the minor yin’s depths—
Then minor yin forms a single *yáo* of yang-lead qi,
Shuttling back and forth within the minor yang.
When true yang stirs,
The mercury is already set in motion to welcome it—
External forces internally ignite with spirit,
Internal forces externally touch with form.
Six reins in hand,
Like threads of dance in subtle play.
Between rising and falling, advancing and retreating,
All aligns with Heaven’s measure—
Five days mark a *hou*,
Six *hou* complete a month,
And the elixir’s methods of medicine and fire
Follow this rhythm naturally.
Thus the *Contract* says:
‘The warp and weft obey the sun’s command.’
The six *hou* correspond to metal and water,
Fixed and unchanging—this is the warp.
The morning and evening use of *Zhūn* and *Meng*,
Advancing and retreating with the times—this is the weft.
Yet *Zhūn* and *Meng* merely reverse the weft’s opposition
To embody the mechanism of advance and retreat.*

*"When gathering the medicine,
The drug lies outside, the fire within—
Fire draws the drug, yet the drug holds its own fire’s measure.
During nourishment,
The drug lies outside, returning within—
Obtaining the drug to kindle fire,
Yet fire contains the drug within.*

*"Gathering the medicine and kindling fire
Both depend on the *Kan*-center’s movement—
*Li* cannot act alone,
As the *Contract* warns:
‘Issue commands in harmony with the seasons,
Never miss the moment the *yáo* stirs.’
When the *yáo* moves, the qi mechanism is already active,
The mysterious orifice’s medicine sprouts—
Then fire must be applied in response,
Lest the opportunity be lost.*

The *Huan Yuan Pian* urges:
*'At the first stir of the phoenix’s rise,
When the thousand mountains’ moon is newly round—
Swiftly issue your decree,
And the Microcosmic Orbit may turn.'*

*"The four seasons’ qi are complete within a single day,
Yet I can respond to their shifts.
The five phases’ principles are whole within advance and retreat,
Yet I can grasp their order.
Then the elixir’s craft is complete."*

**"The period of forty-nine days—fifty-four hundred and eight in total—marks when the *Tian Zhen* qi descends, the water source pure as crystal, bearing qi yet no substance. At the first glimmer of the new moon on the third day, welcome its single portion of water as the true sign—seize it now, for it may be used. When the second portion of water arrives, pair it with two portions of fire, and thus the medicine and fire shall be balanced.

Why two portions of fire? For one *shí* is divided into three *fū*, yet only one *fū* is used in six *xiàng*. The fire of two *xiàng*—Dragon and Tiger in equilibrium—swallows and is swallowed, fire meeting water, containing and receiving, merging into the *Wu Ji* palace. Then water, fire, and earth—three substances—contain and receive the elixir’s formation, and its transformations unfold like divine artistry.

By *‘fēn’* is meant half a day as one portion. Three days yield *gēng*—then it is two portions. Fresh, tender medicine by the fifth day becomes three portions. By five portions, it is half the eighth day, already past the first quarter, the qi’s timing too distant. These two moments—when *Kan* water is most trustworthy, when metal and water first arise at two portions—are the keys.

The *Xian Tian* cauldron completes its cycle of fifty-four hundred and eight days along the Yellow Path, two days before *Wèi*, precisely at the juncture of new and dark moon—when heaven and earth’s yin and yang converge. In a month, this is the half-night of the thirtieth day; in a year, the *Dōng Zhì* moment; in a day, the transition between *Hài* and *Zǐ*; in the body, the instant of motion yet to act. Though named differently, all share this *zào* mechanism. Then the sun and moon unite in the sky, though their omens remain unseen. The Immortals observe the subtle shifts, awaiting the moon’s *gēng* to welcome the moment’s arrival—thus inner truth meets outer response."

**Shàng Yáng Zǐ** said:
*"The initial *gǔi* of *Fu*—this is true yang. When true yang first stirs, it is called *gǔi* giving birth. Heaven and earth return in seven days—*fù*, the Child. Great Yin emerges in three days as *gēng*—gold. The body examines the *jīng* in three days—*jīng*, lead. *Gǔi* moves, then lead is born; lead’s first emergence is called *Xian Tian* one qi, this qi named *Jīn Huá*. Though we speak of lead and *gǔi*, not water, we take their qi. Lead is born of *gǔi*; later yang is produced within lead. Harvest it in half a *shí*—this is the Great Transformation’s essence. Hence, one month has but one day, one day but one *shí*. This *shí* is most rare, for it is when heaven and earth unite in virtue, sun and moon in clarity—truly the source of all transformations."*

**Táo Sù Zhì** said:
*"Snow reflects the ice pond’s purity,
A new moon at the plum’s first bloom—
Only then does the medicine take root."*

**Lù Xī Xīng** said:
*"The mirror’s clarity is innate,
Yet dust obscures it, dimming its light.
Lead’s pearl alone emerges,
For *gǔi* accumulates, then hides it away.
When dust is cleared, the mirror shines anew;
When *gǔi* is spent, the lead’s flower reappears.
Seize the lead now—
Lest *gǔi* water rise again.
Gold is the same:
Its mirror, clouded, serves as metaphor."*

*The *Dào Dé Jīng* states:*
*"Its essence is most true,
Within it lies authenticity."*

The *Xian Tian* true-one qi—born in the void’s depths, this true essence—though faint and hard to perceive, yet bears verifiable signs by which it may be measured. The verifiable signs are:
*"Xian Tian qi, Hou Tian qi—
He who attains them feels as if drunk"*—
the medicine is already formed.
The omens are:
*"Heaven’s star, Earth’s *yíng*,
Exhaust *Wu Ji*, fix *Gēng Shēn*"*—
the medicine’s first emergence.
Without penetrating heaven and earth’s yin and yang,
Without deeply grasping the body’s transformations,
How could one measure these signs?

*The *Mài Lǐ* states:*
*"The Sage observes the Heavenly Path and follows its course,
Distinguishes medicines by the moon’s waxing and waning,
And harvests them knowing the time.
He knows the fire’s timing by day’s early or late,
And the fire’s *fū* aligns with the *xiàng*’s timing.

Seize the living Child’s moment,
Cast it into the receptive *Kūn* embrace—
Qi and essence resonate,
The *Xian Tian* true origin’s foundation is thus established—
This is the meaning of *‘The Great Sun moves within the moon’s light.’*
These two lines reveal the *Xian Tian* medicine’s origin.

The *Fù* hexagram’s center at the *Zǐ* position—
Here *Xian Tian* one qi first takes root,
All things’ numbers arise from this,
The beginning of Heaven’s will’s establishment.
In the Dao of the elixir, others’ *huó zǐ* timing
Is the *zhèn fū* after the new moon’s dawn.

When the moment arrives and the mechanism stirs,
At the dark’s end and the new’s beginning,
The *Xian Tian* true-one gold qi
Manifests as a single crescent on the *Huá’áng* brow—
Gold, though heavy and sinking,
*The *Kè* says: ‘Now sinking, now floating’—
Describing the *yáo*’s movement’s instant.
The method of harvest:
Stir it to rise and take it—
Then the just-watered source is pure.
Within the water, lead is born;
At the dry gold’s first emergence,
It is called the yellow sprout—
Fit for refining the Great Elixir.
Dry gold is the master of the five metals;
*Kan* water can bear gold upward,
Following the Heavenly River’s wheel,
Carrying it into our inner palace—
Thus it is named the Northern River Vehicle.
The scholar who knows gold and water’s alignment in the North as dry gold,
And their embodiment in the West as *Fu* gold,
Shall know the medicine’s source.

The method of elixir-making:
Await the moment of extreme stillness turning to motion,
Harmonize Dragon and Tiger,
Circulate true mercury to meet it—
Then fire steams, water boils,
And the gold follows the water’s rise, also called *‘wood bearing gold afloat.’*
Seizing the qi’s momentum,
Force it upward into the *ní wán*,
Then it disperses, melts, and descends as sweet dew,
Passing through the *Zhànglóu*,
Entering the *Jiānggōng*,
Descending into the *Huáng Tíng*,
Returning to the *Dòngfáng*—
Congealing into the elixir,
As the saying goes: *‘First liquid, then congealed.’*"*

Once the medicine is obtained, a single moment’s opportunity suffices—
Fire must then be halted, and the furnace sealed.
Prolonged exposure risks damaging the elixir.
*The Awakening to Reality* states:
*"Before refining the elixir, refine swiftly;
After refining, know when to cease.
If one clings to excess without restraint,
Disaster may strike in a single day."*

*The Pulse Gazing* says:
"Heaven and Earth generate life through the union of yin and yang;
The Dao of elixir-making generates medicine through the union of yin and yang—
Both share the same mechanism of transformation.
The marvel of human transformation appears at its appointed time.
If one attends to the subtle shifts of vision and hearing,
without losing the moment,
then transformation lies within one’s grasp.

First, one must know the time;
more importantly, one must await it.
Store the vessel within the body,
and when the moon aligns with *Shèn* (震) to generate,
follow the movement of the stalks to gather it.
Before the time arrives, close the *Fu* vessel and draw the curtain,
silently observing the void in anticipation—
never acting prematurely.
When the moment arrives, the subtle principle reveals itself,
and the great use manifests before one—
acting decisively to respond,
never lagging behind.

As for monthly nurturing and cultivation,
from the beginning of *Lún* (屯) to the completion of *Jì* (既),
it merely borrows the principle of return and opposition,
to demonstrate—
*one sequence forward, one sequence reversed*—
each with its own correspondence.

If the mind is unsettled and the refining incomplete,
if the furnace is stirred without purpose,
and the timing of day and hour is misjudged,
disaster follows swiftly.
If there is medicine and fire is applied,
the gold, pressed by the flames,
will surge toward the *Lí Gōng* (离宫),
transforming into water and countering the fire—
thus, fire faces no risk of scorching upward.
But if there is no medicine and fire is applied,
empty yang will rise in assault,
burning itself in the process.

True lead arises from the *Kǎn Gōng* (坎宫),
coarse and unresponsive—
to subdue the true mercury of the *Lí Gōng*,
one must use fierce, rapid fire,
only then will it ascend in flight.
Once lead and mercury unite,
one must then seal and bathe the furnace—
no further fierce fire may be applied;
this is the difference between *Tàipíng* (太平) and *Bīngjí* (兵革).

When the first stirrings of yang emerge,
welcome the moment and apply the fire,
stoking with the *tuóqiè* (橐钥)—
then the fire ignites, and the gold melts.
True breath serves as the furnace’s *tuóqiè*;
unbroken and continuous,
the original spirit merges with it—
fire thus obtains the wind.
True *qi* attains the spirit and transforms itself—
gold melts in the fire.

When refining lead with fire,
the Dragon breathes into the Tiger,
and lead absorbs the mercury’s *qi*.
The Tiger breathes into the Dragon—
each inhalation and exhalation,
the two *qi* intermingle,
like eating and drinking in union.
The gold’s vitality surges with movement—
seize this moment to gather it,
returning it to the earthen tripod,
where it mingles with my long-stored yin essence,
blending into the elixir.
*The Classic of Change* says:
*"The two *qi* respond and interact."*

The water of *Kǎn* is yang *qi*;
ride its stalk’s movement and summon it with intent.
The fire of *Lí* is yin essence;
stillness at its peak allows response,
and it is guided by intent.
The primordial medicine lies before the *xū* and after the *sháo*—
at the beginning and end of each month—
as the lead and mercury medicines.
This truth of Heaven’s mechanism
is known by few."

The Master of Upper Yang says:
*"In a year, twelve degrees of the full moon—
each month has a day when yang is born.
A month’s day and night span three thousand *kè* [刻, a unit of time, roughly 1/100 of a day],
and within each *kè*, one must seek the moment when *jǐ* [癸, the tenth Heavenly Stem, associated with water] is born.
In wild campaigns, one harvests lead;
in besieged defenses, one only nurtures.
Knowing ill and auspicious fates,
one points to the day of success.
'When asked about the *huózì* [活子, "living child," a term in alchemy for the optimal moment to gather mercury *qi*] time,
it is now at the year’s end,
tomorrow at the *wèilái* [未来, "future hour," the *xū* [晦, last day of the lunar month] of the next month.
Is there any wonder beneath Heaven
that can match this?'*

Master Qiu Changchun [邱长春, a historical alchemist] says:
*"The *huózì* time appears when the medicine sprout is fresh."*

*The Pulse Mirror* [《脉望》] says:
*"Alchemists, when gathering medicines at the furnace,
within a single *shíchén* [时辰, two-hour period],
collect the vital *qi* of thirty days—
the timing is measured by two and a half days, thirty *shí* [时, hours].
This is the art of exchanging time for days.
But gathering medicines must combine both dynamic and static practices:
static and besieged defenses [守城]—
if the mind is undisturbed, the Three Treasures [三宝, *sānbǎo*: jing [精, essence], qi [气, energy], shen [神, spirit]] are sealed off;
dynamic and wild campaigns [野战]—
the Tiger and Dragon clash, their movements inverted and misapplied.
Yet within defense and attack,
there are both ill and auspicious signs.
When *qi* is settled and the spirit concentrated, it is auspicious;
when desire surges and emotions prevail, it is ill.
Seeking lead according to the timing is auspicious;
acting recklessly outside the proper time is ill.
'Gathering medicines at the furnace,
one must first perfect oneself—
when body and mind are utterly still,
only then may one proceed.
Beware of overconfidence,
for it risks losing our family’s priceless treasure.
Its scope is vast,
not limited to refining oneself alone.
Then one knows that talismans and incantations are false,
medicinal materials are impure—
one cannot prevail against this.
The Tiger and Dragon are uncoordinated,
the fire’s degree is unclear—
one cannot prevail against this.
The Yellow Wife [黄婆, a term for a skilled alchemical assistant or the female principle in transformation] is unskilled,
the companion is discordant—
one cannot prevail against this.
Grace and authority are untrusted,
words are miscommunicated—
one cannot prevail against this.
The slightest carelessness brings regret,
and not only will one fail to obtain the other’s *mìngbǎo* [命宝, "treasure of life," the refined elixir],
but even our family’s own treasure will be lost.
'When refining oneself to perfection,
the body and mind remain unmoved,
the soul and spirit are controlled,
desires do not interfere,
and essence and *qi* are full—
await the moment when yang first stirs in the heavens.
When the true lead of *xiāntiān* [先天, "pre-Heaven"] is about to emerge,
do not move your own essence and *qi*;
instead, near the lower *shèn* [肾, kidney], in the nearest place,
use a single point of true mercury to welcome it.
The second stage seeks the medicine—
this is called the *qiánxíng duǎn* [前行短, "short forward movement"].
When the true lead has crossed the *Quèqiáo* [鹊桥, "Magpie Bridge," a metaphor for the union of yin and yang],
and lead and mercury are mingled,
then follow the true summons to raise the *lùlú* [辘轳, "well bucket," a metaphor for the alchemical process],
passing through the *shuāngguān* [双关, "double barrier"] and *jiājǐng* [夹脊, "pinched spine"],
up to the *níwán* [泥丸, "clay pill," the upper dantian],
flooding the Nine Palaces [九宫],
pouring into the double eyes [双目],
descending the *Jīnqiáo* [金桥, "Golden Bridge," a metaphor for the alchemical pathway],
lowering to the *zhònglóu* [重楼, "double-decker pavilion," a metaphor for the lower dantian],
entering the *Jiǎnggōng* [绛宫, "Crimson Palace," the heart] for smelting.
The fourth stage completes the elixir—
this is called the *hòuxíng cháng* [后行长, "long backward movement"]."*

Master Tao Suzhi [陶素耜] says:
*"Refining the return elixir [还丹, *huándān*] must rely on the *xiāntiān* water.
The post-Heaven gold and water [后天金水, *hòutiān jīnshuǐ*] serve as furnace and crucible,
but they must all be used only when they are clear.
The *Shī* [《诗》, *Shījīng*, *Classic of Poetry*] says:
*'Jīng [泾] with Wèi’s turbidity'*—
the Jīng water is clear, while the Wèi water is turbid.
Those refining the elixir must await the clarity of Jīng’s water,
relaxing and vigilant, undisturbed.
The critical moment of gathering at the furnace
is none more important than this.
Hence, the Sage throughout the year takes the month to straighten the gold,
within the month measures the day to listen to the tides,
within the day chooses the hour to respond to the *yáo* [爻, lines of the *Classic of Change*],
and within the hour determines the fire to act upon the talismans.
Ancient Sages and worthy predecessors
all guarded against dangers and risks,
until their completion."*"

The Master of Upper Yang says:
*"Having understood the gathering and taking,
one must now awaken to the birth of the body."*

One must consider the **qi** and climate—
within a month, there is but one day,
and within a day, only one moment.

A moment is divided into six **hóu** [候, stages],*
the first two **hóu** yield the medicine,
the last four **hóu** bring forth the elixir.
The elixir’s refinement lies in swiftly combining **yǐhóng** [已汞, cinnabar] with **qiān** [铅, lead].

At this juncture,
harmonize the **zhēnqì** [真息, true breath],
circulate it through the six voids,
from the **Tàixuān Guān** [太玄关, Great Primordial Pass] in reverse,
until it reaches the **Tiāngǔ Xué** [天谷穴, Heavenly Valley Hole],
and then swallow it into the **Huángjīn Shì** [黄金室, Yellow Gold Chamber].
This is the foundation of the **yuánqì** [元气, original qi]’s ignition—
the initial step.
Hence, the **Zhēnyī Zǐ** [真一子, Master of True Unity] says:
*"Establish the furnace and vessels,
stir the celestial mechanisms."*

At first, there is no form or substance,
just as in the **Hóngmáng** [鸿蒙, Primordial Chaos].

Once the fire is ignited and the talismans are activated,
the **yuánqì** [元气, original qi] should then be cultivated over a year.

The *True Transmission of the Golden Elixir* states:
*"The first two **hóu** are for external elixir’s operation,
the moment of obtaining the elixir—
its effect lies in the external, not within oneself.
The last four **hóu** are for internal elixir’s operation,
the moment of elixir formation—
its effect lies within oneself, not externally."*

**Qiú Zhàowèi** [仇兆鳖, Master Qiú] says:
*"The first two **hóu** involve stirring the fire to seek **qiān** [铅, lead].
The last four **hóu** involve refining the elixir by harmonizing **yǐhóng** [已汞, cinnabar].
Within the four **hóu**, there are further distinctions.
**Wú Sīlái** [吴思莱, Master Wú] says:
'Reverse the **Héchē** [河车, River Vehicle],
return to the **Tǔfǔ** [土釜, Earthen Cauldron]—
these two **hóu**’s methods involve sealing the Three Treasures,
concentrating the spirit and stabilizing the breath,
and guarding within the **Shénshì** [神室, Spirit Chamber].
These last two **hóu**’s operations are indeed exquisite.'*

The *Mirror of the Transcendent* states:
*"The twelve moments divided into six **hóu**:
the first two **hóu** involve stirring the fire,
the middle two **hóu** involve gathering the medicine,
and the last two **hóu** involve warming and nurturing."*

**Lǚ Zǔ** [吕祖, Patriarch Lǚ] says:
*"Know that **guǐ** [癸, the tenth Heavenly Stem] generates at dawn,
**guǐ** appears in the moment.
Thirty moments span two half-days.
Gathering lies only within one moment,
and the two **hóu** are seen.
The last four **hóu** have other concerns—
do not covet the time for medicine."*

The *Ode to the Yellow Crane* states:
*"The first two **hóu** and last four **hóu**,
half belong to **Kǎn** [坎, Water], half to **Lí** [离, Fire]."*

The *Song of the Great Dao* says:
*"One moment divided into six **hóu**,
only the first two **hóu** are for refining the Golden Elixir.
The remaining four **hóu** hold divine operations,
whose secrets are hard for a teacher to reveal.
The first two **hóu** yield the medicine—
the process is brief.
The last four **hóu** form the elixir—
the process is long."*

The *Scriptures of the Union of Daoist and Buddhist Schools* state:
*"To gather the Great Medicine in the **Hùndùn** [混沌, Primordial Chaos] of seven days,
this is the creation of substance from nothingness—
one must gather it before it manifests.
The gathering process takes seven days,
and only then is there a result.
Except for the first day, second day, and third day,
where the **qi** is weak and the elixir cannot be obtained,
between the fourth and seventh days,
there may be one day when the **Dāntián** [丹田, Elixir Field] fire blazes,
the two kidneys boil like soup,
the wind howls behind the ears,
and the **Jiù** [鹫, vulture] cries at the **Jīngshān** [京山, Capital Peak].
At this time,
golden light appears at the eyes’ base,
and a single grain of the Great Medicine arrives in the **Dāntián** [丹田, Elixir Field].

If the medicine does not respond to gathering and does not come,
it is as **Qiū Zǔ** [邱祖, Master Qiū] said:
*'Fire is insufficient, then the **Jīngqì** [金精, essence of gold] will not ascend.*
Or if the medicine comes but the strength is lacking to breach the pass,
it is because the **Shuǐyuán** [水源, water source] at its origin
was not yet known to refine—
when the moment for gathering arrives,
the **yīngqì** [炁, subtle energy] is weak and feeble,
unable to breach the pass and achieve the **Dàdào** [大道, Great Way],
all because the gathering was too early—
the **yīngqì** [炁, subtle energy] was still tender,
as in the **Chūjiǔ** [初九, first line of the ninth hexagram]—
*'Do not act.'*

Within **jìngdìng** [静定, stillness and stability],
the spirit-**qi** [神炁] is as one.
Thus,
stillness is also spirit-**qi** [神炁] as one,
movement is also spirit-**qi** [神炁] as one.
If movement scatters outward and follows delusions,
it becomes two.
If movement responds to the mechanisms,
it unifies as one.
For when the original spirit-**qi** [元神] scatters,
the **qi** [炁] scatters as well—
if there is no original spirit-**qi** [元神] to gather,
then the **jīngqì** [精炁, essence-energy] will be depleted.
Thus, the *Scripture of the Body’s Illumination* says:
*'When the mind is still and the spirit is whole, the **Shuǐyuán** [水源, water source] is clear;
when the mind moves and the spirit scatters, the **Shuǐyuán** [水源, water source] becomes turbid.'*

**Chén Zhìxū** [陈致虚, Master Chén] says:
*"When the heart moves, the spirit does not enter the **qi** [炁];
when the body moves, the **qi** [炁] does not return to the spirit."*

**Yú Yùwú** [俞玉吾, Master Yú] says:
*"The **Jīn** [金, gold] and **Huǒ** [火, fire] must be in the same furnace,
most wary of **Gēnchén** [根尘, root dust] touching,
for it scatters the spirit-**qi** [神炁]."*

The *Lotus Sutra* says:
*"**Xìng** [性, nature] is stillness.
**Qì** [气, breath] is movement.
Movement and stillness as one—
how few can the accomplished place their hearts here?"*

**Guǎngchéng Zǐ** [广成子, Master Guangcheng] says:
*"Stillness is stillness of the spirit and intent;
movement is movement of the spirit’s mechanisms."*

The ancients said:
*"When the time arrives, the spirit knows—
the spirit-**qi** [神炁] moves together."*

**Yīngchán Zǐ** [莹蟾子, Master Yīngchán]’s poem:
*"Refining lead and boiling cinnabar has no fixed time,
the student must push within **jìngdìng** [静定, stillness and stability].
Guest dust desires to taint the heart—
no attachment.
When **Tiāngǔ** [天癸, Heavenly Guǐ] arises,
the spirit knows itself."*

The *Treasure Box of the Golden Elixir* states:
*"The method of gathering arises from the true heart.
The heart is the pivot and hinge of all things—
one must forget it before seeking it.
Forgetting is the deluded mind.
Seeking and finding is the true heart.
Yet within forgetting, a true intent must arise—
this is the true heart.
In the midst of confusion,
the true heart begins to appear.
Once the true heart appears,
from it arises a true intent—
with reverse light and inner illumination,
then all orifices are fully opened,
and the original essence emits its brilliance.

The key lies in generating substance from nothingness,
and nothingness from substance.
At this stage,
both the true heart and true intent are abandoned and forgotten.
With nothingness, I await—
when its breath is soft and continuous,
the **Hòutiān** [后天, post-heavenly] **qi** has already stabilized,
and the **Hòutiān** [后天, post-heavenly] **qi** hidden,
the **Xiāntiān** [先天, pre-heavenly] **qi** appears.

When the **Xiāntiān** [先天, pre-heavenly] **qi** arrives,
the hundred vessels of the body
all bloom like spring.
Spring’s vitality melts and gradually lengthens—
at this time, the **Xiāntiān** [先天, pre-heavenly] body begins to stand,
and the **Hòutiān** [后天, post-heavenly] **qi** recedes and hides.

The method of gathering relies on the true heart directing the true intent.
The intent is—
with the eyes lowered in observation,
the heart releases and sends it into the **Yánggōng** [阳宫, Yang Palace],
slowly gathering and then letting go again—
then the **Yáng** [阳, Yang] rises.

For the **Zhēnqiān** [真铅, true lead] and **Zhēnyǐhóng** [真汞, true cinnabar] of the Great Elixir,
gathering must be sought in the **Wǎngxiàng** [罔象, formless realm]."*

「When the **Tiānguǐ** [天癸, celestial water] first emerges, act swiftly and with utmost reverence in gathering.

The ancient hymn says:
*"The dark **Kǎn** [坎, Abyss] deceives with unity,
The bright **Lí** [离, Clinging] manifests five colors.
To know the three places,
Clutch the spirit of the **Mù** [木, Wood] branch.
Refine the elixir first by mastering the secret formulas,
Then consult the ancient scriptures.
When the **Qióngdān** [琼丹, jade elixir] sovereign is complete,
The celestial chariot ascends beneath five cloud canopies."*

The ancient hymn says:
*"At sixteen years, the maiden blooms,
At twenty-eight, the lead essence is refined.
When **Yáng** [阳, Yang] arises and fire ignites,
When **Yīn** [阴, Yin] is exhausted, cease.
Stars circle complete—
The elixir’s potency is now awakened."*

**Xiāo Zǐxū** [萧紫虚] says:
*"External heresies and demons suddenly wield their might,
With seven-starred treasure blades probing forward.
At the ghostly cavern’s battleground,
A pearl of clarity is seized and returned.
